Salah — Prayer

Sajdah al-Sahw After Deliberate Salam
Permissibility of sajdah al-sahw after intentional salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing sajdah al-sahw after an intentional salam and identify the condition that must be met.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw is valid even after deliberate salam, provided you haven't turned from the qibla.

Many worshippers assume that once the salam is pronounced, the prayer is irrevocably ended. However, this concise Hanafi ruling clarifies that the prayer state persists until one physically turns away from the qibla. This lesson unpacks the precise condition that allows sajdah al-sahw after intentional salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the ruling concerns a worshipper who intentionally says salam to end the prayer but later remembers an omission requiring sajdah al-sahw.
The salam here is deliberate, not forgetful.
2
Identify the ruling
The text states that sajdah al-sahw may still be performed even after such a deliberate salam.
This is the Hanafi position; other schools differ.
3
Identify the condition
The worshipper must not have turned his face away from the qibla (direction of prayer).
Turning away severs the prayer state completely.
4
Understand the rationale
The prayer is not considered ended by salam alone; turning from the qibla is the act that definitively ends the prayer.
Thus, the door for corrective prostration remains open until that turning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۴۷) سجدہ سہو کر سکتا ہے اگر چہ جان کر نماز ختم کرنے کے لئے سلام پھیرا ہو جب تک کہ قبلہ سے نہ پھرے۔
(747) He can perform sajdah al-sahw even if he deliberately performed salam to end the prayer, as long as he does not turn away from the qibla.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This is a concise ruling stating that sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) can be performed even after the worshipper has intentionally made salam to terminate the prayer, provided he has not yet turned his face away from the qibla (direction of prayer). This indicates that the state of prayer is not completely severed by the salam alone; turning away from the qibla is what definitively ends the prayer. Therefore, if one remembers a forgotten obligation after salam but before turning away, he may still perform sajdah al-sahw to rectify the prayer.

Key Terms
قبلہ (qibla): The direction of the Kaaba, which must be faced during prayer; turning away from it can invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it permissible to perform sajdah al-sahw after intentionally saying salam?
A) Only if the salam was said forgetfully
B) At any time, even after leaving the mosque
C) As long as one has not turned away from the qibla
D) Sajdah al-sahw is never allowed after intentional salam

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw remains valid after deliberate salam provided the worshipper has not turned from the qibla.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Joining an Imam Before Sujud al-Sahw: Validity and Proof
Ruling on following an imam after first salam for sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on the validity of following an imam who has said the first salam for sujud al-sahw, and explain the dalil from hadith.

Core Idea
The first salam for sujud al-sahw does not end the prayer until sujud is performed.

In Hanafi prayer, an imam who forgets something performs sujud al-sahw. He may say a first salam before the prostration. If someone joins him at that moment, is the follower's prayer valid? This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof from the hadith that the salam is the 'tahlil' (termination) of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Following an imam after he has said the first salam for sujud al-sahw. State the hukm: it is sahih (valid) if the imam performs sujud al-sahw, otherwise it is not valid.
The ruling depends on a subsequent action by the imam.
2
Understand the principle behind the ruling
The first salam for sujud al-sahw is not a termination of the prayer; it is a pause to perform the sujud. The prayer continues until the sujud is done. If sujud is omitted, the first salam becomes the final salam.
This is based on the Hanafi position that sujud al-sahw is part of the prayer.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is the takbir, and its analysis (tahlil) is the salam.' This proves that the salam ends the prayer.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'tahlil' (analysis) means making the prayer permissible (halal) to exit. Thus, a salam that truly ends the prayer is the one after which no part of the prayer remains. The first salam before sujud cannot be that final salam because sujud is still due.
Thus the first salam is conditional; it only ends the prayer if sujud is not performed.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Imagine an imam says the first salam (turning right) after forgetting a wajib. A person joins the congregation at that moment. If the imam then performs sujud al-sahw, the follower's prayer is valid. If the imam forgets to perform the sujud and walks away, the follower must restart his prayer.
The follower must ensure the imam actually performs the sujud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاقتدی به غیره صح ان سجد للسهو والا فلا يصح

ترجمه : (۷۴۶) اور اگر امام سہو والے نے سلام پھیرا پھر اس کے ساتھ دوسرے نے اقتدا کی تو اگر امام سجدہ سہو کرے تو اقتدا صحیح ہے، اور اگر سجدہ نہ کرے تو صحیح نہیں۔
تشریح : یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ سجدہ سہو سے پہلے جو دائیں جانب سلام پھیرتے ہیں، اگر اس کے بعد سجدہ کرلیا تو یہ سلام انقطاع کا نہیں ہوگا بلکہ بعد والاسلام انقطاع کا ہوگا ، اور اگر سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تو یہ سلام انقطاع کا ہوگا اور اسی پر نماز ختم ہو جائے گی ۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام پر سجدہ سہو تھا اس لئے اس نے سجدہ سہو کے لئے سلام پھیرا، اور اس وقت کسی نے اس کی اقتداء کی۔ پس اگر اس کے بعد امام نے سجدہ سہو کیا تو اس کی اقتداء درست ہوگی ، اور سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تو اس کی اقتداء درست نہیں ہوگی۔ وجه : (۱) کیونکہ اس سلام کے بعد سجدہ نہیں کیا تو گویا کہ نماز ختم ہو گئی تب آدمی نے اس کی اقتداء کی ہے اس لئے اس کی اقتداء درست نہیں ہوئی ، اور اگر سجدہ سہو کیا تو یہ سلام درمیان میں ہو گیا اور گویا کہ ابھی نماز باقی ہے اس لئے آنے والے کی اقتداء درست ہے۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ سلام نماز ختم کر دیتا ہے ۔ عن ابی سعید قال قال رسول الله مفتاح الصلوة الطهور وتـحـريـمـهـا الـتـكـبـيـر وتحليلها التسليم ولاصلوة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة في فريضة او غيرها. (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی تحریم الصلوۃ و تحلیلها ص ۵۵ نمبر ۲۳۸ رابو داؤد شریف، باب الامام يحدث بعد ما يرفع رأسه من آخر رکعته ص ۹۸ نمبر ۶۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سلام نماز کو حلال کر دیتا ہے، یعنی نماز کو ختم کر دیتا ہے۔
If another person follows him (the imam), it is valid if he performs sujud al-sahw, otherwise it is not valid.

Translation (746): And if an imam who requires sujud al-sahw says the salam, and then another person follows him, then if the imam performs sujud al-sahw, the following is correct, and if he does not perform sujud, it is not correct.

Explanation: This issue is based on the principle that when one says the salam to the right before sujud al-sahw, if he then performs sujud, this salam is not the one that terminates prayer; rather the later salam is the terminating one. And if he does not perform sujud al-sahw, this salam is the terminating one and the prayer ends with it. The scenario: The imam required sujud al-sahw, so he said the salam for sujud al-sahw, and at that time someone followed him. So if the imam then performs sujud al-sahw, his following is correct, and if he does not perform sujud, his following is not correct. Reason (1): Because after this salam he did not perform sujud, so it is as if the prayer ended, then the person followed him, so his following is not correct. And if he performed sujud al-sahw, this salam occurred in the middle, and it is as if the prayer is still ongoing, so the follower's following is correct. (2) The hadith states that salam terminates the prayer: from Abu Sa'id that the Messenger of Allah said: "The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is the takbir, and its analysis is the salam, and there is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in an obligatory or supererogatory prayer." (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi tahrim al-salat wa tahliliha, p. 55, no. 238; Abu Dawud, Bab al-imam yuhdith ba'da ma yarfa' ra'sahu min akhir rak'atihi, p. 98, no. 618) This hadith states that salam makes prayer halal, i.e., it ends the prayer.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the validity of joining an imam who has already said the first salam for sujud al-sahw. The ruling distinguishes between two outcomes: if the imam performs the sujud al-sahw after the first salam, then that first salam is not considered the final termination of the prayer; the prayer is still ongoing, so the follower's act of joining is valid. If the imam does not perform sujud al-sahw, then the first salam is the terminating salam, and the follower joined after the prayer ended, which is invalid. The author supports this with a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that identifies the salam as the act that ends the prayer (tahlil). The logic is that the salam before sujud al-sahw is not meant to end the prayer but to set the stage for the prostration; thus the prayer remains connected until the sujud is performed. This ruling follows the principle that sujud al-sahw is part of the prayer, not after it. The commentary uses the terms 'shaf' (pair) and 'sujud al-sahw' which are key to understanding the discussion.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, performed before or after the concluding salam depending on the situation.
شفع (shaf'): A pair; in prayer, a set of two rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person follows an imam after the imam has said the first salam (for sujud al-sahw), when is the follower's prayer valid?
A) Always, because the first salam is not the final salam.
B) Only if the imam performs sujud al-sahw after that salam.
C) Only if the follower has not yet performed any rak'ahs.
D) Never, because the first salam always ends the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The first salam for sujud al-sahw does not necessarily end the prayer; its effect depends on whether the sujud is performed.

Sujud al-Sahw After Deliberate Salam for Termination
Ruling with proofs: sujud al-sahw permissible after deliberate terminating salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which sujud al-sahw remains valid after a deliberate terminating salam and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on the hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Deliberate intent to end prayer does not block sujud al-sahw until you turn from the qibla or speak.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: what if a person who owes sujud al-sahw deliberately says the salam with the intention to terminate the prayer? The Hanafi school holds that the obligation of sujud overrides that intention, allowing the sujud to be performed later. However, this window remains open only as long as the person has not turned away from the qibla or spoken extraneous words. The proof is drawn from the Prophetic practice and the statements of the salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and condition
The ruling is that sujud al-sahw is valid (sahih) after a deliberate terminating salam, provided the person has not turned from the qibla or spoken.
The condition is explicitly stated: 'ما لم يتحوّل عن القبلة او يتكلّم'.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The obligation (wujub) of sujud al-sahw overrides the worshipper's intention to terminate the prayer. The salam is retroactively considered the preparatory salam before sujud, not the final termination.
The text states: 'نيت بيكار جائے گي' (his intention is nullified).
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (SAW) prayed five rak'ahs of Zuhr, then said the terminating salam due to forgetfulness. When informed, he performed sujud al-sahw after the salam. This shows that sujud can be performed after a deliberate salam.
Hadith from Bukhari and Muslim is cited.
4
Apply the athar of al-Hasan al-Basri
The tabi'i al-Hasan ruled that if one forgets the sujud al-sahw and remembers before leaving the prayer place (i.e., before turning away), he can perform them.
This supports the condition that turning away breaks the validity.
5
Contrast with nullifying actions
If the person turns from the qibla or speaks deliberately, the prayer is considered ended and sujud al-sahw cannot be performed.
Turning or speaking are mubtilat (invalidators) of the prayer state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسجد للسهو وان سلّم عامدا للقطع ما لم يتحوّل عن القبلة او يتكلّم

ترجمه : (۷۴۷) سجدہ سہو کر سکتا ہے اگر چہ جان کر نماز ختم کرنے کے لئے سلام پھیرا ہو جب تک کہ قبلہ سے نہ پھرے۔
تشریح : سجدہ سہو تھا پھر بھی جان کر نماز ختم کرنے کے لئے سلام پھیر دیا، پھر بھی جب تک قبلہ سے سیدہ نہیں پھرا ہے سجدہ سہو کرنا چاہے تو کرسکتا ہے۔
وجه : (۱) سجدہ سہو سے پہلے ایک سلام تو کرنا ہی تھا، یہ اور بات ہے کہ سجدہ سہو کرنے کی نیت سے وہ سلام کرنا تھا، اور اس نے نماز قطع کرنے کی نیت سے سلام کیا، لیکن اس پر سجدہ واجب ہے اسلئے نیت بیکار جائے گی اور یہ سلام نماز ختم کرنے کا نہیں سمجھا جائے گا بلکہ سجدہ سہو سے پہلے جو سلام کرتے ہیں وہ سلام سمجھا جائے گا ، اسلئے کہ اسکی نیت مشروع طریقے کے خلاف ہے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے پانچ رکعت پڑھ کر بھول کر نماز ختم کرنے کا سلام پھیرا، پھر سجدہ کیا ۔ حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن عبد الله قال ان صلى رسول الله الظهر خمسافقيل له ازيد في الصلوة؟ قال وما ذاك ؟قال صلیت خمسا فسجد سجدتين بعد ما سلم (بخاری شریف، باب اذا اصلی خمسا ص ۱۹۶ نمبر ۱۲۲۶ر مسلم شریف ، باب من صلی خمسا ونحوه ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۱۲۸۳/۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں پانچ رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد انقطاع کا سلام کیا اور یاد آنے پر پھر سجدہ سہو کیا۔ (۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے .عن الحسن فی رجل نسي سجدتي السهو ، قال اذا لم يذكر هما حتى ا انصرف و لم يسجدهما ، فقد مضت صلوته فان ذكر هما و هو قاعد لم يقم ، و يسجدهما - (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب نسیان سجدتي السهو ، ج ثانی، ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۳۵۵۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ سجدہ سہو کرنا بھول گیا تو رخ پھیرانے سے پہلے یاد آیا تو سجدہ کر سکتا ہے۔
And he performs sujud al-sahw even if he deliberately said the salam to terminate (the prayer) as long as he has not turned away from the qibla or spoken.

Translation (747): He can perform sujud al-sahw even if he knowingly said the salam to end the prayer, as long as he has not turned from the qibla.

Explanation: He required sujud al-sahw yet he intentionally said the salam to end the prayer. Nevertheless, as long as he has not turned from the qibla, he may perform sujud al-sahw if he wishes.
Reason (1): He had to say one salam before sujud al-sahw anyway; it is another matter that he was supposed to say it with the intention of sujud al-sahw, but he said it with the intention to cut the prayer. However, since sujud is obligatory on him, his intention is nullified, and this salam will not be considered the termination of the prayer but rather the salam said before sujud al-sahw, because his intention opposed the prescribed way. (2) There is a hadith that the Prophet (SAW) prayed five rak'ahs of Zuhr and then deliberately said the terminating salam due to forgetfulness, then performed sujud. The hadith: from Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah prayed Zuhr five rak'ahs, and it was said to him: 'Has the prayer been increased?' and he said: 'What is that?' They said: 'You prayed five.' So he performed two prostrations after the salam. (Bukhari, Bab idha salla khamsan, p. 196, no. 1226; Muslim, Bab man salla khamsan wa nahwihi, p. 212, no. 1283/572) This hadith indicates that he said the terminating salam after five rak'ahs, then upon remembering, he performed sujud al-sahw. (3) A saying of the tabi'i: from al-Hasan concerning a man who forgot the two prostrations of forgetfulness; he said: 'If he does not remember them until he has departed and has not performed them, his prayer is complete. But if he remembers them while sitting and has not risen, he performs them.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab nisyan sajdatay al-sahw, vol. 2, p. 211, no. 3552) This effect states that if he forgot to perform sujud al-sahw, and remembers before turning his face away, he can perform them.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents another Hanafi ruling: even if a person deliberately says the salam with the intention to end the prayer, if sujud al-sahw was obligatory upon him, he can still perform it provided he has not turned away from the qibla or spoken. The reasoning is that the requirement to perform sujud al-sahw overrides his contrary intention. The salam he said is retroactively considered the preparatory salam before sujud, not the final termination. The author supports this with the hadith of the Prophet (SAW) praying five rak'ahs and then, after being informed, performing sujud al-sahw after the salam. Additionally, a statement from al-Hasan al-Basri is cited: if one forgets the sujud al-sahw and remembers before leaving the prayer place, he may perform them. This underscores the principle that sujud al-sahw remains valid until one physically breaks the prayer connection by turning away or speaking.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations done to compensate for forgetfulness, performed after the salam in this case.
قطع (qat'): Termination; here, deliberately ending the prayer by salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition can a person still perform sujud al-sahw even if they deliberately said the salam to end the prayer?
A) Only if they have not yet sat down.
B) Only if they have not turned from the qibla or spoken.
C) Only if they performed it immediately.
D) Sujud al-sahw is never valid after a deliberate salam.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw can be performed even after a deliberate terminating salam, provided the worshipper has not turned from the qibla or spoken, because the obligation of sujud overrides the contrary intention.

Completing Prayer After Mistaken Salam
Ruling on a person who mistakenly thinks they completed the prayer and says salam, then realizes they prayed only two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on mistaken salam and correctly complete the prayer with sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
A premature salam does not invalidate prayer; you build upon it and perform sujud al-sahw.

Imagine you are praying Zuhr, and after two rak'ahs you mistakenly think you have finished and say the salam. Then you realize your error while still in the sitting position. What do you do? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling based on the Prophet's own action in the hadith of Dhul-Yadain. This lesson will guide you through the steps to recover the prayer correctly, ensuring it remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mistake
Determine that the salam was said under a mistaken assumption (wahm) that the prayer was complete. The prayer in progress must be a four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah prayer, and you have only completed two rak'ahs.
The ruling applies when the mistake is realized while still in the sitting position (before turning away entirely).
2
Calculate Missing Rak'ahs
The number of rak'ahs already performed is known (e.g., two). Subtract from the total required (e.g., four for Zuhr) to find how many are missing (two rak'ahs).
3
Build Upon the Prayer
Stand up immediately and complete the missing rak'ahs as normal, without repeating the opening takbir or anything already done.
The term 'bana' (يَبْنِي) means you continue from where you stopped; the salam was not a valid termination.
4
Perform Sujud al-Sahw
After completing the final rak'ah and saying salam, perform the two prostrations of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw) because the premature salam is considered an interruption.
Sujud al-sahw is wajib here. The Prophet (SAW) performed it in the hadith.
5
Understand the Dalil
The ruling is based on the authentic hadith of Dhul-Yadain, where the Prophet (SAW) ended after two rak'ahs, was reminded, completed the prayer, and performed sujud al-sahw.
The hadith shows that the salam does not invalidate; it is a strong proof for the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو توهّم مصل رباعية او ثلاثية انه اتمها فسلّم ثم علم انه لم يتمها الا بركعة او ركعتين فانه يبني على صلوته و يتمها و يسجد للسهو

ترجمه : (۷۴۸) اور اگر تین رکعت یا چار رکعت پڑھنے والے نے پوری نماز ہو جانے کے وہم سے سلام پھیر دیا پھر معلوم ہوا کہ دو رکعت ہوئی ہے تو باقی پوری کر کے سجدہ سہو کر لے۔
تشریح : مثلا ظہر کی نماز چار رکعت پڑھنی تھی ، اور وہم ہو گیا کہ چار رکعت پوری ہوگئی اس لئے سلام پھیر دیا، ابھی قعدہ ہی میں تھا کہ معلوم ہوا کہ دور رکعت ہی پڑھی ہے ۔ تو دوسری دو رکعت پڑھے اور سجدہ سہو کر لے نماز ہو جائے گی۔ سجدہ سہو اس لئے کرے کہ درمیان میں انقطاع کا سلام کیا ہے۔
وجه : عن ابي هريرة ان النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم انصرف من اثنتين فقال له ذو اليدين : اقصرت الصلاة ام نسیت یا رسول الله ؟ فقال النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم اصدق ذو اليدين ؟ فقال الناس نعم فقام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فصلى اثنتين اخريين ثم سلم ثم كبر فسجد مثل سجوده او اطول ثم كبر فرفع ثم سجد مثل سجوده او اطول . (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرجل يسلم في الركعتين من الظهر والعصر ص ۱۰۷، نمبر ۳۹۹ را بود او د شریف، باب السهو فی السجدتین ، ص ۱۵۴
And if a person praying a four-rak'ah or three-rak'ah prayer mistakenly thinks that he has completed it and says the salam, then realizes that he has only completed one or two rak'ahs, he should build upon his prayer, complete it, and perform sujud al-sahw.

Translation (748): And if a person praying three or four rak'ahs mistakenly thinks the prayer is complete and says the salam, then realizes that he has only prayed two rak'ahs, he should complete the remainder and perform sujud al-sahw.

Explanation: For example, the Zuhr prayer is to be four rak'ahs, and he mistakenly thinks they are complete, so he says the salam. While still in the sitting position, he realizes that he only prayed two rak'ahs. So he should pray the remaining two rak'ahs and perform sujud al-sahw. The prayer will be valid. He performs sujud al-sahw because he said a terminating salam in the middle.
Reason: The hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Prophet (SAW) ended after two rak'ahs, and Dhul-Yadain asked: 'Has the prayer been shortened or did you forget, O Messenger of Allah?' The Prophet said: 'Is Dhul-Yadain truthful?' The people said yes. Then the Messenger of Allah stood and prayed two more rak'ahs, then said the salam, then said takbir and prostrated like his usual prostration or longer, then said takbir and raised, then prostrated like his usual prostration or longer. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-rajul yusallim fi al-rak'atayn min al-zuhr wa al-asr, p. 107, no. 399; Abu Dawud, Bab al-sahw fi al-sajdatayn, p. 154)
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage gives the Hanafi ruling for a person who mistakenly thinks they have completed their prayer (e.g., after two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer) and says the salam. They must realize their mistake (while still in the sitting position, before turning away), stand up and complete the missed rak'ahs, then perform sujud al-sahw. The sujud al-sahw is required because the salam was said in the middle of the prayer, which is an interruption. The proof is the well-known hadith of Dhul-Yadain, where the Prophet (SAW) did exactly this after being alerted by a companion. This incident shows that the prayer is not invalidated by the premature salam; rather, one builds upon what has been done and completes the prayer, then performs sujud al-sahw.

Key Terms
وہم (wahm): A mistaken assumption or doubt; here, thinking the prayer is complete when it is not.
بنی (bana): He builds upon; meaning to continue the prayer from where it was interrupted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Repeat the entire prayer from the beginning.
B) Perform two more rak'ahs and then sujud al-sahw.
C) Perform sujud al-sahw without completing the rak'ahs.
D) The prayer is invalid, so no action is needed.

Key Takeaway
A mistaken salam in prayer does not invalidate it; you build upon it by completing the missing units and then perform sujud al-sahw.

Following an Imam Who Forgets Sajdah al-Sahw
Ruling statement on following an imam who forgets sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following an imam who forgets sajdah al-sahw and identify the condition for the follower's prayer to be valid.

Core Idea
Following an imam who forgets sajdah al-sahw: prayer valid only if ma'mum performs it.

Sajdah al-sahw compensates for forgetfulness in prayer. But what if the imam himself forgets this prostration? This lesson clarifies the rule for the follower (ma'mum) when the imam omits sajdah al-sahw, based on a concise matn statement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A person leads another in prayer. The imam forgets to perform sajdah al-sahw at the end. The ma'mum notices this.
2
State the Ruling
The matn says: the follower's prayer is valid if he performs the sajdah al-sahw himself; otherwise it is invalid.
3
Identify the Condition
The validity hinges on the ma'mum performing the sajdah. This is a condition (shart) for the prayer to be sahih.
The imam's mistake does not automatically invalidate the follower's prayer.
4
Apply to a New Case
Imagine you are praying behind an imam who finishes the prayer and stands up without sajdah al-sahw. You are certain he forgot. What should you do? Perform the sajdah yourself, then complete the prayer. If you don't, your prayer is invalid per the Hanafi school.
This ruling applies even if the imam does not realize his mistake.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو فاقتدی به غیره صح ان سجد للسهو والا فلا يصح (۷۴۷)
Chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. If someone is followed by another, it is valid if he does the sajdah for forgetfulness, otherwise it is not valid.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This is a matn (core text) statement from the chapter on Sajdah al-Sahw. The ruling addresses a scenario where a person leads another in prayer, and the imam forgets to perform the sajdah al-sahw. The text states that if the follower performs the sajdah, the prayer is valid; if not, the prayer is invalid. The proof is not given here, but later in the commentary.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
اقتدى به غيره (iqtada bihi ghayru): Someone follows him in prayer as a ma'mum.
صح (sahh): Valid (sahih) – legally sound and acceptable.
فلا يصح (fa-la yasihh): It is not valid – the opposite of sahih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The follower must repeat the entire prayer.
D) The follower's prayer is always valid regardless.

Key Takeaway
When an imam forgets sajdah al-sahw, the ma'mum must perform it himself to keep his prayer valid.

Sajdah al-Sahw After Intentional Salam
Explains validity of sajdah after intentional salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-sahw after intentionally giving the salam, and identify the condition that preserves the validity of the sajdah.

Core Idea
Intentional salam does not nullify sajdah al-sahw if you haven't turned or spoken.

This lesson explores a subtle yet important point: if a person intentionally gives the salam to end his prayer, can he still perform sajdah al-sahw for an oversight? The Hanafi school answers affirmatively, but with a crucial condition. Understanding this ruling prevents unnecessary repetition of valid prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
From the matn, state the ruling: sajdah al-sahw is performed even after intentional salam, as long as two conditions are avoided.
The matn says 'wa yasjudu li al-sahw wa in sallama aamidan lil-qat'.
2
Analyze the condition
What are the barriers? The text says 'ma lam yatahawwal 'an al-qiblah aw yatakallam' – turning away from the qiblah or speaking.
These actions break the continuity required for sajdah.
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith of the Prophet praying five rak'ahs shows that after intentionally giving salam (due to forgetfulness), he performed sujood. This supports that intentional salam does not invalidate the obligation.
The hadith is cited from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Consider the opposing view
Note that other schools may have different conditions, but the Hanafi position is as stated.
The hanafi_position_box indicates cross_madhhab_ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario, determine if sajdah is valid based on the condition.
Practice with the example in the practice tasks.

And he performs sajdah for forgetfulness even if he intentionally gave salam to cut off, as long as he has not turned from the qiblah or spoken. And if a person praying four or three rak'ahs thought he had completed them and gave salam, then knew... Explanation: He had to do sajdah al-sahw, so even if he gave salam intentionally to end the prayer, as long as he hasn't turned from the qiblah, he can do sajdah. Proofs: (1) The salam before sajdah was required anyway; his intention to cut is ineffective because sajdah is wajib. Commentary
This is an expansion of the matn with proofs. The ruling states that even if a person intentionally gives the salam to cut off the prayer, his sajdah al-sahw is still valid as long as he has not turned away from the qiblah or spoken. The commentary explains that the intention to cut is overridden by the obligation of sajdah. Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of the Prophet who prayed five rak'ahs by mistake and gave salam, then performed sujood after being told. (2) The athar from Hasan al-Basri that if one forgets sajdah and remembers before turning away, he may perform it. Another scenario: a person who thought he completed four rak'ahs but only prayed two must complete the remaining two and then do sajdah al-sahw because he gave an incomplete salam. The hadith of Abu Huraira supports this.

Sajdah al-Sahw Due to Prolonged Reflection
Ruling statement on sajdah al-sahw for prolonged thought

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that triggers sajdah al-sahw for prolonged reflection and apply it to determine when sajdah is obligatory.

Core Idea
Prolonged reflection in prayer triggers sajdah al-sahw only if it lasts the duration of performing a rukn.

This matn from the chapter on doubt presents two scenarios involving sajdah al-sahw. The first is straightforward: after praying two rak'ahs, one completes them and performs sajdah al-sahw (likely due to forgetfulness). The second scenario is more specific: a person reflects for a long time, does not give salam until certain, and the ruling hinges on the duration of that reflection. The Hanafi school uses a precise measure — the time it takes to perform one integral part (rukn) — to determine whether sajdah al-sahw becomes obligatory. This lesson unpacks that condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and note that it first mentions completing two rak'ahs and performing sajdah al-sahw. Then it introduces a separate case: prolonged reflection without salam until certainty. Focus on the second ruling.
The first ruling is a general example; the second is the main lesson.
2
Locate the condition for sajdah
Find the phrase 'in kana qadr ada' rukn' (if it was the duration of performing a rukn). This is the key condition. If the reflection lasted that long, sajdah al-sahw is wajib (obligatory); otherwise, it is not.
The term 'ada' rukn' refers to the time needed to perform one integral, such as a full rak'ah.
3
Understand the measure
The condition is not any amount of thinking, but specifically the duration equivalent to performing a rukn (e.g., reciting al-Fatiha, bowing, and prostrating). Reflect on why this threshold matters — it separates normal hesitation from significant delay that disrupts the prayer's flow.
Hanafi fiqh often uses such concrete measures to avoid ambiguity.
4
Apply the rule
Given a scenario, assess whether the reflection lasted 'qadr ada' rukn'. If yes, sajdah al-sahw is wajib; if no, no sajdah is required. The prayer remains valid without it.
This ruling applies when the person has not yet given salam and later becomes certain of the number of rak'ahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فی الشک صلى ركعتين اتمها وسجد للسهو وان طال تفكره ولم يسلّم حتى استيقن ان كان قدر اداء ركن وجب عليه سجود السهو والا لا . (۷۴۹)
Chapter on Doubt. He prayed two rak'ahs, completed them, and performed sajdah al-sahw. And if his reflection was long and he did not give salam until he was certain: if it was the duration of performing a rukn, sajdah al-sahw is obligatory upon him; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This is a matn statement from the chapter on doubt. It first mentions a case where a person prays two rak'ahs and completes them, then does sajdah al-sahw (presumably due to forgetfulness). Then it discusses a scenario where a person reflects for a long time during prayer, unsure of the number of rak'ahs, and does not give salam until he becomes certain. If his reflection lasted the time it takes to perform one rukn (e.g., one rak'ah), then he must perform sajdah al-sahw; if less, no sajdah is required. This is a concise ruling without proof in this lesson.

Key Terms
قدر اداء ركن (qadr ada' rukn): The duration required to perform one integral part of prayer (e.g., one rak'ah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Thinking for the duration of a rukn.
C) Thinking until one is certain.
D) Thinking and then giving salam.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw for prolonged reflection is wajib only if the reflection lasts the duration of performing a rukn.

When Doubt Invalidates the Prayer – Conditions for Shakk in Rak'ah Count
Ruling on when doubt invalidates prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which doubt about the number of rak'ahs invalidates the prayer and distinguish it from habitual doubt.

Core Idea
Doubt in rak'ahs invalidates only if it is the first occurrence and before completion.

In this passage, we learn a key ruling about doubt (shakk) during prayer. Not every uncertainty breaks the prayer; only specific types. The matn outlines when doubt in the number of rak'ahs invalidates, and the commentary hints at exceptions. Let's unpack the precise conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is doubt (shakk) about the number of rak'ahs. The ruling: prayer becomes invalid (batil).
2
Identify the conditions for invalidation
Two conditions must be met: (1) doubt occurs before completing the prayer; (2) it is the first time such doubt occurs (or the person is not habitually doubtful).
The Arabic phrase 'awwala ma 'arada lahu' indicates first occurrence.
3
Recognize the exception for habitual doubt
If doubt is frequent (habitual), the prayer is not invalid. Instead, the person should act on his stronger assumption (ghalabat al-zann).
This is derived from the commentary and broader Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمه : (۷۵۰) رکعت کی تعداد میں شک سے نماز باطل ہو جاتی ہے، جبکہ نماز پوری کرنے سے پہلے ہو، اور پہلی مرتبہ شک پیش آیا ہو، یا شک اس کی عادت نہ ہو۔ اور اگر شک ہو اسلام کے بعد تو اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا مگر یہ کہ چھوڑنے کا یقین ہو جائے۔ تشریح : یہاں دو باتیں ہیں [1]...

Translation: Doubt in the number of rak'ahs invalidates prayer, provided it is before completion and it is the first time or not habitual. Doubt after Islam (i.e., after becoming Muslim) is not considered unless one is certain of omission. Explanation: There are two points...

Commentary
This matn introduces the chapter on doubt (shakk). The ruling states that if a person doubts the number of rak'ahs they have prayed, the prayer becomes invalid if (a) the doubt occurs before the prayer is completed, and (b) it is the first time such doubt occurs (or the person is not habitually doubtful). The Urdu translation adds that if the doubt occurs after becoming Muslim (i.e., in a general sense), it is not considered unless one is certain of an omission. The commentary begins to explain two points but cuts off.

Key Terms
شک (shakk): Doubt or uncertainty, specifically about the number of rak'ahs in prayer.
اول ما عرض له (awwala ma 'arada lahu): First occurrence of such doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, which of the following invalidates prayer?
A) Doubt after completion of prayer.
B) Doubt before completion and it is the first time.
C) Any doubt about anything.
D) Habitual doubt.

Key Takeaway
Prayer is invalidated only by first-time doubt before completion; habitual doubt requires acting on the stronger assumption.

Prolonged Doubt and Sajdah al-Sahw
Ruling on when prolonged thought requires prostration of forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib when prolonged doubt lasts the measure of one rukn.

Core Idea
Prolonged doubt lasting a rukn's measure makes sajdah al-sahw wajib.

During prayer, a worshiper may become uncertain about the number of rak'ahs already performed. The Hanafi school provides a precise criterion for when this doubt triggers the obligation of sajdah al-sahw. This lesson examines the ruling and its scriptural basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is prolonged thought (tafakkur) about the number of rak'ahs without saying salam. The ruling is that if the thought lasts as long as performing one rukn, sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib; otherwise it is not.
The measure is a rukn standing or sitting, not the entire prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah (Sunan Abi Dawud) where the Prophet ruled that if an imam stands after two rak'ahs and fully straightens, sajdah al-sahw is required. Also the athar of al-Zuhri.
Both proofs establish that committing to a new rukn (standing) without completion triggers sajdah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses 'standing' as a proxy for a rukn; analogically, prolonged thought that lasts the duration of a rukn also constitutes a delay of the next rukn, thus requiring sajdah.
The analogy is based on the shared illa: delaying an upcoming rukn.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may have different thresholds for sajdah al-sahw, but within the Hanafi school this is the established position.
The ruling is considered wajib, not sunnah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that sajdah al-sahw is wajib when the thought equals one rukn, based on the soundness of the analogy and the clarity of the proofs.
No substantial intra-madhhab dispute is recorded on this specific ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلى ركعتين اتمها وسجد للسهو (۷۴۹) وان طال تفكره ولم يسلّم حتى استيقن ان كان قدر اداء ركن وجب عليه سجود السهو والا لا . تشريح: دوركعت پڑھی ہے یا چار رکعت اس بارے میں سوچتارہا، پس اگر ایک رکن ادا کرنے کے برابر سوچتا رہا تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا، کیونکہ آگے والے رکن کی تاخیر ہوئی ، اور اگر ایک رکن ادا کرنے کی مقدار سے کم سوچا تو سجدہ سہولازم نہیں ہوگا ، کیونکہ کسی رکن کی تا خیر نہیں ہوئی۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث کے اشارے سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے ۔ عن مغيرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله الله اذا قام الامام في الركعتين فان ذكر قبل ان يستوى قائما فليجلس فان استوى قائما فلا يجلس ويسجد سجدتي السهو (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من نسی ان بیتشهد وهو جالس ،ص ۲۵۵، نمبر ۰۳۶ار دار قطنی ، باب الرجوع الی القعود قبل استمام القیام ج اول ص ۳۶۷ نمبر ۱۴۰۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھڑا ہو گیا تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا، اس سے استدلال کیا جاسکتا ہے کہ اگلارکن کرنے کی مقدار سوچتارہا تو اس کی تاخیر کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا۔ (2) اس قول تابعی میں بھی ہے۔ عن الزهري عليه في الرجل يسهو في الصلوة ان استوى قائما فعليه السجدتان ، و ان ذكر قبل أن يعتدل قائما فلان سهو ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۲۴۹ من کان یقول : اذالم يستقم قائما فلیس علیہ تھو ، ج اول ص ۳۹۰، نمبر ۴۴۹ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیٹھنے کے قریب ہو سجدہ سہو نہ کرے اور کھڑا ہو گیا ہوتو سجدہ سہو کرے۔ اس سے بھی استدلال کیا جاسکتا ہے کہ ایک رکن کی تا خیر ہوئی تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا۔
He prayed two rak'ahs and completed them and performed sajdah al-sahw. (749) And if his thought prolonged and he did not say salam until he was certain: if it was the measure of performing a rukn, sajdah al-sahw is wajib upon him; otherwise no.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on prolonged doubt during prayer. If a person is unsure whether they have prayed two or four rak'ahs and continues thinking for the duration of performing one rukn (e.g., a prostration), then because they have delayed the next rukn, sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib. If the thought was shorter than one rukn, no sajdah is required. The commentator adduces two proofs: (1) The hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah that if the imam stands up after two rak'ahs and then remembers before fully standing, he should sit; but if he has fully stood, he does not sit and performs sajdah al-sahw. This indicates that committing to the next rukn (standing) triggers sajdah. (2) The athar of al-Zuhri that if a person stands fully, two sajdahs are due; if he remembers before straightening up, no sajdah. Thus delaying a rukn by the measure of performing it makes sajdah wajib.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness or delay in prayer, based on the measure of a rukn.
تفكر (tafakkur): Prolonged thought or uncertainty about the number of rak'ahs.
ركن (rukn): An essential component of the prayer; in this context, it refers to any basic action like standing, bowing, or prostrating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does sajdah al-sahw become wajib due to prolonged thought about rak'ahs?
A) Whenever one doubts the number of rak'ahs
B) If one thinks for the duration of performing one rukn
C) If one thinks and then performs taslim
D) If one thinks for less than one rukn

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib only when prolonged doubt equals the time needed to perform one rukn.

Doubt in Rak'ahs Before Completion
Ruling on doubt in rak'ah count invalidating prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on doubt in prayer rak'ahs by distinguishing between first-time and habitual doubt, and determine when the prayer becomes invalid.

Core Idea
Non-habitual doubt about rak'ahs before salam invalidates the prayer; habitual doubt is resolved by predominant opinion.

Doubt in the number of rak'ahs can disrupt the certainty required for prayer. This passage from the Hanafi tradition clarifies that not all doubt leads to invalidity: the key distinction is whether the doubt is occasional or habitual, and whether it occurs before or after completing the prayer. Let's examine the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The ruling concerns salah. The hukm is batil (invalid) under specific conditions: doubt about the number of rak'ahs before completion, and the doubt is either first-time or not habitual.
The act is salah, the ruling is invalidity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the statement of Ibn Umar (qawl sahabi): 'Whoever does not know whether he prayed three or four should repeat until he is certain.'
This is found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'ya'id hatta yahfaz' implies that doubt invalidates the current prayer, as repeating is required when one is uncertain.
The command to repeat indicates that the initial prayer was not valid.
4
Note the exception for habitual doubt
The Hanafi school limits this ruling to first-time or non-habitual doubt. For habitual doubt, the person acts on predominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) and continues without repetition.
This exception prevents undue hardship for those who frequently doubt.

فصل : (في الشك) (750) تبطل الصلوة بالشك في عدد ركعاتها اذا كان قبل اكمالها وهو اول ما عرض له من الشك او كان الشك غير عادة له فلو شک بعد سلامه لا يعتبر الا ان تيقن بالترک. تشريح: يہاں دو باتیں ہیں [1] ایک تو یہ کہ نماز کی کتنی رکعتیں پڑھیں اس بارے میں پہلی مرتبہ شک ہوا ہو، یا بار بار ہوا ہولیکن شک اس کی عادت نہ ہو تو نماز باطل ہوگی، اس کو دوبارہ نماز پڑھنی چاہئے ۔ اور اگر شک کرنا اس کی عادت بن چکی ہو تو دوبارہ نماز پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے جس رکعت کے بارے میں ظن غالب ہو اس پر بنا کرے، اور نماز پوری کر لے ۔ [2] دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ نماز پوری کرنے سے پہلے ، اور سلام پھیرنے سے پہلے شک پیش آیا ہوتب نماز باطل قرار دی جائے گی، اور اگر سلام پھیر دیا تو نماز مکمل سمجھی جائے گی ، ہاں اگر یقین ہو جائے کہ تین ہی رکعت پڑھی ہے تو اب پہلی نماز باطل ہوگی دوبارہ نماز پڑھے، کیونکہ شک نہیں بلکہ یقین ہو گیا ہے کہ نماز تین ہی رکعت ہوئی ہے۔ وجه : اس قول صحابی میں ہے۔ عن ابن عـمـر فـي الذي لايدرى ثلاثا صلى او اربعا قال يعيد حتى يحفظ (مصنف ابن ابی هیبته ، ۲۳۹ باب من قال اذ اشک فلم یدر کم مصلی اعاد، ج اول ص ۱۳۸۵ نمبر ۴۴۲۲ ) اس اثر کو ہم اس پر حمل کرتے ہیں کہ پہلی مرتبہ شک ہوا ہو تو شروع سے نماز پڑھے، اور بار با رشک ہوتا ہو تو ظن غالب پر عمل کرے اور یقین پر عمل کرے۔جیسا کہ آگے آرہا ہے۔
Section on doubt: (750) Prayer becomes invalid by doubt in the number of its rak'ahs if it is before its completion, and it is the first time such doubt occurs or it is not habitual for him. So if he doubts after his salam, it is not considered unless he is certain of omission.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage addresses two scenarios: (1) The person has doubt about the number of rak'ahs for the first time, or it is not his habit—in this case, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. If doubt is habitual, he acts on his predominant opinion and continues. (2) The doubt occurs before completing the prayer (before salam); then the prayer is invalid. If doubt occurs after salam, the prayer is considered valid unless he becomes certain of having omitted something (e.g., only praying three rak'ahs). The evidence is the athar of Ibn 'Umar that one who does not know whether he prayed three or four should repeat until he is certain. The commentator interprets this as applying to the first occurrence of doubt; for habitual doubt, the later ruling (acting on predominant opinion) applies.

Key Terms
شك (shakk): Equal doubt between two possibilities (e.g., whether prayed two or three rak'ahs).
عادة (aadah): Habit of doubting; if one frequently doubts, special rules apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Non-habitual doubt about rak'ahs before salam invalidates the prayer; habitual doubt is resolved by acting on predominant opinion.

Frequent Doubt in Prayer: Acting on Predominant Opinion
Ruling on how a frequent doubter should proceed in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a frequent doubter (mustars) to determine the correct number of rak'ahs when doubt arises.

Core Idea
Frequent doubters act on predominant opinion; if none, take the lesser and sit after each rak'ah.

This lesson addresses a common issue in salah: doubting the number of rak'ahs. The Hanafi school provides a specific ruling for those who frequently experience doubt (waswas). Instead of repeating the prayer, they rely on their predominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) or, failing that, take the minimum number and add precautionary sittings. The ruling is supported by authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of doubt
Determine whether the person is a frequent doubter (mustars) or occasional. The ruling applies only to frequent doubt.
Frequent doubt is defined as occurring in most prayers or at least once every prayer.
2
Assess predominant opinion
If the doubter has a predominant opinion (ghalib al-zann) about the number of rak'ahs, he acts on that opinion and completes the prayer accordingly.
Predominant opinion means one side seems more likely, e.g., 3 rak'ahs rather than 2.
3
Apply the default: lesser number
If no predominant opinion exists, he takes the lesser number (al-aqall) and sits after every rak'ah that he thinks might be his last.
This precaution ensures the prayer is valid even if the actual number differs.
4
Understand the proof
The hadith: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer, let him seek the correct (opinion) and complete upon it, then prostrate twice.' This commands acting on predominant opinion.
The Hanafi school interprets 'seek the correct' as acting on ghalib al-zann.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٧٥١ وان كثر الشك عمل بغالب ظنه فان لم يغلب له ظن اخذ بالاقل وقعد بعد كل ركعة ظنها آخر صلوته. تشریح : اور بار بار شک ہونے کی عادت ہوگئی ہو تو یہ دیکھے کہ غالب گمان کیا ہے اس کو لے، مثلا دورکعت اور تین رکعت میں شک ہے اور غالب گمان ہے کہ تین پڑھی ہے تو اسی کو لے اور چوتھی رکعت ملا کر نماز پوری کر لے، اور اگر کسی طرف غالب گمان بھی نہیں ہو رہا ہے تو اقل، جو کم درجہ ہے اس کو لے، مثلا دو اور تین رکعت میں شک ہے تو دورکعت کو اصل بنا کر دورکعت اور ملالے اور نماز پوری کرے ۔ لیکن یہ بھی خطرہ ہے کہ جسکو وہ دورکعت سمجھ رہا ہے وہ حقیقت میں تیسری رکعت ہو ، اور ایک مزید ملائی تو یہ چوتھی ہو گئی ، جسکے بعد بیٹھنا فرض ہے، اس لئے ہر رکعت کے بعد بیٹھے۔ وجه (1) پہلے غالب گمان کا اعتبار کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قال عبد الله صلى رسول الله ... واذا شک احـدكـم فـي صـلـوتـه فليتحر الصواب فليتم عليه ثم يسجد سجدتين ۔ دوسرى حدیث میں ہے فلینظر احری ذلك للصواب (مسلم شریف ، باب من شک فی صلوته فلم یدرکم صلی فلطرح الشک الخ، ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۲ ۱۲۷۶/۱۲۷۴/۵۷ را بو داود شریف ، باب اذ اصلی خمسا ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۱۰۲۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ غور کرنا چاہئے کہ کتنی رکعت پڑھی ہے تا کہ جس طرف ظن غالب ہو اس پر عمل کیا جا سکے۔ (2) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ یقین کی طرف جائے۔ عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال قال رسول
751 And if doubt is frequent, he acts on his predominant opinion; if no opinion predominates, he takes the lesser and sits after every rak'ah which he thinks is his last prayer.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage deals with a person who frequently doubts the number of rak'ahs (e.g., a sufferer of waswas). Such a person should not repeat the prayer but instead act on his predominant opinion (ghalib al-zann). For example, if he is between two and three and thinks three is more likely, he adds one more rak'ah to complete four. If no opinion is stronger, he takes the lower number (al-aqall): if between two and three, he assumes two and adds two more. However, because it is possible that the two he thought were actually three, adding one would make four, so to ensure he sits after an odd number, he should sit after every rak'ah thinking it is his last. The commentator provides hadiths: (1) 'If one of you doubts in his prayer, let him seek what is correct and complete it, then prostrate twice.' (Muslim) (2) 'Let him look for the most likely correct.' This supports acting on predominant opinion. Another hadith (Abu Sa'id al-Khudri) advises going with certainty, which in this context means taking the lesser when no opinion dominates.

Key Terms
غالب الظن (ghalib al-zann): Predominant opinion; what appears more likely to the doubter.
اقل (al-aqall): The lesser number of rak'ahs in a doubt scenario (e.g., two if between two and three).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Repeat the prayer
B) Take the lesser number of rak'ahs and sit after every rak'ah
C) Take the greater number
D) Wait until certainty

Key Takeaway
A frequent doubter in prayer acts on predominant opinion; if none, he takes the minimum and adds precautionary sittings after each rak'ah.

Rulings on Doubt in Prayer: Frequent vs. Infrequent Doubters
Explains how to handle doubt in prayer based on whether it is habitual

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the rulings for a frequent doubter (kathir al-shakk) and a non-habitual doubter in prayer, and apply the appropriate remedy according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
For the frequent doubter, act on dominant presumption; for the infrequent, repeat the prayer if doubt occurs before salam.

Doubt in prayer (shakk) is a common issue. The Hanafi school provides distinct rulings based on whether doubt is habitual. This lesson explains the criteria and the proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of doubters
Recognize that the ruling depends on whether doubt is a habitual occurrence for the person (kathir al-shakk) or not ('adah lahu).
Habitual doubter: someone who frequently experiences doubts, to the extent that it becomes characteristic.
2
State the ruling for non-habitual doubt
If doubt occurs before salam, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. If after salam, the prayer stands unless certainty of deficiency arises.
This is based on the hadith to discard doubt and build on certainty.
3
State the ruling for habitual doubt
The habitual doubter should act on his dominant presumption (ghalib al-zann). If no dominant presumption, he takes the minimum number of rak'ahs and sits after every rak'ah as if it were the last.
This provides ease for those with waswas, preventing unnecessary repetition.
4
Locate the dalil for each scenario
The author cites the Companion's statement (Ibn 'Umar) for the non-habitual case, and several ahadith for the habitual case (dominant presumption hadith, building on certainty hadith, and minimum hadith).
All proofs are ahad hadiths, zanni al-thubut, but sufficient for amal.
5
Explain how the hadiths are reconciled
The Hanafi school reconciles the seemingly conflicting hadiths by applying istihsan: the general rule (discard doubt, build on certainty) is for the non-habitual doubter; the exceptions (act on dominant presumption or minimum) are for the habitual doubter.
This illustrates the principle of takhsis al-'amm bi al-istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل فی الشک الشك او كان الشك غير عادة له فلو شک بعد سلامه لا يعتبر الا ان تيقن بالترک (۷۵۱) وان كثر الشك عمل بغالب ظنه فان لم يغلب له ظن اخذ بالاقل وقعد بعد كل ركعة ظنها آخر صلوته. شک اس کی عادت نہ ہو تو نماز باطل ہوگی، اس کو دوبارہ نماز پڑھنی چاہئے ۔ اور اگر شک کرنا اس کی عادت بن چکی ہو تو دوبارہ نماز پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے جس رکعت کے بارے میں ظن غالب ہو اس پر بنا کرے، اور نماز پوری کر لے ۔ [۲] دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ نماز پوری کرنے سے پہلے ، اور سلام پھیرنے سے پہلے شک پیش آیا ہوتب نماز باطل قرار دی جائے گی، اور اگر سلام پھیر دیا تو نماز مکمل سمجھی جائے گی ، ہاں اگر یقین ہو جائے کہ تین ہی رکعت پڑھی ہے تو اب پہلی نماز باطل ہوگی دوبارہ نماز پڑھے، کیونکہ شک نہیں بلکہ یقین ہو گیا ہے کہ نماز تین ہی رکعت ہوئی ہے۔ وجه : اس قول صحابی میں ہے۔ عن ابن عـمـر فـي الذي لايدرى ثلاثا صلى او اربعا قال يعيد حتى يحفظ (مصنف ابن ابی هیبته ، ۲۳۹ باب من قال اذ اشک فلم یدر کم مصلی اعاد، ج اول ص ۱۳۸۵ نمبر ۴۴۲۲ ) اس اثر کو ہم اس پر حمل کرتے ہیں کہ پہلی مرتبہ شک ہوا ہو تو شروع سے نماز پڑھے، اور بار با رشک ہوتا ہو تو ظن غالب پر عمل کرے اور یقین پر عمل کرے۔جیسا کہ آگے آرہا ہے۔ ترجمه : (۷۵۱) اور جس کو زیادہ شک ہوتا ہو وہ اپنے ظن غالب پر عمل کرے۔ اور اگر اس کو کسی جانب گمان غالب نہ ہو تو اقل کو لیوے، اور ہر ایک رکعت پر اخیر نماز کے خیال سے قعدہ کرے۔ تشریح : اور بار بار شک ہونے کی عادت ہوگئی ہو تو یہ دیکھے کہ غالب گمان کیا ہے اس کو لے، مثلا دورکعت اور تین رکعت میں شک ہے اور غالب گمان ہے کہ تین پڑھی ہے تو اسی کو لے اور چوتھی رکعت ملا کر نماز پوری کر لے، اور اگر کسی طرف غالب گمان بھی نہیں ہو رہا ہے تو اقل، جو کم درجہ ہے اس کو لے، مثلا دو اور تین رکعت میں شک ہے تو دورکعت کو اصل بنا کر دورکعت اور ملالے اور نماز پوری کرے ۔ لیکن یہ بھی خطرہ ہے کہ جسکو وہ دورکعت سمجھ رہا ہے وہ حقیقت میں تیسری رکعت ہو ، اور ایک مزید ملائی تو یہ چوتھی ہو گئی ، جسکے بعد بیٹھنا فرض ہے، اس لئے ہر رکعت کے بعد بیٹھے۔ وجه (۱) پہلے غالب گمان کا اعتبار کرے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قال عبد الله صلى رسول الله ... واذا شک احـدكـم فـي صـلـوتـه فليتحر الصواب فليتم عليه ثم يسجد سجدتين ۔ دوسرى حدیث میں ہے فلینظر احری ذلك للصواب (مسلم شریف ، باب من شک فی صلوته فلم یدرکم صلی فلطرح الشک الخ، ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۲ ۱۲۷۶/۱۲۷۴/۵۷ را بو داود شریف ، باب اذ اصلی خمسا ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۱۰۲۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ غور کرنا چاہئے کہ کتنی رکعت پڑھی ہے تا کہ جس طرف ظن غالب ہو اس پر عمل کیا جا سکے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ یقین کی طرف جائے۔ عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا شک احدکم فی صلوته فلم يدر كم صلى؟ ثلاثا ام اربعا؟ فليطرح الشك وليبن على ما استيقن ثم يسجد سجدتين قبل ان يسلم (مسلم شریف، باب السمو في الصلوۃ والسجو د ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۲۷۲٫۵۷ ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا شک فی السنتين والثلاث، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۱۰۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظن غالب نہ ہو بلکہ دونوں طرف شک ہو تو یقین پر بنا کرے۔(۳) اور نظن غالب نہ ہوتا ہو تو اقل درجے کو لے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔عن عبد الرحمن ابن عوف قال سمعت النبي يقول (( اذا سها أحدكم في صلاته فلم يدرواحدة صلى أو اثنين فليبن على واحدة فان لـم يـدر ثـنـتـيـن صـلـى أو ثلاثا فليبن على ثنتين ، فان لم يدر ثلاثا صلى أو أربعا فليبن على ثلاثا ، وليسجد سجدتين قبل أن يسلم ترندی ،شریف، باب فیمن بیشک فی الزيادة والنقصان ، ص ۱۰۷، نمبر ۳۹۸ رابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن شک فی صلاته فرجع الی الیقین ، ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۱۲۰۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اقل پر بناء کرے۔
Chapter on Doubt. Doubt, if it is not habitual for him, then if he doubts after his salam it is not considered unless he becomes certain of omission (751). And if doubt is frequent, he acts on his dominant presumption. If he has no dominant presumption, he takes the minimum and sits after every rak'ah thinking it the last of his prayer. [Urdu commentary: If doubt is not habitual, prayer becomes invalid; he must repeat. If doubt has become habitual, repeating is not necessary; he builds on what is dominant, and completes prayer. Second: If doubt occurs before completion and before salam, prayer is ruled invalid; if salam has been given, prayer is considered complete. However, if he becomes certain he prayed only three rak'ahs, then the first prayer is invalid and he repeats, because it is certainty not doubt. Evidence: from the saying of a Companion: Ibn 'Umar regarding one who does not know whether he prayed three or four: he said he must repeat until he retains. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ...) We interpret this effect as applying to the first occurrence of doubt; for repeated doubt, act on dominant presumption and certainty, as will come. Translation of (751): And one who frequently doubts acts on his dominant presumption. If he has no dominant presumption, he takes the minimum and sits after each rak'ah with the intent that it is his last. Explanation: When doubt becomes habitual, he sees what his dominant presumption is. For example, if he doubts between two and three rak'ahs and his dominant presumption is that he prayed three, he takes that and adds a fourth, completing the prayer. If no dominant presumption, he takes the minimum, e.g., he assumes two rak'ahs and adds two, completing the prayer. But there is a risk: that which he thinks is the second might actually be the third; adding one would make it the fourth, after which sitting is obligatory. Therefore he sits after every rak'ah. Evidence (1): For relying on dominant presumption, there is this hadith: 'Abdullah said: The Messenger of Allah ... and when one of you doubts in his prayer, let him seek what is correct and complete it, then prostrate two prostrations.' Another hadith: 'Let him consider what is more likely correct.' (Muslim, ...) From this hadith it is understood that he should reflect how many rak'ahs he has prayed so that he can act on his dominant presumption. (2) This hadith indicates going towards certainty: Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrated that the Messenger of Allah said: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer and does not know how many he prayed, three or four, let him discard the doubt and build on what he is certain of, then prostrate two prostrations before salam.' (Muslim, ...) This hadith states that when there is no dominant presumption and doubt is equal, he builds on certainty. (3) And when there is no dominant presumption, he takes the minimum degree. For this there is this hadith: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf said: I heard the Prophet say: 'When one of you forgets in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed one or two, let him build on one; if he does not know whether he prayed two or three, let him build on two; if he does not know whether he prayed three or four, let him build on three, and prostrate two prostrations before salam.' (Tirmidhi, ...) This hadith indicates building on the minimum.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on doubt (shakk) in prayer. The author distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) The person for whom doubt is not habitual (ghayr 'adah lahu) and (2) the person for whom doubt is frequent (kathir al-shakk). For the first, if doubt occurs before completing the prayer (i.e., before salam), the prayer is invalid (batil) and must be repeated. If doubt occurs after salam, it is disregarded unless he becomes certain that he omitted something. For the second, the habitual doubter, he should act on his dominant presumption (ghalib al-zann). If he has no dominant presumption, he takes the minimum number of rak'ahs he is sure of and sits after every rak'ah as if it could be the last. The author supports this with several hadiths: from Ibn 'Umar (a Companion's statement), from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (the hadith to discard doubt and build on certainty), and from 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf (the hadith to build on the minimum). The Hanafi position is clear: the habitual doubter's prayer is valid provided he follows these rules; the non-habitual doubter's prayer is invalid if doubt occurs during the prayer. The proofs are from the Sunnah via ahad hadiths, which are zanni in transmission but give probabilistic certainty for legal rulings.

Key Terms
شک (shakk): Doubt or uncertainty about the number of rak'ahs performed in prayer.
ظن غالب (ghalib al-zann): Dominant presumption; a stronger probability in one's mind regarding the number of rak'ahs prayed.
اقل (aqall): The minimum number of rak'ahs that one is certain of having performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person who frequently has doubts in prayer do if he has no dominant presumption?
A) Repeat the prayer from the beginning
B) Build on the minimum number of rak'ahs and sit after each rak'ah
C) Continue as if nothing happened
D) Perform sajdat al-sahw immediately

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between habitual and non-habitual doubt, allowing the frequent doubter to act on dominant presumption or the minimum to avoid excessive repetition.

Sujud al-Tilawah: Definition, Evidence, and First Five Verses
Definition and evidence of sujud al-tilawah, plus list of first five verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of sujud al-tilawah, cite the hadith evidence for its wujub, and list the first five Quranic verses of prostration recognized in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon reciting or hearing any of the fourteen specific Quranic verses.

Sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) is a distinct act of worship in Hanafi fiqh. This lesson introduces its definition, the primary evidence from the Sunnah, and the first five verses that trigger its obligation. Understanding this foundation is essential before studying the remaining verses and the legal details of performing the prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sujud al-tilawah is the prostration performed upon reciting or hearing specific Quranic verses. In the Hanafi school, its ruling is wajib (obligatory), falling between fard and sunnah.
The term 'wajib' indicates a binding obligation with some flexibility in evidence strength compared to fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas (ra) that the Prophet (saws) prostrated at Surah an-Najm, and everyone present (Muslims, polytheists, jinn, humans) prostrated with him. This proves the obligation for both reciter and listener.
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent action, and the participation of all present including non-Muslims, indicates that prostration is an integral part of reciting such verses. In Hanafi usul, this practice amounts to wujub.
The Hanafi school interprets the evidence as proof of obligation; the Shafi'i school sees it as recommended.
4
Note the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i
The Shafi'i school considers sujud al-tilawah sunnah (recommended), not wajib. This difference stems from their interpretation of the same hadith and the principle that the Prophet's action does not obligatory.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are valid within their respective usul.
5
Memorize the first five verses
The text lists the first five of fourteen sajdah verses: Surah al-A'raf (7:206), Surah ar-Ra'd (13:15), Surah an-Nahl (16:49), Surah al-Isra' (17:107), and Surah Maryam (19:58). Commit these to memory.
These are the first five in the commonly accepted Hanafi list; the remaining nine are covered in later lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب: سجدہ تلاوت کے بیان میں کچھ ضروری نوٹ: قرآن کریم میں چودہ آیتیں ہیں جن کے پڑھنے سے سجدہ کرنا واجب ہوتا ہے۔ ان کو سجدہ تلاوت کہتے ہیں۔ سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبی ا ســجــد بالنجم وسجد معه . الله المسلمون والمشركون والجن والانس ( بخاری شریف ، باب سجدة النجم ص ۱۴۶ نمبر ۱۰۷ار مسلم شریف ، باب مسجود التلاوة ص ۲۱۵ نمبر ۱۲۹۷/۵۷۶) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ آیت سجدہ پڑھنے سے سجدہ کرنا چاہئے ۔اور جولوگ سنے ان کو بھی سجدہ کرنا چاہئے ۔ وہ آیتیں یہ ہیں۔ چودہ آیت تلاوت ایک نظر میں ہے [1] ان الذين عند ربك لا يستكبرون عن عبادته و يسبحونه و له يسجدون . (سورۃ اعراف ۷، آیت ۲۰۶) [٢] و الله يسجد من فى السماوات و الارض طوعا و کرها و ظلالهم بالغدو والاصال (سورۃ رعد ۱۳، آیت (۱۵) [٣] ولله يسجد ما في السموات وما فى الارض من دابة و الملائكة و هم لا يستكبرون (،سورة النحل ۱۶ آیت ۴۹) [۴] اذا تتلى عليهم يخرون للاذقان سجدا ( سورۃ اسراء۱۷، آیت ۱۰۷) [۵] اذا تتلى عليهم آيات الرحمن خروا سجدا وبكيا (سورۃ مریم ۱۹، آیت ۵۸)
Chapter: Some necessary notes on the prostration of recitation. In the Holy Quran, there are fourteen verses upon whose recitation prostration becomes wajib. They are called sujud al-tilawah. The evidence for sujud al-tilawah being wajib is this hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet prostrated at [the verse of] an-Najm, and the Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans prostrated with him. (Bukhari, Bab sajdat an-najm; Muslim, Bab masajid at-tilawa) From this hadith it is established that upon reciting a verse of prostration, one should prostrate. And those who hear it should also prostrate. Those verses are: [list of 5 verses given]
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The author states that there are fourteen verses in the Quran that make prostration wajib when recited or heard. The evidence is a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas: the Prophet (peace be upon him) prostrated at the verse of Surah an-Najm, and everyone present – Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans – prostrated with him. This demonstrates that the action is wajib for both reciter and listener. The author then lists the first five of these fourteen verses: from Surah al-A'raf (7:206), Surah ar-Ra'd (13:15), Surah an-Nahl (16:49), Surah al-Isra' (17:107), and Surah Maryam (19:58). This list is commonly memorized by Hanafi students. The Hanafi school holds sujud al-tilawah to be wajib, whereas the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. The difference stems from the interpretation of the command; Hanafis view the Prophet's consistent practice as indicating obligation.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing specific Quranic verses of prostration; wajib in the Hanafi school.
سجدة (sajdah): A single prostration, performed in sujud al-tilawah without takbirat al-ihram or sitting between prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many verses of prostration (ayaat sajdah) are there in the Quran according to the Hanafi school?
A) 10
B) 14
C) 12
D) 7

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib in the Hanafi school; the obligation is triggered by reciting or hearing any of the fourteen sajdah verses, with evidence from the Prophet's practice in Surah an-Najm.

Ruling on Doubt in Rak'at: Building on Certainty
Explains sajdah al-sahw for doubt in prayer rak'at

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on doubt in the number of rak'at by identifying when to build on certainty and when to act on predominant guess, and state the correct timing of sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
When doubt arises in rak'at without predominant guess, build on the lesser number and prostrate before salām.

In prayer, doubt about the number of rak'at can occur. The Hanafi school, based on authentic hadith, provides clear guidance: if you have no strong presumption (zann ghalib), you must build on what is certain (yaqeen)—the lesser number—and then perform two extra prostrations (sajdah al-sahw) before ending the prayer. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Doubt in the number of rak'at triggers the obligation of sajdah al-sahw. Determine if the doubt is pure (shakk) or with a predominant guess (zann ghalib).
If zann ghalib is present, act on it and still prostrate before salam.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith in Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah. The first hadith commands building on certainty; the second specifies the lesser number for each case.
These are ahad hadith, with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperatives 'falyatruh' (let him cast aside) and 'fal yabni' (let him build) indicate obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul. The command to prostrate before salam confirms the timing.
The Shafi'i school interprets these commands differently, leading to a later timing.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school builds on the lesser number but prostrates after salam, citing other evidence.
Both schools agree on building on the lesser; the dispute is on timing.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the explicit wording 'before salām' and the principle that sajdah al-sahw for deficiency is performed before salam. This is the relied-upon view.
The tarjih is from zahir al-riwayah and supported by later Hanafi masters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود التلاوة ثمرة النجاح جلد ٢ ۴۷ باب سجود التلاوة صلى الله الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا شک احدکم فی صلوته فلم يدر كم صلى؟ ثلاثا ام اربعا؟ فليطرح الشك وليبن على ما استيـقـن ثـم يـسـجـد سجدتين قبل ان يسلم (مسلم شریف ، باب السمو في الصلوۃ والسجو د ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۱۲۷۲٫۵۷ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب اذا شک فی السنتين والثلاث ، ص ۱۵۵، نمبر ۱۰۲۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ظن غالب نہ ہو بلکہ دونوں طرف شک ہو تو یقین پر بنا کرے۔(۳) اور نظن غالب نہ ہوتا ہو تو اقل درجے کو لے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔عن عبد الرحمن ابن عوف صلى الله قال سمعت النبي عل يقول (( اذا سها أحدكم في صلاته فلم يدرواحدة صلى أو اثنين فليبن على واحدة فان لـم يـدر ثـنـتـيـن صـلـى أو ثلاثا فليبن على ثنتين ، فان لم يدر ثلاثا صلى أو أربعا فليبن على ثلاثا ، وليسجد سجدتين قبل أن يسلم ترندی ،شریف، باب فیمن بیشک فی الزيادة والنقصان ، ص ۱۰۷، نمبر ۳۹۸ رابن ماجہ شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن شک فی صلاته فرجع الی الیقین ، ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۱۲۰۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اقل پر بناء کرے۔
Chapter of prostration of recitation. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'If one of you doubts in his prayer and does not know how many he prayed, three or four, then let him cast aside the doubt and build upon what he is certain of, then prostrate two prostrations before salām.' (Muslim, Abu Dawud). This hadith indicates that when there is no predominant guess and both sides are doubtful, he builds on certainty. And when there is no predominant guess, he takes the lesser number; for this there is the hadith from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf: He heard the Prophet say: 'If one of you forgets in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed one or two, let him build on one; if he does not know two or three, build on two; if he does not know three or four, build on three, and prostrate two prostrations before salām.' (Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah). This hadith indicates building on the lesser.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding sajdah al-sahw when one doubts the number of rak'at performed. The first hadith, from Muslim and Abu Dawud, instructs that when doubt occurs without any predominant guess (zann ghalib), one must build on certainty (yaqeen) and then perform two extra prostrations (sajdah al-sahw) before ending the prayer. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this applies when both possibilities are equally likely. The second hadith, from Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah, provides specific guidance for different levels of doubt: if uncertain between one and two, build on one; between two and three, build on two; between three and four, build on three. In all cases, prostrate before salam. This is the Hanafi position: in the absence of zann ghalib, one takes the lesser number (which is also the yaqeen). If a predominant guess exists, one acts on it and still performs sajdah al-sahw. These hadith are the primary textual evidence for this ruling.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness or doubt in prayer.
ظن غالب (zann ghalib): A strong presumption that overcomes doubt; the prayer's prevailing belief.
شك (shakk): Equal doubt between two possibilities, such as between three and four rak'at.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if he doubts whether he prayed three or four rak'at and has no predominant guess?
A) Build on four rak'at and prostrate after salam.
B) Build on three rak'at (the lesser) and prostrate before salam.
C) Repeat the entire prayer.
D) Build on whatever comes to mind.

Key Takeaway
In case of doubt in rak'at without predominant guess, the Hanafi ruling is to build on the lesser number (yaqeen) and perform sajdah al-sahw before salām.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Sujūd al-Tilāwah: Ruling, Verses, and Evidence
Lists 14 ayat of sajdah and rules on prostration obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of sujūd al-tilāwah, identify the fourteen sajdah verses, and explain the evidence from hadith that obligates prostration on both the reciter and the listener.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilāwah is wajib upon reciting or hearing any of the fourteen verses, proven by the Prophet's consistent practice.

In the Hanafi school, reciting or hearing certain Quranic verses triggers an obligation: a single prostration known as sujūd al-tilāwah. This lesson identifies the fourteen verses and unpacks the textual evidence that establishes this duty as wajib (not fard) and binding on both the reciter and the attentive listener.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is sujūd al-tilāwah (prostration of recitation). According to the text, it is wajib when a sajdah verse is recited or heard.
The text says 'واجب' and 'fi al-sahih' indicates the relied-upon view.
2
Locate the primary proof
Find the hadith evidence: the Prophet's prostration at Surah An-Najm and the companions prostrating with him. The text cites Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar.
The hadith are from Bukhari and Muslim, indicating ahad transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves obligation: the Prophet's consistent action and the companions' practice without disapproval shows wujub according to Hanafi usul (al-fil al-mutāba‘ yadull ‘alā al-wujūb).
This is a zanni proof, hence the ruling is wajib, not fard.
4
Note the scope: reciter and listener
The text states 'سببه التلاوة على التالى والسامع' – the cause is recitation for both the reciter and the listener. The commentary affirms this with additional athar.
The listener must hear attentively; the obligation applies even if not reciting.
5
Understand the timing: with delay (alā al-tarākhī)
The obligation is not immediate; one may delay the prostration, but it must be performed eventually. The text says 'وهو واجب على التراخي'.
If delayed, it remains a debt (qada) until performed.

The proof that sajdat al-tilāwah is obligatory is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prostrated at Surah An-Najm and prostrated with him the Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans (Bukhari, Muslim). Translation: (752) The cause of prostration is recitation upon the listener and also upon the reciter according to the correct madhhab. Proof (1) The proof of it being obligatory is this hadith: From Ibn Umar: The Prophet used to recite a sajdah while we were with him, and he would prostrate and we would prostrate with him, and we would crowd so much that none of us could find a place for his forehead to prostrate (Bukhari, Muslim). From this hadith, it is understood that prostration is obligatory on the reciter and on the listeners. (2) From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet prostrated at Surah An-Najm, and prostrated with him Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith proves that when a verse of sajdah is recited, one should prostrate, and those who hear should also prostrate. (3) This is supported by the saying of a tabi'i: From Ibn Umar: 'Indeed the sajdah is upon the one who hears it.' (No. 4225) (4) From Ibrahim, Nafi', and Sa'id ibn Jubayr: They said, 'Whoever hears the sajdah, upon him is to prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol.1 p.1367 no.4222).
