Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding sujūd al-tilāwah. It begins by stating that there are fourteen verses in the Quran that, upon recitation, make prostration wajib. It then provides the primary proof: the hadith of Ibn Abbas (in the introduction) and later repeats it along with the hadith of Ibn Umar. The core ruling is given in the matn lines (752 and 753): the cause (sabab) of sujūd al-tilāwah is recitation (tilāwah), and it applies to both the reciter (tāli) and the listener (sāmi‘) according to the correct view. Furthermore, it is wajib with delay (alā al-tarākhī), meaning if one does not prostrate immediately, the obligation remains and can be fulfilled later. The text then lists all fourteen verses of sajdah as per the Hanafi school. The Urdu commentary elaborates on the matn, providing additional hadith evidence: the hadith of Ibn Umar showing the Prophet and his companions prostrated together, and the hadith of Ibn Abbas with the prostration during Surah An-Najm. It also quotes statements of tabi‘ūn (successors) to affirm that hearing the verse obligates prostration. This establishes the wajib nature of sujūd al-tilāwah for both reciter and attentive listener, regardless of whether one is in prayer or outside it. The passage emphasizes that the obligation is not immediate but can be delayed, though it must be performed eventually without undue procrastination.

Key Terms
سجدہ تلاوت (sajdah al-tilāwah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing specific Quranic verses of prostration.
تالى (tāli): The person who recites a verse of sajdah aloud or silently.
سامع (sāmi‘): The person who hears a verse of sajdah (attentively).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is sunnah, not wajib.
B) It is wajib only if he is listening intentionally.
C) It is wajib upon hearing, same as recitation.
D) It is not required unless he also recited.

Key Takeaway
Sujūd al-tilāwah is a wajib act triggered by recitation or attentive hearing of any of the fourteen designated Quranic verses, with the obligation being delayable but not remissible.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Obligation and Cause of Sajdah al-Tilawah
Defines cause, obligation, and respite ruling with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cause of Sajdah al-Tilawah, explain its Hanafi ruling of wajib, and apply the rule of 'respite' (tarakhi) outside prayer.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-Tilawah is wajib upon both reciter and listener, but outside prayer it may be delayed.

This lesson covers the foundational ruling of Sajdah al-Tilawah: what triggers it, who must perform it, and when. The Hanafi school considers it wajib (obligatory but less than fard), supported by hadith evidence. A key nuance is that outside of prayer, the obligation is on respite—you may postpone it, though delaying unnecessarily is discouraged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its cause
The cause is recitation of a sajdah verse, and the obligation falls on both the reciter and the listener (the one who hears it).
Listener includes even those who hear unintentionally.
2
State the ruling
Sajdah al-Tilawah is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, not fard. This is because the evidence is ahad (solitary hadith).
Wajib requires intention and certainty but is one degree below fard.
3
Note the epistemic weight
The evidence: hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas show the Prophet and companions consistently prostrated upon recitation. This prophetic action (fi‘l) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul when done consistently without explanation of permissibility.
Thus the ruling is based on Sunnah ahad, hence wajib.
4
Apply the condition of 'respite'
Outside prayer, the obligation is not immediate; one may delay the sajdah. However, delaying without excuse is makruh tanzihi (disliked).
The action of Ibn Umar, who made up a sajdah after sunrise, is the proof.
5
Evaluate the evidence
The text presents four proofs: the hadith of Ibn Umar, the hadith of Ibn Abbas, the saying of Ibn Umar as a Tabi‘i, and the athar from Ibrahim, Nafi‘, and Sa‘id ibn Jubayr. All establish obligation on both reciter and listener.
The third proof is a qawl of a Tabi‘i, which supports but does not independently establish obligation.

ترجمه : (۷۵۳)، اگر نماز میں نہ ہو تو مؤخر کر کے واجب ہے۔ البتہ اس کی تاخیر مکروہ تنزیہی ہے۔ تشریح : اگر نماز میں نہ ہو تو جس وقت سنا اسی وقت سجدہ تلاوت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ تاخیر کے ساتھ بھی سجدہ کرسکتا ہے، البتہ بغیر عذر کے تاخیر کرنا مکروہ نزیہی ہے، کیونکہ عبادت میں بلا تاخیر کرنا اچھا نہیں ہے۔
وجه : عن المغيرة بن الحكيم قال كنت مع ابن عمر فقرا قاص بسجدة بعد الصبح فصاح عليه ابن عمر فسجد القاص و لم يسجد ابن عمر فلما طلعت الشمس قضاها ابن عمر يقول سجدها ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب هل تقضى السجدة ؟ ج ثالث ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۵۹۵۳) اس عمل صحابی میں ہے کہ بعد میں قضا کیا۔
ترجمه : (۷۵۴) جس نے آیت تلاوت کی اس پر بھی سجدہ لازم ہو گا چاہے فارسی زبان میں ہی کیوں نہ تلاوت کرے۔ تشریح : اوپر حدیث گزرگئی جس میں ہے کہ پڑھنے والے پر بھی سجدہ واجب ہے، چنانچہ فارسی زبان میں تلاوت کرے تب بھی سجدہ واجب ہوگا۔
ترجمه : (۷۵۵) آیت سجدہ کا ایک حرف پڑھنا ماقبل کے کلمے کے ساتھ ملا کر، یا مابعد کے ساتھ ملا کر صحیح روایت میں پوری آیت کی طرح ہے۔ تشریح : حرف السجدة ، سے مراد ہے وہ پورا کلمہ جس میں سجدہ کا لفظ ہے، یا سجدے کی طرف اشارہ ہے مثلا, و لله يسجد ما في السموات ، میں یسجد ، حرف سجدہ ہے۔ اور عبارت کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تنہا سجدے کے کلمے کو پڑھنے سے سجدہ واجب نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ سجدے سے پہلے کے کلمے مثلا اللہ کو پڑھے یا سجدے سے بعد کے کلمے مثلا, مافی السموات، کو پڑھے تب سجدہ لازم ہوگا ، اور ایسا سمجھا جائے گا آیت سجدہ کی پوری آیت کو پڑھی۔
ترجمه (۷۵۶) اور سجدہ کی چودہ آیتیں مندرجہ ذیل سورتوں میں ہیں: [1] سورہ اعراف [۲] رعد [۳) محل [۴] بنی اسرائیل [۵] مریم [1] سورہ حج کا پہلا سجدہ [1] فرقان [۸] نمل [9] سجدۂ [۱۰] ص ۱۱ حم سجده [۱۲] نجم [۱۳] انشقت [۱۴] اقراء تشریح : ان چودہ سورتوں میں آیت سجدہ ہے، اور اس کی تفصیل پہلی ایک نظر میں گزر چکی ہے۔
Chapter of Prostration of Recitation. (752) Its cause is recitation upon the reciter and the listener in the correct view. (753) It is obligatory with respite if not in prayer, and its delay is disliked as tanzih. (754) It is obligatory upon the one who recites a verse even if in Persian. (755) Reading a letter of the prostration verse with a word before or after it from the verse is like the entire verse in the correct view. (756) Its verses are fourteen verses in al-A'raf, ar-Ra'd, an-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, the first of al-Hajj, al-Furqan, an-Naml, as-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim as-Sajdah, an-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and Iqra'. … Translation: (752) The cause of prostration is recitation, upon the listener and the reciter according to the madhhab. Proof: (1) The evidence for obligation is this hadith: from Ibn Umar: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to recite a sajdah verse while we were with him and he would prostrate and we would prostrate with him until some of us could not find a place to put his forehead. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith shows that prostration is obligatory upon the reciter and listeners. (2) From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet prostrated at [Surah] an-Najm and the Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans prostrated with him. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith proves that when a sajdah verse is recited, one should prostrate, and those who hear should also prostrate. (3) The saying of a Tabi'i supports this: From Ibn Umar: Verily the sajdah is upon whoever hears it. (4) From Ibrahim, Nafi', and Sa'id ibn Jubayr: Whoever hears a sajdah verse must prostrate. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This athar shows that whoever hears a sajdah verse must prostrate, whether he intended to listen or not. Translation: (753) If one is not in prayer, it is obligatory with respite. However, delaying it is makruh tanzihi. Explanation: If one is not in prayer, then at the moment of hearing, it is not necessary to perform the prostration immediately; rather, one can do it later. However, delaying without excuse is makruh tanzihi because it is not good to delay worship without need. Proof: From al-Mughirah ibn al-Hakim: I was with Ibn Umar when a reciter recited a sajdah after Fajr. Ibn Umar shouted at him; the reciter prostrated but Ibn Umar did not. When the sun rose, Ibn Umar made up the sajdah saying 'I will prostrate for it.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq) This action of a companion shows that one can make it up later. Translation: (754) The one who recited a verse is also required to prostrate, even if he recited in Persian. Explanation: The hadith already passed that prostration is obligatory upon the reciter; likewise if he recites in Persian, it is still obligatory. Translation: (755) Reading one letter of the sajdah verse along with a word before or after it is like the full verse according to the correct narration. Explanation: 'Harful sajdah' means the complete word that contains the prostration word or indicates prostration, e.g., 'yasjudu' in 'wa lillahi yasjudu ma fi as-samawati'. The meaning is that reading only the word of prostration alone does not obligate prostration; rather, one must read a preceding word like 'Allah' or a following word like 'ma fi as-samawati' to obligate prostration, and this is considered as reciting the full verse. Translation: (756) And the verses of prostration are fourteen in the following surahs: [1] al-A'raf, [2] ar-Ra'd, [3] an-Nahl, [4] Bani Isra'il, [5] Maryam, [1] the first of al-Hajj, [1] al-Furqan, [8] an-Naml, [9] as-Sajdah, [10] Sad, [11] Ha Mim as-Sajdah, [12] an-Najm, [13] al-Inshiqaq, [14] Iqra'. Explanation: In these fourteen surahs there is a sajdah verse, and its detail has already passed in one glance.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Sajdah al-Tilawah (prostration of recitation) and presents the core rulings of the Hanafi school on this topic. It begins by stating the cause of the prostration: recitation of a sajdah verse. According to the correct position of the madhhab, it is obligatory (wajib) upon both the reciter and the listener. The author then lists the proofs: hadith from Ibn Umar showing the Prophet and companions prostrated during his recitation, indicating obligation; hadith from Ibn Abbas showing prostration at Surah an-Najm with a large group including non-Muslims; and athar from Ibn Umar and other tabi'un affirming obligation on the listener. The ruling is that it is wajib on respite (mutlaq) when not in prayer—that is, it can be delayed, though delaying unnecessarily is makruh tanzihi. The author proves this with the action of Ibn Umar who made up a sajdah after sunrise. Next, the ruling applies even if the recitation is in Persian (or any non-Arabic language), as the obligation is based on reciting the meaning. Then, a detail: if one recites only a part of the verse that includes the word of prostration along with a word before or after, it is considered like reciting the full verse in the correct view. Finally, the number of sajdah verses is fourteen, listed in specific surahs: al-A'raf, ar-Ra'd, an-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, al-Hajj (first), al-Furqan, an-Naml, as-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim as-Sajdah, an-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-Alaq (Iqra'). This matches the standard Hanafi list. The commentary emphasizes that the obligation is established by strong hadith evidence, and the rulings apply to both reciter and listener without distinction of language or specific phrase.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran containing a command or indication of prostration.
التراخي (al-tarākhī): The obligation is with respite, meaning it can be performed at a later time and not immediately upon hearing/recitation outside prayer.
حرف السجدة (ḥarf al-sajdah): The specific word or phrase in the sajdah verse that indicates prostration, e.g., 'yasjudu' or 'kharra sajidan'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on Sajdah al-Tilawah for a person who hears a sajdah verse outside prayer?
A) Must prostrate immediately.
B) Must prostrate but may delay (wajib with respite).
C) It is sunnah, not required.
D) Not required at all.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Tilawah is wajib on reciter and listener alike, with the flexibility of delay outside prayer.

Salah — Prayer

Further Rulings of Sajdah al-Tilawah: Language, Partial Recitation, and Number of Verses
Additional rulings: language, partial recitation, and list of verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the obligation of sajdah when reciting in Persian, define 'harf al-sajdah' and the rule for partial recitation, and list the 14 sajdah verses.

Core Idea
Sajdah is obligatory even in non-Arabic; reciting a part of a sajdah verse with an adjacent word suffices; there are exactly 14 sajdah verses.

This lesson covers three specific rulings: the obligation of sajdah when reciting in Persian, the rule that reciting only the prostration word with a preceding or following word counts as the full verse, and the enumeration of the 14 sajdah verses. These details help ensure proper practice of this obligatory act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the language ruling
The obligation applies regardless of language. The text says 'even if in Persian', meaning any language triggers wajib.
This is based on the general principle that the obligation is on the meaning, not the specific Arabic wording.
2
Analyze the 'harf al-sajdah' ruling
Reciting only the specific prostration word (e.g., 'yasjudu') alone does not obligate sajdah; it must be with an adjacent word from the same verse. The text says: 'reading a letter of the prostration verse with a word before or after it from the verse is like the entire verse'.
This is the correct view in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the rule for partial recitation
If someone recites 'yasjudu' alone, no sajdah is required. If they recite 'wa lillahi yasjudu' (a preceding word with the prostration word), it is sufficient to obligate sajdah.
The 'harf al-sajdah' is the word indicating prostration; an adjacent word makes it a meaningful phrase.
4
List the 14 verses
Memorize the surah names provided in the text: al-A'raf, ar-Ra'd, an-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, first in al-Hajj, al-Furqan, an-Naml, as-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim as-Sajdah, an-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and Iqra' (al-Alaq).
In the Hanafi school, there are exactly 14; other schools differ.

باب سجود التلاوة (۷۵۲) سببه التلاوة على التالى والسامع في الصحيح (۷۵۳) وهو واجب على التراخي ان لم يكن في الصلوة وكره تاخيره تنزيها (۷۵۴) ويجب على من تلا آية ولو بالفارسية. (۷۵۵) وقراءة حرف السجدة مع كلمة قبله او بعده من آيتها كالآية في الصحيح . (۷۵۶) و آياتها اربع عشرة آية في الاعراف والرعد والنحل والاسراء ومريم واولى الحج والفرقان والنمل والسجدة وص وحم السجدة والنجم وانشقت واقرأ.

وجه :(۱) واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقرأ السجدة ونحن عنده فيسجد ونسجد معه فنزدحم حتى مايجد احدنا لجبهته موضعا يسجد عليه ( بخاری شریف، باب ازدحام الناس اذ اقرا الامام السجدۃ، ص ۱۴۶، نمبر ۹۷۶ ارباب ما جاء في سجود القرآن رمسلم شریف، باب سجود التلاوۃ ص ۲۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۹۵/۵۷۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ سجدہ واجب ہے پڑھنے والے پر اور سننے والوں پر بھی ۔ (۲) عن ابن عباس ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سجد بالنجم وسجد معه المسلمون والمشركون والجن والانس ( بخاری شریف، باب سجدة النجم ص ۱۴۶، نمبر ۷ ۱۰ار مسلم شریف ، باب سجود التلاوۃ ص ۲۱۵ نمبر ۱۲۹۷/۵۷۶) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ آیت سجدہ پڑھنے سے سجدہ کرنا چاہئے ۔ اور جو لوگ سنے ان کو بھی سجدہ کرنا چاہیئے (۳) اس قول تابعی سے اس کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال انما السجدة على من سمعها. (نمبر ۴۲۲۵) (۴) عن ابراهيم ، و نافع و سعيد بن جبير قالوا : من سمع السجدة فعليه ان يسجد ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۰۷ ، باب من قال السجدة على من جلس لھا و من سمعھا ، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۷، نمبر (۴۲۲۲ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو بھی آیت سجدہ سنے گا اس پر سجدہ کرنا واجب ہوگا چاہے سننے کا ارادہ کرے یا نہ کریا۔

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Sajdah al-Tilawah (prostration of recitation) and presents the core rulings of the Hanafi school on this topic. It begins by stating the cause of the prostration: recitation of a sajdah verse. According to the correct position of the madhhab, it is obligatory (wajib) upon both the reciter and the listener. The author then lists the proofs: hadith from Ibn Umar showing the Prophet and companions prostrated during his recitation, indicating obligation; hadith from Ibn Abbas showing prostration at Surah an-Najm with a large group including non-Muslims; and athar from Ibn Umar and other tabi'un affirming obligation on the listener. The ruling is that it is wajib on respite (mutlaq) when not in prayer—that is, it can be delayed, though delaying unnecessarily is makruh tanzihi. The author proves this with the action of Ibn Umar who made up a sajdah after sunrise. Next, the ruling applies even if the recitation is in Persian (or any non-Arabic language), as the obligation is based on reciting the meaning. Then, a detail: if one recites only a part of the verse that includes the word of prostration along with a word before or after, it is considered like reciting the full verse in the correct view. Finally, the number of sajdah verses is fourteen, listed in specific surahs: al-A'raf, ar-Ra'd, an-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, al-Hajj (first), al-Furqan, an-Naml, as-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim as-Sajdah, an-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-Alaq (Iqra'). This matches the standard Hanafi list. The commentary emphasizes that the obligation is established by strong hadith evidence, and the rulings apply to both reciter and listener without distinction of language or specific phrase.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran containing a command or indication of prostration.
التراخي (al-tarākhī): The obligation is with respite, meaning it can be performed at a later time and not immediately upon hearing/recitation outside prayer.
حرف السجدة (ḥarf al-sajdah): The specific word or phrase in the sajdah verse that indicates prostration, e.g., 'yasjudu' or 'kharra sajidan'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 13
C) 14
D) 15

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Tilawah is obligatory upon reciting a sajdah verse in any language, and reciting only the prostration word alone does not obligate it.

The Ruling on Delaying Sajdah al-Tilawah
Ruling on delaying prostration of recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Sajdah al-Tilawah and identify the proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Delaying sajdah al-tilawah is permissible but disliked; the obligation remains until performed.

This lesson examines the Hanafi perspective on the timing of Sajdah al-Tilawah. While the prostration is obligatory immediately during prayer, outside of prayer a delay is allowed but considered slightly disliked (makruh tanzihan). The evidence from the practice of Ibn Umar clarifies how the Companions understood this obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
First, note that sajdah al-tilawah is wajib upon the reciter and listener. If one is not in prayer, they may delay it, but this delay is makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked).
2
Locate the evidence
The author cites a narration from Mughirah ibn al-Hakim: Ibn Umar was with a reciter who prostrated after Fajr; Ibn Umar shouted but did not prostrate immediately, then made it up later. This shows delay is permissible.
Reference: Musannaf Abdurrazzaq
3
Analyze the evidence
Ibn Umar's initial objection indicates disapproval of the reciter's timing, while his own delay and later performance demonstrate that immediate performance is not obligatory. The obligation was fulfilled later.
The karahah is derived from his objection.
4
Understand the classification
Why is it karahah tanzihiyah? Because the act is valid but delaying without a valid reason is less preferred. The obligation is not nullified by delay.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school holds it as wajib; the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. This affects whether delay with dislike applies or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود التلاوة. ويجب السجود على من سمع وتلى. وإن لم يكن في الصلاة فله التأخير مع الكراهة. وكره تاخيره تنزیها. وجه: عن المغيرة بن الحكيم قال كنت مع ابن عمر فقرا قاص بسجدة بعد الصبح فصاح عليه ابن عمر فسجد القاص و لم يسجد ابن عمر فلما طلعت الشمس قضاها ابن عمر يقول سجدها ۔ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب هل تقضى السجدة ؟ ج ثالث ص ۲۱۱، نمبر ۵۹۵۳)
Chapter of the prostration of recitation. And prostration is obligatory upon the one who hears and recites. And if he is not in prayer, he may delay it with dislike. And its delay is disliked as tanzih. Evidence: From Mughirah ibn al-Hakim: I was with Ibn Umar when a reciter recited a sajdah after Fajr; Ibn Umar shouted at him; the reciter prostrated but Ibn Umar did not; when the sun rose, Ibn Umar performed it saying he made it up.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: Sajdah al-tilawah is obligatory immediately upon hearing or reciting if one is in prayer; otherwise, it may be delayed. However, delaying without a valid reason is makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked). The proof is a narration from Ibn Umar who delayed his sajdah until after sunrise, indicating its permissibility but with disapproval. The Hanafi school emphasizes performing it promptly as a preferred act.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karahah tanzihiyah): A level of dislike that is not prohibitively disliked; avoiding it is better but doing it is not sinful.
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran known as ayah al-sajdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Obligation of Sajdah in Non-Arabic Recitation
Ruling on sajdah for non-Arabic recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah when the verse is recited in a non-Arabic language and explain the basis for this ruling.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib upon meaning, not language.

What happens if you recite an ayah al-sajdah in a language you understand, like English or Urdu? Does the obligation of sajdah still apply? This short but powerful ruling from the Hanafi school settles the matter: the obligation stands. Let's unpack the reasoning and see how it differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting an ayah al-sajdah. The ruling (hukm) is that sajdah al-tilawah becomes wajib upon the reciter.
Note: The ruling applies even if the recitation is not in Arabic, as per this text.
2
Understand the scope: does language matter?
The text explicitly says 'even if in Persian' (بالفارسية). This indicates that the obligation is not tied to the Arabic wording but to the act of reciting the verse itself.
Other schools may disagree, as noted in the dispute map.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The Hanafi proof is from the general hadith commanding sajdah upon reciting a verse of sajdah, without restricting to Arabic. The principle is: the command attaches to the meaning (ma'na) rather than the specific wording (lafz).
This is a classic Hanafi usul position.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that sajdah is only for Arabic recitation since the Quran is defined by its Arabic form. The Hanafi tarjih relies on the broader evidence.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis will perform sajdah when reciting translations; others may not consider it obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۵٤) ويجب على من تلا آية ولو بالفارسية.
(754) And it is obligatory upon the one who recites a verse even if in Persian.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This ruling states that reciting an ayah al-sajdah in Persian (or any non-Arabic translation) still obligates the sajdah. The proof is the general hadith that sajdah is on the reciter. The Hanafi school holds that the obligation is due to the meaning, not the specific Arabic wording, so translation does not lift the obligation.

Key Terms
بالفارسية (bil-farisiya): In the Persian language, indicating any non-Arabic translation of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah.
C) It is not required because Persian is not Arabic.
D) It is haram to recite in Persian.

Key Takeaway
Reciting an ayah al-sajdah in any language triggers the wajib of sajdah al-tilawah in the Hanafi school.

Reciting Part of a Sajdah Verse to Obligate Prostration
Ruling with condition for sajdah al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum recitation that obligates sajdah al-tilawah.

Core Idea
Reciting the sajdah word with an adjacent word from its verse counts as the full verse, making prostration wajib.

When you recite a verse of sajdah during prayer or otherwise, you might wonder if saying just the word 'yasjudu' is enough. The Hanafi school clarifies that you need a bit more context: the sajdah word together with a word before or after it from the same verse. This lesson explains that ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is reciting a portion of a Quranic verse that contains a word indicating sajdah (like 'yasjudu').
2
Determine the ruling
If the recitation includes the sajdah word AND at least one adjacent word (previous or next) from the same verse, then sajdah al-tilawah becomes wajib.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the condition
The condition for obligation is that the recited portion must include the sajdah word plus a connecting word from the verse. Reciting only the sajdah word alone does not obligate sajdah.
The phrase 'كلمة قبله او بعده' indicates any single word from the verse before or after the sajdah word.
4
Recognize the equivalence
Such partial recitation is treated like reciting the full verse (كالآية) for the purpose of wajib sajdah.
5
Note the school's authority
This is the sahih (correct) position in the Hanafi school, as stated in Zahir al-Riwayah.
Other schools may require the full verse; this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۵۵) وقراءة حرف السجدة مع كلمة قبله او بعده من آيتها كالآية في الصحيح.
(755) And reciting the letter of prostration along with a word before it or after it from its verse is like the verse in the correct opinion.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage clarifies that merely reciting the word containing the sajdah (such as 'yasjudu') is not enough to obligate sajdah. One must recite either the preceding word (e.g., 'lillahi') or the following word (e.g., 'ma fis-samawati') so that the recited portion is considered the verse as a whole. The correct position in the school is that such partial recitation suffices to make sajdah wajib.

Key Terms
حرف السجدة (harf al-sajdah): The specific word in the verse that indicates prostration, e.g., 'yasjudu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Reciting the sajdah word with a word before or after it from the same verse.
C) Reciting the entire ayah from beginning to end.
D) Reciting any part of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Reciting the sajdah word with an adjacent word from its verse triggers the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah in the Hanafi school.

The Fourteen Verses of Sajdah in Hanafi Fiqh
Enumeration of fourteen ayas of sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourteen verses of sajdah according to the Hanafi school and explain the reconciliation of the fifteen-sajdah hadith.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school counts fourteen wajib sajdahs; the hadith of fifteen is reconciled by counting one sajdah in Surah al-Hajj.

This passage enumerates the fourteen verses where prostration is wajib. Although a hadith reports fifteen, the Hanafi school follows the practice of the Companions and counts only one sajdah in Surah al-Hajj. Mastering this list is essential for anyone leading prayer or teaching others.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the list of surahs
Learn the fourteen surahs that contain ayah as-sajdah: al-A'raf (7:206), al-Ra'd (13:15), al-Nahl (16:49), al-Isra' (17:107), Maryam (19:58), al-Hajj (22:18), al-Furqan (25:60), al-Naml (27:25), al-Sajdah (32:15), Sad (38:24), Fussilat (41:37), al-Najm (53:62), al-Inshiqaq (84:21), and Iqra' (96:19).
2
Understand the evidence
The hadith from Amr ibn al-As (Abu Dawud) states fifteen sajdahs. Identify the hadith and its content.
The hadith is ahad and zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets 'two sajdahs in Surah al-Hajj' as referring to a difference of opinion among Companions. The relied-upon view among the Hanafis is that there is only one sajdah in al-Hajj, making the total fourteen.
The tarjih is based on the practice of most Companions and consistency in the list.
4
Compare with other schools
Note that the Shafi'i school counts fifteen sajdahs, including two in al-Hajj. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
Both positions have textual evidence; the difference arises from differing interpretations of the same hadith.
5
Apply in practice
When reciting the Quran, know which verses require sajdah. Prostration is wajib upon reciting or hearing these specific verses.
Sajdah tilawah is performed immediately or may be delayed if needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۵۶) و آياتها اربع عشرة آية في الاعراف والرعد والنحل والاسراء ومريم واولى الحج والفرقان والنمل والسجدة وص وحم السجدة والنجم وانشقت واقرأ. عن عمرو بن العاص أن النبي صلى الله عليه أقرأه خمس عشرة سجدة في القرآن، منها ثلاث في المفصل، و في سورة الحج سجدتان. (ابوداود شریف، باب تفريح ابواب السجو دو كم سجدة في القرآن ؟ ، ص ۲۱۰، نمبر ۱ ۱۴۰)۔
(756) And its verses are fourteen verses: in al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, al-Isra', Maryam, the first of al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Sajdah, Sad, Ha Mim al-Sajdah, al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and Iqra'. From Amr ibn al-As that the Prophet recited to him fifteen sajdahs in the Quran, among them three in al-Mufassal, and in Surah al-Hajj two sajdahs. (Abu Dawud, chapter on number of sajdahs, p. 210, no. 140).
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
The Hanafi school specifies fourteen ayas of sajdah. The hadith mentions fifteen, but the Hanafi position is that Surah al-Hajj contains only one sajdah according to the majority of companions and scholars. Thus, the total is fourteen. The list includes surahs from al-A'raf to al-'Alaq (Iqra'). This is a memorization anchor for the student.

Key Terms
آية السجدة (ayat al-sajdah): A Quranic verse that contains a command or indication to prostrate.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed when reciting or hearing a verse of sajdah.

Obligation of Sajdah on the Listener
Ruling with proof on listener's sajdah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah for the listener, identify the exception for menstruating and postpartum women, and cite the primary evidence from the Prophet's practice and the statements of Ibn Umar and Ibrahim.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib on the listener, even unintentional, except for ha'id and nufasa'.

This passage expands the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah beyond the reciter to include anyone who hears the ayah, regardless of intent. It then introduces an important exception: women in menstruation or postpartum bleeding are exempt, drawing on a stronger analogy with the greater obligation of prayer. The proofs ground the ruling in prophetic practice and early scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Exception
Read the first line: 'Sajdah is obligatory on the one who hears, even if he did not intend to hear, except for ha'id and nufasa'.' Note that the ruling has two parts: general obligation and specific exemption.
The exception is absolute, not conditional on missing conditions.
2
Analyze the First Proof: Prophetic Practice
Examine the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet prostrated at Surah al-Najm and all present, including polytheists and jinn, prostrated. This shows that even non-Muslims and unintended listeners performed sajdah, indicating intention is not required.
The hadith demonstrates the universal scope of the obligation at the moment of recitation.
3
Analyze the Second Proof: Sahabi Statement
Ibn Umar said 'Indeed the sajdah is upon the one who hears it.' This explicit statement from a Companion directly supports the ruling and is considered a strong proof in Hanafi usul.
Such a qawl sahabi, when not contradicted, is a legitimate source according to Abu Hanifa.
4
Understand the Exception via Tabi'i Reasoning
Ibrahim's statement: a menstruating woman who hears sajdah should not prostrate because she leaves what is greater: the obligatory prayer. This indicates a qiyas: if she is excused from the greater obligation (salah) due to impurity, she is likewise excused from the lesser obligation (sajdah).
This reasoning shows the Hanafi method of extending exemptions from greater to lesser acts.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Nuance
While the Hanafi school holds sajdah as wajib on the listener, other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider it sunnah or require intention. Recognize that the proofs used here establish the distinct Hanafi position.
The difference affects whether one must repeat a missed sajdah or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۵۷) ويجب السجود على من سمع وان لم يقصد السماع الا حائض والنفساء. وجه: عن ابن عباس ان النبي سجد بالنجم و سجد معه المسلمون و المشركون و الجن والانس. (بخاري شریف، باب سجود المسلمين مع المشركين، ص ۱۷۳، نمبر ۱۰۷۱). وعن ابن عمر قال انما السجدة على من سمعها. (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة، ج اول، ص ۱۳۶۷ نمبر ۴۲۲۵). وعن ابراهيم انه كان يقول في الحائض تسمع السجدة قال : لا تسجد، هي تدع أعظم من السجدة : الصلوة المكتوبة (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة، ج اول ص ۱۳۷۵، نمبر ۴۳۱۵).
(757) And prostration is obligatory upon the one who hears even if he did not intend to hear, except for a menstruating woman and a woman in postpartum bleeding. Evidence: From Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prostrated at Surah al-Najm, and the Muslims, polytheists, jinn, and humans prostrated with him. From Ibn Umar: 'Indeed the sajdah is upon the one who hears it.' From Ibrahim that he used to say about a menstruating woman who hears the sajdah: 'She does not prostrate; she leaves what is greater than sajdah: the obligatory prayer.'
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This ruling extends the obligation of sajdah to anyone who hears the verse, whether intentionally or accidentally. The proof is that even polytheists prostrated when hearing the Prophet recite, indicating that intention is not a condition. However, women in menstruation (haid) or postpartum (nifas) are exempt because they are not in a state of ritual purity required for the sajdah. The tabi‘i Ibrahim emphasizes that they are already excused from the greater obligation of prayer, so sajdah is not required.

Key Terms
حائض (ha'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding, who is exempt from sajdah al-tilawah.
نفساء (nufasa'): A woman experiencing postpartum bleeding, similarly exempt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah is wajib on any hearer of a sajdah verse, with the sole exception of women in haid or nifas, based on prophetic practice, Companion statement, and analogical reasoning.

Imam and Muqtadi Hearing External Sajdah During Prayer
Ruling with proof from a tabi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when an imam or muqtadi hears an external sajdah recitation during prayer and explain why prostrating during prayer is insufficient.

Core Idea
External sajdah heard during prayer requires sajdah after the prayer, not during.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in salah: an imam or follower hears an ayah al-sajdah being recited by someone outside the prayer. Should they interrupt their prayer to prostrate? The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling: they must prostrate after completing the prayer. Prostrating during the prayer does not fulfill the obligation but also does not break the prayer. The proof comes from the practice of the tabi'i Ta'us.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hearing an ayah al-sajdah from an external source while engaged in salah. The ruling: the imam and muqtadi must perform the sajdah after completing the prayer.
The ruling applies to both imam and follower.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the statement of Ta'us: 'He does not prostrate' during the prayer. This is a qawl sahabi (saying of a Companion's successor) found in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
The dalil is zanni in thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Ta'us explicitly prohibits prostrating during prayer for someone who hears the sajdah from an external source. This indicates the sajdah should be postponed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) allow prostrating immediately during prayer if the recitation is from someone outside. The Hanafi school, however, holds that it must be after.
The Hanafi position is based on the principle that actions not part of the prayer are prohibited during it unless required.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is considered wajib to follow.
The proof from Ta'us, a known authority, is deemed sufficient for the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۵۸) والامام والمقتدى به ولو سمعوها من غيره سجدوا بعد الصلوة ولو سجدو فيها لم تجزهم ولم تفسد. وجه: عن طاؤس في الرجل سمع السجدة وهو في الصلوة قال لا يسجد. (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۲۱۶).
(758) And the imam and the one being led (muqtadi) - if they hear it from other than him - they prostrate after the prayer; and if they prostrate during it, it does not suffice for them and does not invalidate (the prayer). Evidence: From Ta'us concerning a man who hears the sajdah while in prayer: he said, 'He does not prostrate.'
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This ruling addresses a scenario where an imam or muqtadi hears an ayah al-sajdah from someone outside the prayer (e.g., from a different reciter) while they are engaged in salah. They should not prostrate during the prayer; rather, they must perform the sajdah after completing the salah. If they mistakenly prostrate during the prayer, it does not fulfill the obligation (so they must repeat the sajdah after salah), but it does not invalidate the prayer. The proof is the statement of Ta'us, a tabi'i, who advised against prostrating during prayer in such a case.

Key Terms
مقتدى (muqtadi): The person praying behind the imam (follower).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Obligation of Sujud al-Tilawah for the Listener
Ruling with proof on sujud al-tilawah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujud al-tilawah for the listener and identify the exceptions from the text.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajdah verse obligates prostration, even without intent, except for those in menstrual or postpartum bleeding.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text clarifies the ruling on sujud al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). It establishes that the obligation falls upon anyone who hears a verse of prostration, regardless of their intention to listen, and then provides proofs from hadith and athar. The text also addresses exceptions: women in menstruation (ḥāʾiḍ) and postpartum bleeding (nafas) are exempt, and the imam and follower who hear a sajdah from someone else during prayer must prostrate after the prayer, not during it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The matn states that sujud is obligatory upon the one who hears a sajdah verse (sujud al-tilawah).
The ruling is wajib, not fard, as the evidence is from ahad hadith.
2
Note the condition of intent
The obligation applies even if the listener did not intend to hear the verse. This is proven by the hadith of Ibn Abbas where polytheists prostrated despite not intending to listen.
3
Identify the exceptions
The menstruating woman (ḥāʾiḍ) and postpartum woman (nafas) are exempt from sujud al-tilawah, as they are not in a state of ritual purity required for prostration.
This is supported by the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
4
Understand the ruling for the imam and follower
If the imam or follower hears a sajdah from someone else (not the imam), they must prostrate after the prayer. Prostrating during the prayer does not suffice and does not invalidate the prayer.
This shows that sujud al-tilawah is a separate act that must be performed outside the prayer if heard during it.
5
Review the proofs
The passage cites proofs: the hadith of Amr ibn al-As enumerating sajdahs, the hadith of Ibn Abbas on prostration with polytheists, and athar from Ibn Umar and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
The hadith of Amr ibn al-As is used to count sajdahs, while the other proofs establish obligation upon hearing without intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود التلاوة (۷۵۷) ويجب السجود على من سمع وان لم يقصد السماع الا حائض والنفساء (۷۵۸) والامام والمقتدى به ولـو سـمـعـوهـا من غيره سجدوا بعد الصلوة ولو سجدو فيها لم تجزهم ولم تفسد وجه : (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قرآن کریم میں پندرہ سجدے ہیں ، حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عمر وبن العاص أن النبي علي صلى الله أقرأه خمس عشرة سجدة في القرآن ، منها ثلاث في المفصل ، و في سورة الحج سجدتان . (ابوداود شریف، باب تفريح ابواب السجو دو کم سجدة في القرآن ؟ ، ص ۲۱۰، نمبر ۱ ۱۴۰ رابن ماجه ، باب عدد سجود القرآن ، ص ۱۴۸، نمبر ۱۰۵۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قرآن کریم میں پندرہ سجدے ہیں، البتہ ہمارے یہاں سورہ حج میں ایک ہی سجدہ ہے اسلئے کل چودہ سجدے رہ گئے۔ ترجمه : ۷۵۷) جس نے سنی ہے اس پر سجدہ واجب ہوگا چاہے سننے کا ارادہ نہ کیا ہو۔ سواء حائضہ اور نفساء عورت کے۔ تشریح : جسنے آیت سجدہ سنی اس پر سجدہ واجب ہے چاہے سنے کی نیت سے سنی ہو چاہے اچانک سن لی ہو، البتہ حیض اور نفاس والی عورت پر پڑھنے یا سننے سے سجدہ نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ سجدہ کرنے کا اہل نہیں ہیں۔ صلى الله وجه (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبي له سـجـد بـالـنـجـم و سجد معه المسلمون و المشركون و الجن والانس - ( بخاری شریف، باب سجود المسلمين مع المشركين والمشرک نجس لیس لہ وضوء، ص ۱۷۳، نمبر ۱۰۷۱) اس حدیث میں مشرک نے بھی سجدہ کیا حالانکہ وہ سننے کی نیت نہیں رکھتے تھے، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ سننے کی نیت نہ بھی ہو تب بھی سجدہ واجب ہوگا ۔ (۲) عن ابن عمر قال انما السجدة على من سمعها. نمبر۴۲۲۵ (۴) عن ابراهیم ، و نافع و سعيد بن جبير قالوا : من سمع السجدة فعليه ان يسجد - (مصنف ابن ابى شيبة ، ۲۰۷ ، باب من قال السجدة على من جلس لھا و من سمعھا ، ج اول ، ص ۱۳۶۷ نمبر (۴۲۲۲ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو بھی آیت سجدہ سنے گا اس پر سجدہ کرنا واجب ہوگا چاہے سنے کا ارادہ کرے یا نہ کریا۔ (۳) اور حائضہ اور نفساء پر سجدہ نہیں ہے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن ابراهيم انه كان يقول في الحائض تسمع السجدة قال : لا تسجد ، هي تدع أعظم من السجدة : الصلوة المكتوبة ( مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب الحائض تسمع السجدة ، ج اول ص ۱۳۷۵، نمبر ۴۳۱۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حائضہ عورت نہ پڑھنے سے سجدہ کرے گی اور نہ سننے سے۔
Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah. (757) And sujud is obligatory upon one who hears even if he did not intend to hear, except the menstruating and postpartum woman. (758) And the imam and the follower; if they hear it from someone else, they prostrate after the prayer, and if they prostrate during it, it does not suffice them and does not invalidate. Proof: (1) This hadith states that in the Noble Quran there are fifteen prostrations...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins with the matn stating that sujud is wajib upon anyone who hears the verse of sajdah, even if they did not intend to hear it, except for a woman in menstruation (ha'id) and postpartum bleeding (nafas). The text then provides proofs: a hadith from Amr ibn al-As listing 15 sajdahs in the Quran, but in the Hanafi school there are 14, with only one in Surah al-Hajj. Another hadith from Ibn Abbas shows that the Prophet prostrated while reciting Surah Najm, and the polytheists prostrated too, indicating that intent is not required. Athar from Ibn Umar and Ibrahim al-Nakhai affirm that whoever hears must prostrate. For the exception, an athar from Ibrahim states that a menstruating woman should not prostrate because she is exempt from even the greatest act, the obligatory prayer.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran containing a sajdah.

D) An imam in prayer

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing a sajdah verse, even without intent, except for women in menstruation or postpartum bleeding.

Sujud al-Tilawah for Imam and Follower Hearing from Outside Prayer
Ruling on sujud al-tilawah for imam/follower hearing from outside prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of sujud al-tilawah for an imam or follower who hears a sajdah verse from outside the prayer, and apply the rule that performing sujud during prayer does not invalidate it.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah heard from outside is wajib after prayer; performing it during does not invalidate the prayer.

When an imam or follower hears a sajdah verse from a source outside their prayer, the Hanafi school prescribes that they delay the obligatory prostration until after completing the prayer. The text clarifies that if they prostrate during the prayer, it does not fulfill the obligation, but neither does it invalidate the prayer according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). This lesson unpacks the ruling and its evidence from the practices of early authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is sujud al-tilawah for imam/follower hearing a sajdah verse from outside. The ruling: wajib after prayer, not during.
The obligation of sujud remains, but its timing is delayed.
2
Locate the Dalil
Citing athar from Tawus (advising not to prostrate during prayer), Ibn Sirin (prostrate after finishing), and Ibrahim (permitting prostration during, indicating validity).
These reports are from the Musannaf of Ibn Abi Shaybah and Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The combination shows that prostration during prayer does not invalidate it; the preferred practice is to delay.
The Hanafi position harmonizes the reports by delaying sujud to after prayer.
4
Note the Zahir al-Riwayah Position
The apparent narration holds that if sujud is performed during prayer, the prayer remains valid though the sujud is not sufficient.
This is the authoritative position for fatwa.
5
Apply to Practical Scenario
If an imam in congregation hears a sajdah verse from a latecomer reciting, he should not prostrate immediately but wait until after salam.
This avoids mixing external acts with the obligatory prayer.

Source Text

If they prostrate during it, it is not sufficient, but in the apparent narration, the prayer does not become invalid. Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for an imam or a follower who hears a sajdah verse from someone else while they are in prayer. They must delay the sujud to after the prayer. If they perform sujud during the prayer, it does not count as the required sujud al-tilawah, but it does not invalidate the prayer according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). The proof includes an athar from Tawus advising not to prostrate during prayer, and from Ibn Sirin advising to prostrate after finishing, and from Ibrahim permitting prostration during prayer, which indicates the prayer remains valid.

Sujud al-Tilawah upon Hearing a Translation: The Hanafi Position
Ruling on hearing sajdah verse in translation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sujud al-tilawah when hearing a translation of a sajdah verse and apply the condition of understanding to determine obligation.

Core Idea
Sujud is wajib when you understand that what you heard is a sajdah verse, regardless of language.

This lesson addresses a common contemporary scenario: hearing a translation of a Quranic verse of prostration (ayat al-sajdah) in a language other than Arabic. Many Muslims today listen to Quran translations in Persian, Urdu, English, etc. The Hanafi school has addressed this issue, and this passage presents the relied-upon position (mu'tamad) that sujud al-tilawah becomes obligatory if the listener understands that the recited passage is a sajdah verse. The source also discusses a problematic aspect in modern times due to frequent broadcasts and recordings, and cites an athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab that one who did not intentionally sit to listen is not obligated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sujud al-tilawah upon hearing a translation. The ruling according to the mu'tamad is that it is wajib.
2
Locate the condition
The obligation is conditional upon the listener understanding that the recitation is a sajdah verse. Without this knowledge, sujud is not required.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is a principle: if one knows it is a sajdah verse, sujud becomes wajib. Additionally, an athar from Ibn al-Musayyab indicates that one who did not sit to listen is not obligated, implying obligation when one intentionally listens with understanding.
4
Note the contemporary application
The text acknowledges difficulties with modern media (radio, TV, internet) where sajdah verses are often heard unexpectedly. The mufta bihi remains, but caution may be exercised when the listener is uncertain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Sujud al-Tilawah When Hearing from a Sleeping or Insane Person
Dispute on obligation when hearing from a sleeping or insane person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ikhtilaf on sujud al-tilawah when hearing from a sleeping or insane person and identify the operative ruling.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is not wajib when hearing from a non-mukallaf; this is the majority Hanafi view.

This lesson addresses a specific question: if someone recites a sajdah verse while asleep or insane, does the listener owe sujud al-tilawah? The classical Hanafi texts record an ikhtilaf among the imams. We will map the positions and identify the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its normal ruling
Recall that sujud al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing or reciting a sajdah verse, provided the reciter is a mukallaf (sane adult Muslim).
Normal ruling: wajib when heard from a valid reciter.
2
State the point of disagreement
The disagreement is whether hearing from a non-mukallaf (sleeping or insane person) triggers the same obligation.
3
Present the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They hold that sujud is not wajib because the recitation of a non-mukallaf is not valid qira'ah that can cause obligation.
This is the majority position.
4
Present the position of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that sujud is wajib because the obligation is on the listener, independent of the reciter's state.
His reasoning: hearing the verse itself triggers the wajib.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: sujud is not wajib.
This is the view adopted in the later Hanafi works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۶۰) اور سونے والے اور دیوانے سے سننے پر واجب ہونے کی صحت میں اختلاف ہے۔ تشریح : سونے والے، یاد یوانے کی زبان سے آیت سجدہ سنی تو سجدہ واجب ہے یا نہیں اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔
Translation: (760) And regarding hearing from a sleeping person or an insane person, there is a difference of opinion on the correctness of its obligation. Commentary: If one hears a sajdah verse from a sleeping person or an insane person, there is disagreement on whether sujud is wajib.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage simply states that there is a difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) among Hanafi scholars on whether sujud al-tilawah becomes wajib if the reciter is asleep or insane. The text does not elaborate on the positions, so we cannot give a definitive ruling from this excerpt. The matter would be resolved by referring to the detailed works of the school.

Key Terms
اختلاف (ikhtilaf): Difference of opinion among Hanafi authorities on the ruling.
سجدہ تلاوت (sujud al-tilawah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a sajdah verse from the Quran.
واجب (wajib): An obligation that is established by a zanni (speculative) proof; omission is sinful but not as severe as fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school, is sujud al-tilawah wajib when hearing a sajdah verse from a sleeping person?
A) Yes, it is wajib
B) No, it is not wajib
C) It is haram
D) It is sunnah mu'akkadah

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi position is that sujud al-tilawah is not wajib when hearing from a sleeping or insane person.

Ruling on Sujud al-Tilawah from a Bird or Echo
Ruling on hearing sajdah from a bird or echo

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujud al-tilawah when hearing a sajdah verse from a bird or echo, and identify the condition that determines the obligation.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajdah verse from a bird or echo does not obligate sujud because it is not valid human recitation.

This lesson addresses a specific edge case in the rules of sujud al-tilawah. During prayer or outside, you may hear a sajdah verse recited by a bird that was taught it, or hear an echo of a human recitation. The Hanafi school clarifies that such hearing does not trigger the obligation of sujud. The key is that the recitation must come from a responsible human (mukallaf) for the sujud to be wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act is hearing a sajdah verse from a bird or an echo. This is a trigger for sujud al-tilawah. Identify the ruling: is sujud wajib or not?
The text explicitly says 'not wajib'.
2
Isolate the underlying condition
The obligation of sujud al-tilawah depends on the source of recitation. For sujud to be wajib, the recitation must be by a human who is mukallaf (responsible). A bird's imitation or an echo is not considered valid recitation.
The echo is not even a new recitation; it's a reflection.
3
Apply the condition to the cases
Apply the condition: bird and echo both fail the condition. Therefore, sujud is not wajib. This is a strict application of the Hanafi rule.
Some other schools may differ, but this is the Hanafi position.
4
Note the scope of the ruling
This ruling applies whether you are in salah or outside salah. Hearing a bird or echo does not interrupt your prayer or obligate sujud.

This passage clarifies that hearing a sajdah verse from a bird or as an echo does not impose the obligation of sujud al-tilawah. The reason is that these are not valid recitations by a responsible human. The bird's imitation is not considered proper recitation, and an echo is not a direct communication from a person.

Key Terms

Conditions for Sajdah Tilawah upon Hearing a Translation
Ruling on sajdah upon a translation with a condition and an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which sajdah tilawah becomes wajib upon hearing a translation of a verse of prostration in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sajdah tilawah is wajib upon hearing a translation only if the listener understands it as a verse of prostration.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation) when one hears a translation of a verse of prostration, such as in Persian or Urdu. The key condition is understanding that the recited passage is a verse of prostration. The commentary also introduces an exception based on an athar about intentional listening, which adds nuance to the general rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sajdah tilawah. The ruling in the Hanafi school is wajib (obligatory) when the conditions are met.
This is the mu'tamad (relied-upon) position.
2
Identify the condition for wajib
The condition is understanding (فهم) that the heard text is a verse of prostration. This applies whether the recitation is in Arabic or a translation.
The text explicitly says 'if he understands it' (ان فهمها).
3
Note the exception from the athar
The commentary cites an athar from Ibn al-Musayyab that sajdah is not required if one did not intentionally sit to listen. This suggests that intention to listen may be a prerequisite.
This exception is debated; the matn itself does not include it.
4
Recognize modern challenges
The commentary notes difficulties with electronic media broadcasting verses repeatedly. The ruling remains based on the condition of understanding, but the exception may be applied in cases of unintended hearing.
This is an area for ijtihad and fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۵۹) ويجب بسماع الفارسية ان فهمها على المعتمد
ترجمه : (۷۵۹) اور فارسی زبان میں سننے والے پر اگر اس کو سمجھیں تو معتمد روایت پر سجدہ واجب ہے۔ تشریح : آیت سجدہ کا مفہوم فارسی زبان میں یا کسی اور زبان میں سمجھ میں آگیا کہ آیت سجدہ ہے تو معتمد قوی یہ ہے کہ سجدہ تلاوت لازم ہوگا۔ وجه : (۱) یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ کسی طرح یہ سمجھ میں آجائے کہ یہ آیت سجدہ ہے تو سجدہ لازم ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن اس میں اس دور میں پریشانی یہ ہے کہ ریڈیو، ٹیلی وژن ، انٹرنیٹ اور ٹیپ رکارڈ پر بار بار بے وقت بھی آیت سجدہ سنائی دیتی ہے، اب اس پر سجدہ واجب کریں تو لوگ پریشان ہوتے ہیں اس لئے یہ مسئلہ قابل غور ہے، خصوصا جبکہ اس طرح کا ثبوت حدیث ، قرآن ، اور قول صحابی یا قول تابعی سے نہ ہو۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ جو آیت سننے کے لئے نہ بیٹھا ہو اور اچانک سن لیا تو اس پر سجدہ نہیں ہے . عن المسيب ان عثمان مر بقاص فقرأ سجدة ليسجد معه عثمان فقال عثمان انما السجود على من استمع ثم مضى و لم يسجد . قال الزهرى و قد كان ابن المسيب يجلس في ناحية المسجد و يقرأ القاص السجدة فلا يسجد معه ، و يقول اني لم اجلس لها ـ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب السجدة على من سمعھا ، ج ثالث ، ص ۲۰۶، نمبر ۵۹۲۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جو سننے کے لئے نہ بیٹھا ہو اس پر سجدہ نہیں ہے۔
(759) And it becomes obligatory by hearing the Persian (translation) if he understands it, according to the relied-upon (view). Translation: (759) And upon the one who hears in Persian, if he understands it, sajdah is wajib according to the relied-upon narration. Explanation: If the meaning of the verse of prostration in Persian or another language is understood that it is a verse of prostration, then the stronger relied-upon view is that sajdah tilawah becomes necessary. Reason: (1) This issue is based on the principle that however one comes to understand that this is a verse of prostration, sajdah becomes obligatory. But in this era, there is difficulty because radio, television, internet, and tape recorders repeatedly broadcast verses of prostration at inappropriate times. If we hold sajdah obligatory in all such cases, people would be troubled, so this issue is worth considering, especially since there is no such textual evidence from hadith, Qur'an, or saying of a companion or follower that specifically addresses this. (2) There is a saying of a follower that one who did not sit to listen [to the verse] but heard it suddenly, sajdah is not obligatory upon him. From al-Musayyab that 'Uthman passed by a storyteller who recited a verse of prostration for 'Uthman to prostrate with him, but 'Uthman said: 'Sajdah is only upon the one who listens [by intention],' then he went on and did not prostrate. Al-Zuhri said: Ibn al-Musayyab used to sit in a corner of the mosque and the storyteller would recite a verse of prostration, but Ibn al-Musayyab would not prostrate with him, saying: 'I did not sit for it.' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-Sajdah 'ala man sami'aha, vol. 3, p. 206, no. 5925) This effect indicates that one who did not sit to listen is not required to prostrate.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation) when hearing a translation of a verse of prostration in Persian or another language. The author, Thamaratun Najah, states that if the listener understands that it is a verse of prostration, sajdah becomes wajib according to the relied-upon (mu'tamad) position. This is based on the principle that comprehension of the meaning triggers the obligation, as the purpose of hearing is understanding. The Urdu commentary elaborates on the modern problem of repeated hearing through electronic media and notes that there is no explicit textual evidence from primary sources for this scenario. It also cites an athar from Ibn al-Musayyab that if one did not intentionally sit to listen, sajdah is not required. This suggests a possible exception, though the matn itself is unconditional. The lesson type is a ruling statement with commentary expanding on its application.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Qur'an.
المعتمد (al-mu'tamad): The relied-upon position within the Hanafi school, upon which fatwa is given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Sajdah upon Hearing from a Sleeping or Insane Person: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sajdah tilawah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the existence of disagreement within the Hanafi school on the obligation of sajdah tilawah when the reciter is asleep or insane and explain the practical consequence of this ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajdah verse from a sleeping or insane person triggers ikhtilaf among Hanafis — no single ruling.

This lesson examines a brief but significant passage from a Hanafi matn that records an intra-madhhab dispute. The issue: if you hear a verse of prostration (āyat sajdah) recited by someone who is asleep or insane, is the sajdah tilawah obligatory upon you? The matn does not resolve the dispute; it simply reports that scholars differed. Understanding why such ikhtilaf arises and its practical effect is key to navigating Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? Sajdah tilawah upon hearing a verse. The ruling is disputed: some say wajib, others not.
This is not a settled ruling; the text only reports ikhtilaf.
2
Recognize the nature of the dispute
It is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: different Hanafi scholars hold different views.
The passage uses 'ikhtilāf al-taṣḥīḥ' to indicate disagreement on the correct position.
3
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence for the listener: whether to perform sajdah or not when hearing from a sleeping/insane person.
This affects daily practice, especially in congregational settings.
4
Note the absence of tarjih
The text does not prefer one view; this is left unresolved.
A mufti must refer to larger fiqh works for a preferred position.

Source Text

Translation: (760) And there is difference regarding the validity of its obligation when hearing from a sleeping or insane person. Explanation: If one hears a verse of prostration from the tongue of a sleeping or insane person, is sajdah obligatory or not? There is disagreement about this.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage identifies a point of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school regarding sajdah tilawah when the reciter is asleep or insane. The matn states that there is disagreement about the validity (or correctness) of obligating sajdah in such cases. The Urdu commentary clarifies that the dispute centers on whether hearing from such a person triggers the obligation. The text does not specify which view is preferred, leaving it as an area of scholarly difference. This is typical of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where later scholars may have differing positions based on the reliability of the recitation.

Key Terms
اختلاف التصحيح (ikhtilāf al-taṣḥīḥ): Disagreement in the correct (valid) position on a ruling.

The Ruling of Sajdah Tilawah from Bird or Echo
Ruling that sajdah tilawah is not wajib from bird or echo

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of sajdah tilawah obligation regarding the source of recitation and apply it to bird and echo cases.

Core Idea
A bird's recitation or echo does not obligate sajdah tilawah because they are not genuine human recitations.

In this lesson, we clarify a specific condition for sajdah tilawah: the recitation must come from a human. Hearing a verse of prostration from a bird or from an echo does not create the obligation to perform sajdah. The Urdu commentary explains the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Consider the act of hearing a verse of prostration (sajdah tilawah) from a source that is not a human, specifically a bird or an echo.
The source does not need to be a responsible human; any human recitation triggers obligation on the listener.
2
State the ruling
According to the text, sajdah tilawah is not wajib (obligatory) in such cases. The exact phrase: 'ولا يجب بسماعها من الطير والصدى'.
This is a clear ruling with no internal dispute mentioned.
3
Understand the reason
The commentary explains that these sounds are not 'in reality a verse of prostration' — a bird's recitation is not human, and an echo is not the original utterance. Therefore the condition of hearing a proper recitation is not met.
The key condition is that the recitation must originate from a human.
4
Distinguish from standard cases
Contrast this with hearing a verse directly from a human reciter: in that case, sajdah is wajib on the listener regardless of the reciter's age or status (as long as the recitation is clear).
This distinction helps solidify the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۶۱) ولا يجب بسماعها من الطير والصدى
ترجمه : (۷۶۱) اور پرندہ اور صدائے بازگشت سے سننے سے واجب نہیں۔ تشریح : پرندے کو آیت سجدہ سکھایا تھا، اس نے آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو اس سے سجدہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح کسی نے مسجد کے اندر آیت سجدہ پڑھی اور اس کی بازگشت سنی تو اس سے سجدہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ حقیقت میں آیت سجدہ نہیں۔ صدی: بازگشت۔
(761) And it is not obligatory to hear it from a bird and an echo. Translation: (761) And it is not obligatory upon hearing from a bird or an echo. Explanation: A bird was taught a verse of prostration; it recited the verse, then sajdah is not wajib from that. Similarly, someone recited a verse of prostration inside a mosque and its echo was heard, then sajdah is not wajib from that. Because this is in reality not a verse of prostration. Sada: echo.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This ruling clarifies that sajdah tilawah is not obligatory when the source of the recitation is a bird (parrot trained to recite) or an echo (the reflected sound of a human recitation). The reason given in the commentary is that these are not genuine recitations of the verse; a bird's sound is not considered a human recitation, and an echo is not the original utterance. Therefore, the condition of hearing a proper recitation from a responsible human is not fulfilled. This ruling is straightforward and is likely agreed upon in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الصدى (al-ṣadā): The echo returning from a valley or wall after recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, because the bird is not a human.
C) Yes, if it is a parrot and the words are clear.
D) No, because it is wajib only if the listener intends to listen.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah tilawah is not obligatory when the verse is heard from a bird or an echo, as these are not genuine human recitations.

Modes of Performing Sajdah Tilawah within Salah
Modes of performing sajdah tilawah within prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four methods of performing sajdah tilawah inside prayer and apply the condition of fawr al-tilawah to determine when a prayer's ruku or sujud suffices.

Core Idea
Sajdah tilawah inside prayer can be fulfilled by a separate sujud, separate ruku, or by the prayer's own ruku/sujud under strict conditions of recitation continuity.

This passage details the Hanafi ruling on how to perform sajdah tilawah when one recites a verse of prostration (ayat sajdah) during salah. The text presents four possible methods, two of which involve the prayer's own movements. The key condition is fawr al-tilawah – the recitation must not be interrupted by more than two verses. We will examine each method and the evidence from the sayings of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sajdah tilawah is wajib upon reciting/hearing a sajdah verse. Determine what options exist for performing it during prayer.
The passage focuses on performance inside prayer, not on the obligation itself.
2
List the four methods
Read the Urdu commentary and enumerate: (1) separate sujud, (2) separate ruku, (3) prayer's ruku with intention, (4) prayer's sujud without intention.
Method 1 is stated as best.
3
Apply the condition of fawr
For methods 3 and 4, the recitation must not be interrupted by more than two verses. Check whether the recitation after the sajdah verse is within this limit.
Interruption means reciting more than two ayahs, not a time gap.
4
Examine the proofs
Two statements from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i are cited: one commands separate sujud, the other allows using the prayer's ruku/sujud.
These are mursal hadith accepted by Hanafis.
5
Note the comparative ranking
Separate sujud is the best method; other methods are valid alternatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۶۲) وتؤدّى بركوع او سجود في الصلوة غير ركوع الصلوة وسجودها ويجزى عنها ركوع الصلوة ان نواها وسجودها وان لم ينوها اذا لم ينقطع فور التلاوة باكثرها من آيتين.
ترجمه : (۷۶۲ ) نماز میں جو رکوع اور سجدہ ہے اس کے علاوہ رکوع اور سجدے سے سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہوتا ہے۔ اور نماز کے رکوع اور اس کے سجدے سے بھی سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہو گا اگر اس کی نیت کرے بشرطیکہ تلاوت کی تیزی دو آیت سے زیادہ سے منقطع نہ ہوئی ہو تشریح : نماز میں آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو اس کو ادا کرنے کی چار صورتیں بتا رہے ہیں ۔ [1] نماز میں جو رکوع سجدہ ہے اس کے علاوہ سجدہ کر لے، یہ سب سے بہتر طریقہ ہے ۔ [۲] نماز میں جو رکوع سجدہ ہے، اس کے علاوہ رکوع کر لے تب بھی سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہو جائے گا۔ (۳) آیت سجدہ پڑھنے کے بعد دو آیتوں سے کم پڑھی ہو اور نماز کا رکوع کر لیا اور اس میں سجدہ تلاوت کی نیت کر لی تو اس سے بھی سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہو جائے گا ۔ [۴] آیت سجدہ پڑھنے کے بعد دو آیت سے کم پڑھی ، اور نماز کے سجدے میں چلا گیا ، اب اس سجدے میں سجدہ تلاوت کی نیت نہیں بھی کرے گا تب بھی سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ دونوں سجدے قریب قریب ہو گئے۔ وجه : (ا) عن ابراهيم انه كان يقول اذا سمع الرجل السجدة و هو يصلى فليخر ساجدا ( مصنف ابن ابی شبيبة ، باب من قال اذا سمعها و ھو یصلی فلیسجد ، ج اول ص ۱۳۷۴ نمبر ۴۳۱۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ نماز کے سجدے کے علاوہ سے سجدہ تلاوت کرے۔ (۲) اور نماز کے رکوع یا اس کے سجدے سے سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہو گا اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن ابراهیم قال اذا سمعت السجدة و انت تصلى فاسجد فان كنت راكعا او ساجدا أجزاك من السجدة (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب اذا سمعت السجدة وانت تصلى وفي کم یقرأ القرآن، ج ثالث ، ص ۲۱۲، نمبر ۵۹۵۷) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ نماز کا ہی رکوع یا سجدہ کر لیا تو سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہو جائے گا۔
(762) And it is performed by bowing or prostration in prayer other than the prayer's bowing and prostration, and the prayer's bowing is sufficient for it if he intends it, and its prostration even if he does not intend it, when the immediacy of recitation is not interrupted by more than two verses. Translation: (762) Sajdah tilawah is performed by ruku' or sujud within the prayer other than the prayer's own ruku' and sujud. And the prayer's own ruku' suffices for it if he intends it, and its sujud even if he does not intend it, provided the immediacy of recitation is not broken by more than two verses. Explanation: If one recites a verse of prostration during prayer, four scenarios are mentioned for performing it. [1] Best: perform a separate sujud besides the prayer's sujud. [2] Perform a separate ruku'. [3] If after reciting the verse one recites less than two more verses and then goes into the prayer's ruku' with the intention for sajdah tilawah, that suffices. [4] If after reciting the verse one recites less than two more verses and then goes into the prayer's sujud without intention, that also suffices because the two prostrations are close. Evidence: (a) From Ibrahim: he used to say, 'When a man hears a verse of prostration while praying, let him fall into prostration.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) This indicates a separate sujud. (b) From Ibrahim: he said, 'When you hear a verse of prostration while praying, prostrate. And if you are bowing or prostrating, that suffices for the prostration (of tilawah).' (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq) This indicates that the prayer's own ruku' or sujud can suffice with or without intention.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage provides the Hanafi ruling on how to perform sajdah tilawah when one recites or hears a verse of prostration while they are already in prayer. The matn lists four methods: (1) performing a separate sujud outside the prayer's normal sujud; (2) performing a separate ruku'; (3) using the prayer's own ruku' with the intention for tilawah, provided no more than two ayahs have been recited after the sajdah verse; (4) using the prayer's own sujud without intention, also conditioned by the recitation not being interrupted by more than two verses. The commentary explains that these options exist, with the separate sujud being the best. The evidence comes from sayings of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, a tabi'i, which the Hanafi school accepts as proof. The lesson type is ruling with proof, as the text includes both the ruling and the supporting athar. The key condition is the continuity of recitation (fawr) not being broken by more than two verses; otherwise, the prayer's ruku' or sujud cannot substitute.

Key Terms
فور التلاوة (fawr al-tilāwah): The immediacy of recitation; the uninterrupted sequence of verses after the sajdah verse.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdah al-tilāwah): The prostration of recitation performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
آية سجدة (āyah sajdah): A Quranic verse that contains a command or indication to prostrate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid method of performing sajdah tilawah inside prayer according to the Hanafi school as described in the passage?
A) Performing a separate sujud.
B) Using the prayer's ruku without intention as long as fawr is maintained.
C) Using the prayer's sujud without intention as long as fawr is maintained.
D) Using the prayer's ruku with intention as long as fawr is maintained.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah tilawah inside prayer can be performed by a separate sujud (best), a separate ruku, or by the prayer's own ruku (with intention) or sujud (without intention), provided the recitation is not interrupted by more than two verses.
