Sajdah Tilawah When Hearing from Imam
Ruling on sajdah for one hearing imam's recitation but not following him

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of hearing a sajdah verse from an imam and apply the Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajdah verse from an imam obligates prostration; timing varies by whether you join before or after his sujud.

The obligation of sajdah tilawah is triggered by hearing or reciting a verse of prostration. But what if you hear it from an imam during congregational prayer and are not following him? The Hanafi school provides a clear rule for three distinct scenarios, as explained in this classical manual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its category
Determine that the act in question is sajdah tilawah, which is wajib upon hearing or reciting a verse of prostration.
This is a general rule; the passage specifies the timing relative to an imam.
2
Identify the hukm level
Sajdah tilawah is wajib in all scenarios; only the method of performance differs.
The 'azhar' view confirms wajib status.
3
List the three scenarios
The passage describes: (1) hearing but not joining prayer, (2) joining after imam's sujud, (3) joining before imam's sujud.
These are derived from the matn and Urdu commentary.
4
Apply the ruling to each scenario
For scenarios 1 and 2, prostrate outside the prayer; for scenario 3, prostrate with the imam.
The condition 'before his prostration' is key for scenario 3.
5
Note the authority
The ruling is given as the 'azhar' (most apparent) view within the Hanafi school, indicating it is the relied-upon position.
This strengthens the obligation and timing rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۶۳) ولو سمع من امام فلم يأتم به او ائتم في ركعة اخرى سجد خارج الصلوة في الاظهر وان ائتم قبل اندر آیت سجدہ پڑھی اور اس کی بازگشت سنی تو اس سے سجدہ واجب نہیں ہے۔
ترجمه : (۷۶۳) اگر امام سے آیت سجدہ سنی اور اس کی اقتداء نہیں کی ، یا دوسری رکعت میں اقتداء کی تو ظاہر روایت یہ ہے کہ نماز سے باہر سجدہ کرے۔ اور اگر امام کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے اقتداء کر لی تو امام کے ساتھ سجدہ کرے گا۔ تشریح : یہاں تین صورتیں ہیں [1] مسجد میں گیا تو امام آیت سجدہ پڑھ رہے تھے جسکو اس آدمی نے سنا لیکن اس نماز میں شریک ہی نہیں ہوئے تو نماز سے باہر سجدہ کرے گا ۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ جس رکعت میں آیت سجدہ پڑھی اس رکعت میں شریک نہیں ہوئے ، بلکہ دوسری رکعت میں شریک ہوئے اور امام اس سے پہلی رکعت میں سجدہ تلاوت کر چکے تھے ، تب بھی یہ آدمی باہر سجدہ کرے گا۔ [۳] اور تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ امام کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے نماز میں شریک ہوئے تو امام کے ساتھ سجدہ کرے گا
(763) And if he hears from an imam and does not follow him, or follows in another rak'ah, he prostrates outside the prayer in the apparent view, and if he follows before [the imam prostrates]... Translation: (763) If one hears a verse of prostration from an imam and does not follow him, or he follows in a different rak'ah, then according to the apparent narration, he should prostrate outside the prayer. And if he joins before the imam prostrates, he will prostrate with the imam. Explanation: Three scenarios: 1) He enters the mosque and hears the imam reciting the verse but does not join the prayer; he prostrates outside prayer. 2) He joins the prayer in a later rak'ah after the imam already performed sajdah tilawah; he prostrates outside prayer after completing his own prayer or immediately? The text says outside prayer. 3) He joins the prayer before the imam performs the tilawah sujud; then he prostrates with the imam.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This ruling addresses the situation where a person hears an imam recite a verse of prostration during congregational prayer but is not a follower of that imam, either because he is not praying or because he joins the prayer at a later rak'ah. The matn states that in such cases, according to the 'azhar' (most apparent) view, he should perform sajdah outside of the prayer (i.e., after the prayer concludes, or independently if he is not in prayer). However, if he joins the congregation before the imam performs the tilawah sujud, then he follows the imam in that sujud. The Urdu commentary clarifies three scenarios: (1) hearing but not joining at all; (2) joining after the imam's tilawah sujud; (3) joining before. In scenarios 1 and 2, he prostrates outside; in scenario 3, he prostrates with the imam. This ruling is based on the principle that the tilawah sujud requires immediate performance, but if one misses it with the imam, he makes it up later.

Key Terms
في الاظهر (fī al-aẓhar): In the most apparent (or correct) view; i.e., the relied-upon position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a person do if he hears the imam recite a sajdah verse but does not join the congregation?
A) Prostrate with the imam immediately.
B) Prostrate outside of the prayer (e.g., after it).
C) Sajdah is not obligatory since he did not join.
D) He must repeat the verse himself and then prostrate.

Key Takeaway
When you hear a sajdah verse from an imam but are not following him, you must still prostrate, but outside the prayer; only if you join before his prostration do you prostrate with him.

Performing Sajdat al-Tilawah During Prayer
Explains the four methods of performing sajdat al-tilawah in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four methods of performing sajdat al-tilawah in prayer and apply the condition of fawr al-tilawah to determine validity.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah in prayer can be fulfilled by separate acts or by the prayer's own ruku/sujud under strict conditions.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on how to perform sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation) when one is already engaged in prayer. The text outlines four distinct methods, each with specific requirements regarding intention and continuity of recitation. Understanding these options is essential for correctly fulfilling this wajib act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that sajdat al-tilawah is wajib (obligatory) upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration while in prayer.
The Hanafi school holds it as wajib, based on a proof from the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
2
Enumerate the four methods
List the four ways to fulfill the sajdah in prayer: (1) extra ruku, (2) extra sujud, (3) prayer's ruku with intention, (4) prayer's sujud without intention.
The text prioritizes separate ruku/sujud as the best method.
3
Understand the condition of fawr al-tilawah
Recognize that the prayer's ruku/sujud only suffices if the connection to recitation is not broken by more than two verses. If broken, a separate sujud is required.
Fawr al-tilawah means immediate continuity.
4
Apply to a scenario
Practice: If a person recites a sajdah verse, then prays two more verses before bowing, is the ruku sufficient? No, because the gap exceeds two verses.
The condition applies to both ruku and sujud methods.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider sajdat al-tilawah sunnah, not wajib. This affects the emphasis on fulfilling it.
The Hanafi view is based on the imperative in the reported statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود التلاوة
وَتُؤَدَّى بِرُكُوعٍ أَوْ سُجُودٍ فِي الصَّلَاةِ غَيْرِ رُكُوعِ الصَّلَاةِ وَسُجُودِهَا وَيُجْزِي عَنْهَا رُكُوعُ الصَّلَاةِ إِنْ نَوَاهَا وَسُجُودُهَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْوِهَا إِذَا لَمْ يَنْقَطِعْ فَوْرُ التِّلَاوَةِ بِأَكْثَرَ مِنْ آيَتَيْنِ.
وَالصَّدَى (٦٢) وَتُؤَدَّى بِرُكُوعٍ أَوْ سُجُودٍ فِي الصَّلَاةِ غَيْرِ رُكُوعِ الصَّلَاةِ وَسُجُودِهَا وَيُجْزِي عَنْهَا رُكُوعُ الصَّلَاةِ إِنْ نَوَاهَا وَسُجُودُهَا وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْوِهَا إِذَا لَمْ يَنْقَطِعْ فَوْرُ التِّلَاوَةِ بِأَكْثَرَ مِنْ آيَتَيْنِ. (۷۶۳) وَلَوْ سَمِعَ مِنْ إِمَامٍ فَلَمْ يَأْتَمَّ بِهِ أَوِ ائْتَمَّ فِي رَكْعَةٍ أُخْرَى سَجَدَ خَارِجَ الصَّلَاةِ فِي الْأَظْهَرِ وَإِنِ ائْتَمَّ قَبْلَ سُجُودِ إِمَامِهَا سَجَدَ مَعَهُ.
The prostration of recitation is performed by a bow or prostration in the prayer other than the bow and prostration of the prayer, and the bow of the prayer suffices for it if he intends it, and its prostration suffices even if he does not intend it, when the immediacy of recitation is not interrupted by more than two verses.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on performing sajdat al-tilawah during prayer. It states that the sajdah can be performed by an extra ruku or sujud beyond those of the prayer (best method). Alternatively, the prayer's own ruku or sujud can fulfill the obligation if intention is made (ruku) or even without intention (sujud) provided the connection to recitation is not broken by more than two verses. The proof is from the sayings of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a tabi'i). The text then transitions to the next ruling (763).

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujūd al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (ayat as-sajdah).
فور التلاوة (fawr al-tilāwah): The immediate continuity of recitation; if broken by more than two verses, the sajdah is not replaced by prayer's ruku/sujud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following methods of performing sajdat al-tilawah during prayer requires intentional (niyyah)?
A) Performing an extra ruku
B) Using the prayer's ruku
C) Using the prayer's sujud
D) Performing an extra sujud

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah in prayer can be fulfilled in four ways, but only the prayer's ruku requires intention; the prayer's sujud suffices without intention if recitation continuity is unbroken.

Ruling on Sajdat al-Tilawah When Hearing from an Imam Without Joining
Ruling on sajdat al-tilawah when hearing from an imam without following his prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for sajdat al-tilawah when hearing an imam's recitation without joining the prayer, and apply the rule to different scenarios of joining.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing; if not following the imam, prostrate separately.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses a common scenario: you hear an imam recite a sajdah verse, but you are not praying behind him, or you join later. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance on when to prostrate with the imam and when to do it independently. Understanding this ruling prevents confusion in daily mosque attendance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that sajdat al-tilawah is a wajib act upon hearing or reciting a sajdah verse. The text assumes it is wajib; the discussion is about the method when hearing from an imam.
The ruling of the sajdah itself is not in dispute here.
2
Determine the relationship to the imam
Are you following the imam in prayer (iqtida) or not? This is the key variable. The text distinguishes between those who join the prayer and those who do not, and between joining before or after the imam's sajdah.
Iqtida is established by joining the congregation with the intention of following.
3
Apply the dichotomy
If you do not follow at all, or join after the imam has already performed the sajdah, you must prostrate outside the prayer (the 'azhar' narration). If you join before the imam's sajdah, you prostrate with him.
The phrase 'في الأظهر' indicates this is the preferred narration; other narrations may differ.
4
Understand the proof
The sajdah is tied to the recitation, but following the imam synchronizes the obligation. If not following, you are independent and perform the sajdah outside the prayer. This is based on qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) from general principles of following the imam.
The proof is aqli (rational) rather than from a specific text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۶۳) وَلَوْ سَمِعَ مِنْ إِمَامٍ فَلَمْ يَأْتَمَّ بِهِ أَوِ ائْتَمَّ فِي رَكْعَةٍ أُخْرَى سَجَدَ خَارِجَ الصَّلَاةِ فِي الْأَظْهَرِ وَإِنِ ائْتَمَّ قَبْلَ سُجُودِ إِمَامِهَا سَجَدَ مَعَهُ.
ترجمه : (۷۶۳) اگر امام سے آیت سجدہ سنی اور اس کی اقتداء نہیں کی ، یا دوسری رکعت میں اقتداء کی تو ظاہر روایت یہ ہے کہ نماز سے باہر سجدہ کرے۔ اور اگر امام کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے اقتداء کر لی تو امام کے ساتھ سجدہ کرے گا۔ تشریح : یہاں تین صورتیں ہیں [1] مسجد میں گیا تو امام آیت سجدہ پڑھ رہے تھے جسکو اس آدمی نے سنا لیکن اس نماز میں شریک ہی نہیں ہوئے تو نماز سے باہر سجدہ کرے گا ۔ [۲] دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ جس رکعت میں آیت سجدہ پڑھی اس رکعت میں شریک نہیں ہوئے ، بلکہ دوسری رکعت میں شریک ہوئے اور امام اس سے پہلی رکعت میں سجدہ تلاوت کر چکے تھے ، تب بھی یہ آدمی باہر سجدہ کرے گا۔ [۳] اور تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ امام کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے نماز میں شریک ہوئے تو امام کے ساتھ سجدہ کرے گا‎
And if he heard from an imam but did not follow him, or followed in another rak'ah, he prostrates outside the prayer in the most apparent (narration). And if he followed before the prostration of his imam, he prostrates with him.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents three scenarios regarding sajdat al-tilawah when hearing from an imam without joining the prayer initially. If one hears the verse but does not join the prayer at all, or joins in a later rak'ah after the imam has already prostrated, he must perform the sajdah outside the prayer. This is the relied-upon position (al-azhar). If he joins before the imam's sajdah, he prostrates with the imam. The proof is based on the principle that the sajdah is tied to the recitation, and if one does not follow the imam in the prayer, he is independent in his obligation.

Key Terms
الأظهر (al-azhar): The most apparent or preferred narration within the Hanafi school.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration of recitation upon hearing or reciting a sajdah verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person enters the mosque and hears the imam reciting a sajdah verse but does not join the prayer. What should he do?
A) Prostrate with the imam immediately.
B) Prostrate after the imam's prayer.
C) Prostrate outside the prayer on his own.
D) No sajdah is required as he is not in prayer.

Key Takeaway
If you hear a sajdah verse from an imam but are not following him in prayer, you must perform sajdat al-tilawah outside the prayer; only if you join before his prostration do you prostrate with him.

Joining Imam After Sajdah of Recitation
Ruling on joining imam after sajdat al-tilawah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a person who joins the imam after sajdat al-tilawah and identify the condition under which no sajdah is required.

Core Idea
If you join the imam after his sajdah in the same rak'ah, you catch it in ruling — no sajdah needed.

In the previous lessons we discussed scenarios of sajdat al-tilawah. Here we address the case of joining the imam after he has prostrated. The ruling is that you are considered to have caught the sajdah in hukm, so you do not perform it yourself. This is similar to catching a rak'ah for recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a person who joins the imam in the same rak'ah after the imam has already performed sajdat al-tilawah, before ruku'. This is the fourth scenario in the series.
Key condition: joining before ruku' in the same rak'ah.
2
Recognize the key term: mudrik
Such a person is called mudrik — one who catches an action in ruling (hukman). He is considered to have caught the sajdah even though he did not perform it personally.
The term mudrik is used here to indicate legal attribution.
3
Apply the analogy with catching recitation
Just as joining before ruku' gives credit for the recitation of that rak'ah, joining before ruku' gives credit for the sajdah. The analogy (qiyas) is explicit in the Urdu commentary.
This analogy strengthens the ruling.
4
State the ruling
The mudrik does not perform sajdat al-tilawah at all — neither during nor after the prayer. The text says 'فلا يسجدها أصلا' (so he does not prostrate it at all).
This is the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۶۴) فَإِنِ اقْتَدَى بِهِ بَعْدَ سُجُودِهَا فِي رَكْعَتِهَا صَارَ مُدْرِكًا لَهَا حُكْمًا فَلَا يَسْجُدُهَا أَصْلًا.
ترجمه : (۷۶۴) اور اگر امام کی اقتدا اسی رکعت میں سجدہ کرنے کے بعد کیا تو حکما اس سجدے کو پانے والا ہو گیا، اس لئے اب بالکل سجدہ نہ کرے۔ تشریح : یہ چوتھی شکل ہے۔ آدمی نے نماز میں شریک ہونے سے پہلے امام صاحب سے آیت سجدہ سنی ، پھر امام صاحب نے سجدہ کیا ، اس وقت یہ آدمی نماز میں شریک نہیں تھا اب بعد میں اسی رکعت میں رکوع سے پہلے اس نے شرکت کی تو یہ کہا جائے گا کہ اس آدمی کو امام کا سجدہ حکم مل گیا، اس لئے اب بعد میں نماز میں یا نماز سے باہر سجدہ نہ کرے، جس طرح یہ رکوع میں ملتا تو اس رکعت کی قرآت مل جاتی ، اسی طرح یہاں مسجد مل گیا۔
And if he followed him after his prostration in its rak'ah, he becomes a perceiver of it in ruling, so he does not prostrate it at all.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion from the previous lesson. Here, the fourth scenario: a person hears the imam's prostration verse, does not join immediately, the imam prostrates, then later before ruku the person joins the prayer in that same rak'ah. In this case, he is considered to have caught the sajdah in ruling (hukman), so he does not need to prostrate later, either inside or outside the prayer. The analogy is with catching a rak'ah for recitation: if one joins before ruku, he catches the recitation.

Key Terms
مدرك (mudrik): One who joins the prayer after the imam has already performed an action, but is considered to have caught it in ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Not perform it at all.
D) Perform it in the next rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
If you join the imam in the same rak'ah before ruku after his sajdat al-tilawah, you catch it in ruling and do not need to prostrate.

No Qada of Prayer's Sajdah Outside Prayer
Ruling that the sajdat al-tilawah missed in prayer is not made up outside

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada of sajdat al-tilawah missed in prayer and apply it to different scenarios of remembrance timing.

Core Idea
A sajdat al-tilawah missed in prayer cannot be made up outside; if remembered before speaking, it is done within; after speaking, repeat prayer.

Sometimes during prayer you recite a sajdah verse but forget to prostrate. What then? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: you cannot make up that sajdah after the prayer ends. Instead, the ruling depends on when you remember — before or after speaking — with distinct consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making up (qada) a missed sajdat al-tilawah outside the prayer. The ruling is that it is not valid; it must be done within the prayer itself.
The text explicitly says: 'وَلَمْ تُقْضَ الصَّلَوْتِيَّةُ خَارِجَهَا' — the prayer's sajdah is not made up outside it.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence comes from statements of the tabi'een Ibrahim al-Nakha'i and al-Hasan al-Basri, recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
These are considered ahad reports but sufficient for this ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase is 'في صلوته' (in his prayer) — the sajdah must be performed within the prayer. This restricts qada to within the same prayer session.
If remembered after the prayer but before speaking, it is still considered 'within' the prayer state.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may allow qada outside the prayer in certain circumstances, but the Hanafi position is clear: no qada outside the prayer.
This is marked as mukhtalaf fih.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Scenario A: Remember during prayer → perform the sajdah immediately. Scenario B: Remember after prayer, before speaking → perform one sujud. Scenario C: Remember after speaking → prayer invalid, must be repeated with the sajdah.
The source mentions that if one speaks, 'استأنف الصلوة' — he restarts the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۶۵) وَلَمْ تُقْضَ الصَّلَوْتِيَّةُ خَارِجَهَا.
ترجمه : (۷۶۵) اور نماز کا سجدہ اس کے باہر قضا نہ کیا جائے۔ تشریح : آیت سجدہ نماز کے اندر پڑھی اس لئے نماز کے اندر ہی سجدہ واجب تھا، اب نماز میں سجدہ نہیں کیا تو اس کو باہر قضا نہ کرے، بلکہ یہ سجدہ چھوٹ گیا۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن يونس عن الحسن في رجل نسى سجدة من صلوته فلم يذكرها حتى كان في آخر ركعة من صلوته قال يسجد فيها ثلاث سجدات فان لم يذكرها حتى يقضى صلوته غير انه لم يسلم بعد ، قال : يسجد سجدة واحدة ما لم يتكلم فان تكلم استأنف الصلوة . (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب الرجل بينسى السجدة من الصلوة فيذكرها وهو يیصلی ، ج اول ص ۳۸۳، نمبر ۴۳۹۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اگر نماز میں سجدہ نہیں کیا اور بات کر لی، تو شروع سے نماز پڑھے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ نکلا کہ نماز ہوئی ہی نہیں، دوبارہ نماز بھی پڑھے اور سجدہ بھی کرے۔(۲) دوسرے اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال : اذا نسى الرجل سجدة من الصلوة فليسجدها متى ما ذكرها في صلوته (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب الرجل ينسى السجدة من الصلوۃ فیذ کرھا وھو یصلی ، ج اول ص ۳۸۳، نمبر ۴۳۹۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نماز میں جب تک ہو تو سجدہ کر سکتا ہے۔ جسکا مطلب یہ نکلا کہ نماز سے باہر سجدہ نہ کرے۔
And the prayer's (sajdah) is not made up outside it.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This ruling states that if one omits sajdat al-tilawah during prayer, it cannot be made up after the prayer ends. The evidence from the sayings of al-Hasan and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i indicates that if one remembers before speaking (talking), he can make it up within the prayer by adding an extra sujud or even repeating the prayer. Once he speaks outside the prayer, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated with the sajdah.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qadā): Making up an obligatory act after its prescribed time; here, not allowed for sajdat al-tilawah outside prayer.
الصَّلَوْتِيَّة (al-ṣalawtiyya): The sajdah related to the prayer, i.e., sajdat al-tilawah performed within prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone recites a sajdah verse in prayer but forgets to prostrate and only remembers after the prayer has ended and he has spoken, what should he do?
A) Perform sajdat al-tilawah immediately outside prayer.
B) Repeat the entire prayer with the sajdah performed in it.
C) Do nothing; it is forgiven.
D) Perform sajdat al-sahw instead.

Key Takeaway
The missed sajdat al-tilawah from prayer cannot be made up outside; it must be performed within the prayer, and if spoken after, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.

Reciting Sajdah Outside and Again Inside Prayer
Ruling on reciting a prostration verse after prior sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting a prostration verse after having already performed its sajdah outside prayer, and identify that the obligation is discharged by the first performance.

Core Idea
One sajdah per verse: performing sajdat al-tilawah once fulfills the obligation for all subsequent recitations.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: if you have already performed the prostration for a particular sajdah verse outside of prayer, and then you recite the same verse again inside prayer, you are not required to repeat the sajdah. The ruling is based on the principle that the obligation is tied to the recitation and is discharged by the first performance. Understanding this prevents unnecessary repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Sequential Acts
Break down the scenario: first, a prostration verse is recited outside prayer and the sajdah is performed. Second, the same verse is recited again inside a subsequent prayer.
The order is important: the sajdah outside prayer must have already been performed.
2
Determine the Ruling
The text states 'لم يلزمه سجدة أخرى' meaning another prostration is not obligatory. Recognize that this is a negation of obligation (wujub).
The key term is 'لازم' (lāzim), indicating legal obligation.
3
Extract the Condition
The condition for no second sajdah is that the first sajdah was already performed for the same verse. The obligation is fulfilled by the first act.
If the first sajdah had not been performed, the recitation inside prayer would obligate a sajdah.
4
Note the Madhhab Context
This is the Hanafi position. Other schools may hold that each recitation in a new prayer requires a new sajdah, even if previously performed.
The difference arises from varying definitions of the obligation's trigger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۷۶۶) وَلَوْ تَلَا خَارِجَ الصَّلَاةِ فَسَجَدَ ثُمَّ دَخَلَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ فَتَلَاهَا فِيهَا لَمْ يَلْزَمْهُ سَجْدَةٌ أُخْرَى.
ترجمه : (۷۶۶) اور اگر خارج نماز میں آیت سجدہ تلاوت کر کے سجدہ کر لیا پھر نماز میں اس آیت کو دہرایا تو اب دوسرا سجدہ لازم نہیں ہے۔
And if he recites outside the prayer and prostrates, then enters the prayer and recites it therein, another prostration is not obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This ruling states that sajdat al-tilawah is only obligated once for the same recitation. If one recites a prostration verse outside prayer and performs the sajdah, then later in prayer recites the same verse, no second sajdah is required. This is because the obligation is tied to the first recitation and has been fulfilled.

Key Terms
لازم (lāzim): Legally obligatory; here, the second sajdah is not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person recites a sajdah verse while walking and performs sajdat al-tilawah. Later, in his prayer, he recites the same verse again. What is required?
A) A second sajdah inside prayer.
B) No second sajdah.
C) A sajdah only if he intends it.
D) He must repeat the first sajdah with intention.

Key Takeaway
One sajdat al-tilawah per prostration verse suffices for all subsequent recitations of that verse, even across different contexts like outside and inside prayer.

Ruling on Joining Imam After Tilāwah Prostration
States ruling for one who joins after imam's prostration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for joining the imam after sajdah tilawah and explain the qiyas that underlies it.

Core Idea
Joining after sajdah tilawah legally counts as performing it, so no further prostration is needed.

What happens when you hear a prostration verse outside prayer, the imam prostrates, and then you join the congregation? Does the missed prostration still need to be performed? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling based on analogy to joining the imam in ruku. Understanding this scenario helps you know when a prostration is satisfied and when it is not, avoiding unnecessary repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Pinpoint the exact situation: a person hears the imam recite a prostration verse and prostrate while he is not in prayer, then later joins the same rak'ah before ruku.
This is distinct from joining during the prostration or after completing the rak'ah.
2
State the ruling
According to the Hanafi school, the latecomer does not perform any prostration for that verse, either during prayer or afterward.
The ruling applies 'hukman' (legally), not necessarily physically.
3
Trace the analogy (qiyas)
The ruling is derived by analogy to joining the imam in ruku: just as joining in ruku grants the recitation of that rak'ah, joining after sajdah tilawah grants the prostration.
This is a clear (jali) qiyas based on the common illa of 'catching the act in the same rak'ah'.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the latecomer must still perform the prostration because he missed the physical act. The Hanafi position considers the legal attainment sufficient.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf with practical consequences in congregational prayer.
5
Apply to similar scenarios
If the person joins after ruku or in a different rak'ah, the ruling changes. Here, only the specific scenario results in no additional prostration.
The key condition is joining in the same rak'ah before ruku.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۶۴) اور اگر امام کی اقتدا اسی رکعت میں سجدہ کرنے کے بعد کیا تو حکما اس سجدے کو پانے والا ہو گیا، اس لئے اب بالکل سجدہ نہ کرے۔ تشریح : یہ چوتھی شکل ہے۔ آدمی نے نماز میں شریک ہونے سے پہلے امام صاحب سے آیت سجدہ سنی ، پھر امام صاحب نے سجدہ کیا ، اس وقت یہ آدمی نماز میں شریک نہیں تھا اب بعد میں اسی رکعت میں رکوع سے پہلے اس نے شرکت کی تو یہ کہا جائے گا کہ اس آدمی کو امام کا سجدہ حکم مل گیا، اس لئے اب بعد میں نماز میں یا نماز سے باہر سجدہ نہ کرے، جس طرح یہ رکوع میں ملتا تو اس رکعت کی قرآت مل جاتی ، اسی طرح یہاں مسجد مل گیا۔
Translation: (764) If he follows the imam in that same rak'ah after the prostration, he becomes, legally speaking, one who has attained that prostration, so he should not prostrate at all. Explanation: This is the fourth scenario. A man heard the verse of prostration from the imam before joining the prayer, then the imam prostrated at that time, the man was not in the prayer. Later in the same rak'ah, before bowing, he joined. Then it will be said that this man has legally attained the imam's prostration, so thereafter he should not prostrate either in prayer or outside prayer, just as when he joins in bowing, he attains the recitation of that rak'ah, similarly here he has attained the prostration.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof by analogy (qiyas jaliy). It addresses a specific scenario: a person hears a verse of prostration being recited by the imam while he (the listener) is not yet in prayer. The imam then performs the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah). Afterwards, this person joins the prayer in the same rak'ah before bowing. The ruling is that he should not perform any prostration for that verse, neither in prayer nor later, because he is considered to have caught up with the imam's prostration legally (hukman). The reasoning is analogous to joining the imam in ruku: if one joins in ruku, he attains the recitation of that rak'ah; similarly, joining after the prostration means he attains the prostration. This is a Hanafi ruling based on qiyas, and the text mentions no direct dalil, so the argument type is qiyas jaliy.

Key Terms
حکما (ḥukman): Legally (i.e., in the estimation of law, regardless of actual physical performance).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hears the imam recite a prostration verse and prostrate, then joins the prayer in the same rak'ah before ruku, what should he do?
A) Perform the prostration immediately after joining
B) Perform the prostration after the prayer
C) Not perform any prostration for that verse
D) Repeat the entire rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Joining the imam after sajdah tilawah in the same rak'ah legally fulfills the prostration, so no further action is needed.

Sajdah Tilawah Forgotten in Prayer Is Not Made Up Outside
Ruling with proof: sajdah tilawah missed in prayer is not made up outside.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing sajdah tilawah after forgetting it during prayer and explain the evidence from the two athar.

Core Idea
A sajdah tilawah missed in prayer is not made up outside; it is lost.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah addresses a common situation: you recite an ayat sajdah during prayer, forget to prostrate, and only remember after salam. What is the ruling? The author rules that the prostration is not to be performed outside the prayer. Let us examine the evidence from the sayings of the Tabi‘un that support this position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Forgetting to perform sajdah tilawah during prayer. The ruling: it is not made up outside the prayer.
The act is sajdah tilawah, which is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Two athar from the Tabi‘un (al-Hasan and Ibrahim) in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah are cited as evidence.
These are sayings of the Tabi‘un, not directly from the Prophet, but used as supporting proofs in the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The second athar states: 'if a man forgets a prostration of his prayer, let him prostrate whenever he remembers it in his prayer.' The phrase 'in his prayer' (في صلوته) restricts the prostration to within the prayer, implying it cannot be done outside.
The first athar gives practical consequences but does not allow prostration after salam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that if one forgets sajdah tilawah, he should prostrate whenever he remembers, even after salam. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The difference stems from how each school interprets the general command to prostrate when reciting sajdah verses.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit restriction in the athar. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that sajdah tilawah is not made up after salam.
This is the standard position in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۶۵) اور نماز کا سجدہ اس کے باہر قضا نہ کیا جائے۔ تشریح : آیت سجدہ نماز کے اندر پڑھی اس لئے نماز کے اندر ہی سجدہ واجب تھا، اب نماز میں سجدہ نہیں کیا تو اس کو باہر قضا نہ کرے، بلکہ یہ سجدہ چھوٹ گیا۔ وجه : (۱) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن يونس عن الحسن في رجل نسى سجدة من صلوته فلم يذكرها حتى كان في آخر ركعة من صلوته قال يسجد فيها ثلاث سجدات فان لم يذكرها حتى يقضى صلوته غير انه لم يسلم بعد ، قال : يسجد سجدة واحدة ما لم يتكلم فان تكلم استأنف الصلوة . (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب الرجل بينسى السجدة من الصلوة فيذكرها وهو يیصلی ، ج اول ص ۳۸۳، نمبر ۴۳۹۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اگر نماز میں سجدہ نہیں کیا اور بات کر لی، تو شروع سے نماز پڑھے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ نکلا کہ نماز ہوئی ہی نہیں، دوبارہ نماز بھی پڑھے اور سجدہ بھی کرے۔(۲) دوسرے اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال : اذا نسى الرجل سجدة من الصلوة فليسجدها متى ما ذكرها في صلوته (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب الرجل ينسى السجدة من الصلوۃ فیذ کرھا وھو یصلی ، ج اول ص ۳۸۳، نمبر ۴۳۹۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ نماز میں جب تک ہو تو سجدہ کر سکتا ہے۔ جسکا مطلب یہ نکلا کہ نماز سے باہر سجدہ نہ کرے۔
Translation: (765) And the prostration of prayer is not made up outside of it. Explanation: The verse of prostration was recited inside the prayer, so the prostration was obligatory inside the prayer. Now, if he did not prostrate in the prayer, he should not make it up outside; rather, this prostration is lost. Reasoning: (1) This is in the saying of a Tabi‘i: from Yunus from al-Hasan concerning a man who forgot a prostration of his prayer and did not remember it until he was in the last rak‘ah of his prayer; he said: he should perform three prostrations in it. If he does not remember until he completes his prayer, but he has not yet said salam, he said: he should perform one prostration as long as he has not spoken; if he speaks, he should restart the prayer. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab al-Rajul yansa al-sajdah min al-salah… no. 4398). This athar indicates that if he did not prostrate in prayer and spoke, he should pray from the beginning, meaning the prayer is invalid and he must repeat both the prayer and the prostration. (2) Another athar: from Ibrahim: if a man forgets a prostration of his prayer, let him prostrate whenever he remembers it in his prayer. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 4399). This athar indicates that as long as he is still in prayer, he may prostrate, implying he should not prostrate outside prayer.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling supported by two athar (sayings of Tabi‘un). The ruling is clear: if one forgets to perform a tilawah prostration during prayer, it is not made up after the prayer. The reasoning is that prostration is tied to the prayer; once the prayer is complete, the time for that prostration has passed. The first athar (from al-Hasan) addresses a scenario where a person remembers the missed prostration during the last rak‘ah: he should perform three prostrations (presumably one for the missed prostration plus two for the regular sajdatayn of that rak‘ah). If he remembers only after completing prayer but before salam, he may perform one prostration. But if he speaks after salam, he must restart the prayer. The second athar (from Ibrahim) allows prostration as long as he is still in prayer, implying it cannot be done outside. The overall ruling is consistent: sajdah tilawah missed in prayer is not made up outside; it is lost. However, if remembered while still in prayer, it should be performed immediately.

Key Terms
قضا (qaḍā’): Making up a missed act of worship after its prescribed time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgets to perform sajdah tilawah during the prayer and only remembers after saying salam, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Perform the prostration immediately after salam
B) Prostrate during the next prayer
C) Not perform the prostration; it is lost
D) Repeat the entire prayer

Key Takeaway
Sajdah tilawah missed in prayer is not made up after prayer; it is lost.

Repeating a Prostration Verse: Effect of Prior Prostration
Ruling on repeating a prostration verse after already prostrating.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios of repeating a prostration verse and apply the rule of tadakhul to determine when one prostration suffices.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one sitting, but prior prostration outside does not fulfill the prayer requirement.

This lesson explores how the Hanafi school handles the situation where a prostration verse is recited multiple times, either in or out of prayer. The key is the rank of the prostration and unity of sitting. By understanding three specific cases, you will learn when a new prostration is required and when one suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger and location
Determine if the recitation is inside or outside prayer and whether a prior prostration was performed.
2
Apply the rank hierarchy
Understand that outside prostration is lower (adna) and inside prostration is higher (a'la). The lower cannot fulfill the higher, but the higher can fulfill the lower.
3
Check for tadakhul (overlap)
If multiple recitations occur in one sitting (majlis), only one prostration is needed due to tadakhul.
4
Derive the ruling per scenario
Use the above principles to state whether a new prostration is required or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۶۶) اور اگر خارج نماز میں آیت سجدہ تلاوت کر کے سجدہ کر لیا پھر نماز میں اس آیت کو دہرایا تو اب دوسرا سجدہ کرے اور اگر پہلے سجدہ نہ کیا ہو تو اس کو ظاہر روایت میں ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے، جیسے اگر کوئی ایک ہی مجلس میں دو مجلس میں نہیں ، ایک آیت کو مکرر پڑھے تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے۔ تشریح : یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں ۔ [1] نماز سے باہر آیت سجدہ پڑھی اور وہیں سجدہ بھی کر لیا، پھر نماز کی نیت باندھی اور اس میں بھی وہی آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو نماز میں دوبارہ سجدہ کرے، کیونکہ پہلا سجدہ ادنی ہے اور نماز کا سجدہ اعلی ہے اس لئے ادنی سے اعلی ادا نہیں ہوگا ، دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ کئی مرتبہ آیت پڑھی اور بعد میں سجدہ کرے تو سب کے لئے کافی ہے، یہاں پہلے سجدہ کر لیا اس کے بعد آیت پڑھی اس لئے پہلا سجدہ بعد کے لئے کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ [۲] دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز سے باہر آیت پڑھی اور اس کا سجدہ نہیں کیا اور پھر اسی جگہ نماز کی نیت باندھی اور اس میں دوبارہ آیت پڑھی تو نماز کا سجدہ باہر کے لئے کافی ہوگا، کیونکہ باہر کا ادنی ہے اور نماز کا اعلی ہے اس لئے اعلی سے ادنی ادا ہو جائے گا۔[۳] تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مجلس میں ایک آیت کو کئی مرتبہ پڑھے تو ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا ، کیونکہ اتحاد مجلس کی وجہ سے تداخل ہو جائے گا۔ وجه : (۱) نماز کا سجدہ اعلی ہے اس لئے ادنی کے لئے کافی ہے۔ اور چونکہ مجلس ایک ہے اسلئے نماز والا ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہو گا (۲) ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہونے کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن مجاهد قال اذا قرأت السجدة اجزاك ان تسجد بها مرة ، عن ابراهيم في الرجل يقرأ السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها قالا تجزيها السجدة الاولی . (مصنف بن ابی شیبۃ ۲۰۴ ، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها كيف يصنع ج اول ص ۳۶۵، نمبر ۴۱۹۹/۴۲۰۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کئی مرتبہ آیت سجدہ پڑھنے سے اگر مجلس ایک ہو تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے۔ اصول : مجلس بدلتی جائے گی تو سجدہ لازم ہوتا جائے گا۔ اور ایک ہی مجلس میں چند بار آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔
Translation: (766) And if he recited a verse of prostration outside prayer and prostrated, then repeated that verse in prayer, then he should perform another prostration. And if he did not prostrate the first time, then one prostration is sufficient in the apparent narration, like when one repeats a verse in one sitting, not in two. Explanation: Here there are three issues. [1] He recited a prostration verse outside prayer and prostrated there, then he entered prayer and recited the same verse again: in this case he must prostrate again in prayer, because the first prostration is of a lower rank and the prostration in prayer is of a higher rank, so the lower does not fulfill the higher. Also, if he recites multiple times and then prostrates, it suffices for all, but here he prostrated first and then recited, so the first prostration does not suffice for the later recitation. [2] Second issue: If he recited the verse outside prayer and did not prostrate, then he enters prayer in the same place and recites the verse again, then the prostration in prayer will suffice for the one outside, because the outside is lower and the prayer is higher, so the higher fulfills the lower. [3] Third issue: If he recites the same verse multiple times in one sitting, one prostration is necessary, because due to unity of sitting, they overlap (tadakhul). Reasoning: (1) The prostration in prayer is higher, so it suffices for the lower. And because the sitting is one, one prostration suffices. (2) For the sufficiency of one prostration, this is the saying of a Tabi‘i: from Mujahid: if you recite a prostration verse, one prostration will suffice you. From Ibrahim concerning a man who recites a prostration verse and then repeats its recitation: they (both narrators) said that the first prostration suffices for it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, p. 365, nos. 4199/4200). This effect shows that if the sitting is one, one prostration is enough. Principle: If the sitting changes, prostration becomes due repeatedly; in one sitting, several recitations require only one prostration.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage addresses three sub-rulings about the interaction of prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah) when performed inside and outside prayer. The first ruling: if a person prostrates for a verse outside prayer and later recites the same verse inside prayer, he must prostrate again inside. Reason: the first prostration is of lower status (adna) and cannot fulfill the higher requirement of prayer prostration; also, since he prostrated before the second recitation, it cannot suffice for it. The second ruling: if he recites outside without prostrating and then recites inside and prostrates, that inside prostration suffices for both because the higher (prayer prostration) covers the lower. The third ruling: multiple recitations in one sitting (majlis) require only one prostration due to tadakhul (overlap). The reasoning is supported by athar from Mujahid and Ibrahim. The passage concludes with a principle: changing the sitting (majlis) necessitates a new prostration for each recitation.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadākhul): The merging or overlapping of multiple obligations into one performance due to unity of cause or context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person recites a prostration verse multiple times in one sitting, how many prostrations are needed?
A) One for each recitation
B) One total
C) Two
D) None

Key Takeaway
One prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one sitting, but a prior outside prostration does not fulfill the inside requirement because the inside prostration is of higher rank.

Change of Sitting (Majlis) for Sajdah Tilawah
Defines what constitutes a change of sitting for tilawah prostration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define what constitutes a change of sitting (majlis) for sajdah tilawah and apply the rule to determine when multiple prostrations are required.

Core Idea
Any physical relocation changes the sitting; each separate recitation in a new location requires a separate prostration.

In sajdah tilawah, a key question is when a single recitation of a prostration verse triggers one obligation versus many. The Hanafi school clarifies that the determining factor is the majlis (sitting). This passage defines what constitutes a change of majlis, using vivid examples like moving between branches of a tree or swimming across a river.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being defined? The change of majlis for sajdah tilawah. Determine when a new prostration becomes wajib.
2
State the principle
The text states that moving from one place to another changes the majlis.
3
Apply the principle to the given examples
Analyze each example (branch to branch, swimming) to confirm they involve relocation.
4
Derive the consequence
If the same verse is recited again in a new majlis, a new sajdah becomes due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۶۷) اور مجلس بدل جاتی ہے اس جگہ سے منتقل ہونے سے، چاہے وہ تا نا بنتے ہوئے دوسری ڈالی پر جائے، اور منتقل ہونے سے ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف ، اور نہر ، یا بڑے حوض میں تیرنے سے ہیچ تر روایت میں ۔ تشریح : ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے اس سے مجلس بدل جاتی ہے، اور جتنی مرتبہ مجلس بدلتی جائے اور اس میں ایک ہی آیت کو پڑھتا جائے اتنی مرتبہ سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔ آگے مجلس بدلنے کی چند صورتیں پیش کر رہے ہیں ۔ [1] تانا بنتے ہوئے ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف جائے تب بھی مجلس بدل جائے گی۔ [۲] ایک ہی درخت کی مختلف ڈالیوں پر ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف جائے تو مجلس بدل جائے گی [۳] نہر یا بڑے حوض میں تیرے اور ایک کونے سے دوسرے کونے کی طرف
Translation: (767) And the sitting changes by moving from one place to another place, even if he goes from one branch to another while (weaving/climbing?), and by moving from one branch to another, and by swimming in a river or large tank, according to one narration. Explanation: Moving from one place to another changes the sitting. Whenever the sitting changes and he recites the same verse, a prostration becomes due for each occasion. The following are some scenarios of change of sitting: [1] If he moves from one branch to another while (weaving?), even then the sitting changes. [2] If he moves from one branch to another of the same tree, the sitting changes. [3] If he swims in a river or large tank from one corner to another...
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage defines what constitutes a change of sitting (majlis) for the purpose of sajdah tilawah. The principle is: any physical movement from one location to another changes the sitting. If one recites a verse of prostration in one location and then moves to another location and recites the same verse again, a new prostration becomes due. The text gives specific examples: moving from one branch of a tree to another (while climbing or weaving), moving to a different branch of the same tree, or swimming from one end of a river or tank to another. This ruling is based on a narration (riwayah) in the Hanafi school. The underlying principle results in multiple prostrations if the verse is recited in separate sittings.

Key Terms
مجلس (majlis): The sitting or location where one is present; change of majlis occurs by physical movement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Change of majlis occurs by physical relocation; each separate recitation in a new location requires a new sajdah tilawah.

Sujūd al-Tilāwah: Repetition and Tadākhul (Merging)
Ruling on repetition of prostration verses with tadakhul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple recitations of a prostration verse in one session and apply the principle of tadakhul to determine the number of prostrations required.

Core Idea
One prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one session due to tadakhul, avoiding hardship.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: if you recite a prostration verse multiple times, do you need multiple prostrations? The Hanafi school, relying on the principle of tadakhul and the practice of the Tabi'un, rules that one prostration suffices in a single session. We will explore the three scenarios and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Examine the three cases: (1) prostration outside prayer then same verse in prayer, (2) recitation outside without prostration then same verse in prayer, (3) same verse repeated in one session outside prayer. Note how the ruling differs.
Focus on the third scenario as it is the core of the lesson.
2
Understand the principle of tadakhul
Tadakhul (merging) means that multiple causes (recitations) in one session are fulfilled by a single act of prostration. This is a concession to avoid hardship.
The key condition is unity of session (ittihad al-majlis).
3
Analyze the proofs (athar)
Examine the statements from Mujahid and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah. They explicitly state that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations.
These are mursal hadith (Tabi'i sayings) which Hanafis accept as proof when supported by practice.
4
Apply the ruling to new cases
Given the principle and proofs, practice applying the rule: if the session is the same, one prostration; if the session changes, multiple prostrations.
The definition of session change is covered in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود التلاوة
اعاد فيها سجد اخرى وان لم يسجد اولا كفته واحدة فى ظاهر الرواية كمن كرّرها في مجلس واحد لا مجلسين. (٦٧) ويتبدّل المجلس بالانتقال منه ولا مسدّيا وبالانتقال من غصن الى غصن
كرے اور اگر پہلے سجدہ نہ کیا ہو تو اس کو ظاہر روایت میں ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے، جیسے اگر کوئی ایک ہی مجلس میں دو مجلس میں نہیں ، ایک آیت کو مکرر پڑھے تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے۔
تشریح : یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں ۔ [1] نماز سے باہر آیت سجدہ پڑھی اور وہیں سجدہ بھی کر لیا، پھر نماز کی نیت باندھی اور اس میں بھی وہی آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو نماز میں دوبارہ سجدہ کرے، کیونکہ پہلا سجدہ ادنی ہے اور نماز کا سجدہ اعلی ہے اس لئے ادنی سے اعلی ادا نہیں ہوگا ، دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ کئی مرتبہ آیت پڑھی اور بعد میں سجدہ کرے تو سب کے لئے کافی ہے، یہاں پہلے سجدہ کر لیا اس کے بعد آیت پڑھی اس لئے پہلا سجدہ بعد کے لئے کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ [۲] دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز سے باہر آیت پڑھی اور اس کا سجدہ نہیں کیا اور پھر اسی جگہ نماز کی نیت باندھی اور اس میں دوبارہ آیت پڑھی تو نماز کا سجدہ باہر کے لئے کافی ہوگا، کیونکہ باہر کا ادنی ہے اور نماز کا اعلی ہے اس لئے اعلی سے ادنی ادا ہو جائے گا۔[۳] تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مجلس میں ایک آیت کو کئی مرتبہ پڑھے تو ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا ، کیونکہ اتحاد مجلس کی وجہ سے تداخل ہو جائے گا۔
وجه : (۱) نماز کا سجدہ اعلی ہے اس لئے ادنی کے لئے کافی ہے۔ اور چونکہ مجلس ایک ہے اسلئے نماز والا ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہو گا (۲) ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہونے کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن مجاهد قال اذا قرأت السجدة اجزاك ان تسجد بها مرة ، عن ابراهيم في الرجل يقرأ السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها قالا تجزيها السجدة الاولی . (مصنف بن ابی شیبۃ ۲۰۴ ، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها كيف يصنع ج اول ص ۳۶۵، نمبر ۴۱۹۹/۴۲۰۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کئی مرتبہ آیت سجدہ پڑھنے سے اگر مجلس ایک ہو تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے۔ اصول : مجلس بدلتی جائے گی تو سجدہ لازم ہوتا جائے گا۔ اور ایک ہی مجلس میں چند بار آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔ ترجمه : (۷۶۷) اور مجلس بدل جاتی ہے اس جگہ سے منتقل ہونے سے، چاہے وہ تا نا بنتے ہوئے دوسری ڈالی پر جائے، اور منتقل ہونے سے ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف ، اور نہر ، یا بڑے حوض میں تیرنے سے ہیچ تر روایت میں ۔ تشریح : ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے اس سے مجلس بدل جاتی ہے، اور جتنی مرتبہ مجلس بدلتی جائے اور اس میں ایک ہی آیت کو پڑھتا جائے اتنی مرتبہ سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔ آگے مجلس بدلنے کی چند صورتیں پیش کر رہے ہیں ۔ [1] تانا بنتے ہوئے ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف جائے تب بھی مجلس بدل جائے گی۔ [۲] ایک ہی درخت کی مختلف ڈالیوں پر ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف جائے تو مجلس بدل جائے گی [۳] نہر یا بڑے حوض میں تیرے اور ایک کونے سے دوسرے کونے کی طرف

 جائے تو مجلس بدل جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) قیاس کے اعتبار سے ہر آیت پڑھنے کے لئے الگ الگ سجدہ واجب ہونا چاہئے۔ لیکن حرج کے لئے تداخل کر دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اس میں شرط یہ ہے کہ مجلس ایک ہو۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ادنی اعلی میں داخل ہوگا لیکن اعلی ادنی میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ اب اوپر کی صورت میں ایک ہی آیت کئی مرتبہ پڑھی ہے تو اگر مجلس ایک ہے تو تداخل ہو کر ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور مجلس بدل گئی تو کئی سجدے لازم ہونگے ۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن ابی عبد الرحمن انه كان يقرأ السجدة فيسجد ثم يعيدها في مجلسه ذلك مرارا لا يسجد - (مصنف ابن ابی شیت ۲۰۴، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها كيف يصنع ، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۶ نمبر ۴۲۰ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مجلس میں کئی مرتبہ آیت سجدہ پڑھا تو تداخل ہوگا اور ایک ہی سجدہ لا زم ہوگا۔ (۳) عن مجاهد قال اذا قرأت السجدة اجزاك ان تسجد بها مرة ، (۴) عن ابراهيم في الرجل يقرأ السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها قالا تجزيها السجدة الاولى. (مصنف بن ابى شيبة ۲۰۴ ، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة ثم يعيد قر آ تھا کیف یصنع ج اول ص ۱۳۶۵، نمبر ۴۱۹۹/۴۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کئی مرتبہ آیت سجدہ پڑھنے سے اگر مجلس ایک ہو تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے۔
لغت : مدیا سدی سے مشتق ہے، تا نا بنا۔ غصن : ڈالی ۔عوم: تیرنا۔ ترجمه : (۷۶۸) اور گھر اور مسجد کے مختلف کونوں میں جانے سے مجلس نہیں بدلتی چاہے بڑا ہو۔ اور نہ کشتی کے چلنے سے ، اور نہ ایک دو رکعت پڑھنے سے ، اور نہ پینے سے ، اور نہ ایک دو لقمے کھانے سے، اور ایک دو قدم چلنے سے ، اور نہ ٹیک لگانے سے، اور نہ بیٹھنے سے، اور کھڑے ہونے سے، اور سوار ہونے سے، اور تلاوت کی جگہ اترنے سے، اور نہ نماز پڑھتے ہوئے چوپائے کے چلنے سے تشریح : یہاں ۱۲ صورتیں بیان کر رہے ہیں جن سے مجلس نہیں بدلتی ۔ [1] اورگھر اور مسجد کے مختلف کونوں میں جانے سے مجلس نہیں بدلتی چاہے مسجد اور گھر بڑا ہو ، کیونکہ پورا گھر ایک ہی جگہ شمار کی جاتی ہے۔ [۲] کشتی چل رہی ہے جسکی وجہ سے سمندر کا مقام بدلتا جارہا ہے، لیکن جو آدمی کشتی میں بیٹھا آیت پڑھ رہا ہے اس کی مجلس نہیں بدلے گی، کیونکہ وہ ایک ہی جگہ بیٹھا ہوا ہے۔[۳] اور نہ ایک دو رکعت پڑھنے سے، [۴] اور نہ پینے سے، [۵] اور نہ ایک دو لقمے کھانے سے ، [۶] اور ایک دو قدم چلنے سے، [۷] اور نہ ٹیک لگانے سے ، [۸] اور نہ بیٹھنے سے ، [9] اور کھڑے ہونے سے ، [۱۰] اور سوار ہونے سے ، [۱۱] اور تلاوت کی جگہ اترنے سے ، جہاں تلاوت ختم ہوئی وہیں سواری سے اتر گیا تو اس سے مجلس نہیں بدلے گی [۱۲] اور نہ نماز پڑھتے ہوئے چوپائے کے چلنے سے۔ سواری چل رہی تھی اور آدمی اس پر نماز پڑھ رہا تھا اور آیت بھی تلاوت کر رہا تھا تو چاہے سواری کا مقام بدلتا جارہا ہے، لیکن آدمی ایک
Chapter of Prostration of Recitation. If he repeats it, he prostrates another [prostration], and if he did not prostrate the first time, one prostration suffices him in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), like one who repeats it in one session, not two sessions. (767) And the session changes by moving from it, whether by climbing to another branch, and by moving from one branch to another. ... Explanation: Here there are three issues. [1] He recited a verse of prostration outside prayer and prostrated there, then he intended prayer and recited the same verse in prayer, so he should prostrate again in prayer because the first prostration is lower and the prayer's prostration is higher, so the higher is not fulfilled by the lower. Another reason: if he recites multiple times and prostrates afterward, it suffices for all; here he prostrated first then recited, so the first prostration does not suffice for the later [recitation]. [2] Second issue: He recited a verse outside prayer and did not prostrate, then he intended prayer in that same place and recited the verse again, then the prayer's prostration will suffice for the outside [recitation] because the outside is lower and the prayer's is higher, so the lower is fulfilled by the higher. [3] Third issue: If he recites one verse multiple times in one session, one prostration becomes obligatory because due to the unity of the session, merging (tadakhul) occurs. Proof: (1) The prayer's prostration is higher, so it suffices for the lower; and since the session is one, the one prostration of prayer suffices. (2) For one prostration being sufficient, there is this saying of a Tabi'i: From Mujahid, he said: When you recite the prostration verse, it suffices you to prostrate once for it. From Ibrahim regarding a man who recites a prostration verse and then repeats its recitation, they both said: The first prostration suffices for it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 204, Bab al-Rajul yaqra' al-sajdah thumma yu'id qira'ataha kayfa yasna', Vol. 1, p. 365, nos. 4199/4200). From this athar it is known that if one recites the verse of prostration multiple times and the session is one, one prostration suffices. Principle: If the session changes repeatedly, prostration becomes obligatory repeatedly. And if he recites the verse of prostration several times in one session, one prostration becomes obligatory. Translation: (767) And the session changes by moving from that place, whether by climbing to another branch, and by moving from one branch to another, and by swimming in a river or a large basin, in some narrations. Explanation: When one moves from one place to another, the session changes; and as many times as the session changes and he recites the same verse, that many times prostration becomes obligatory. It presents several forms of session change: [1] When climbing from one branch to another, the session changes. [2] When moving from one branch to another of the same tree, the session changes. [3] When swimming in a river or large basin from one corner to another, the session changes. Proof: (1) By analogy (qiyas), for every recitation a separate prostration should be obligatory. But to avoid hardship, merging (tadakhul) is allowed. However, the condition is that the session is one. Another point: the lower is included in the higher, but the higher is not included in the lower. Now in the above case, if he recited one verse multiple times and the session is one, then due to merging one prostration becomes obligatory. And if the session changes, multiple prostrations become obligatory. (2) There is this saying of a Tabi'i: From Abu Abd al-Rahman, that he used to recite the prostration verse and prostrate, then repeat it in that same session many times and would not prostrate. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 204, Bab al-Rajul yaqra' al-sajdah thumma yu'id qira'ataha kayfa yasna', Vol. 1, p. 1366, no. 4201). From this athar it is known that if one recites the verse of prostration multiple times in one session, merging occurs and one prostration becomes obligatory. (3) From Mujahid, he said: When you recite the prostration verse, it suffices you to prostrate once for it. (4) From Ibrahim regarding a man who recites a prostration verse and then repeats its recitation, they both said: The first prostration suffices for it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 204, Bab al-Rajul yaqra' al-sajdah thumma yu'id qira'ataha kayfa yasna', Vol. 1, p. 1365, nos. 4199/4200). From this athar it is known that if one recites the verse of prostration multiple times and the session is one, one prostration suffices. Lexicon: Misdad is derived from sadda, to climb. Ghush: branch. 'Awm: swimming. Translation: (768) And the session does not change by moving to different corners of the house and mosque, even if large; nor by the sailing of a ship; nor by praying one or two rak'ahs; nor by drinking; nor by eating one or two morsels; nor by walking a few steps; nor by leaning; nor by sitting; nor by standing; nor by riding; nor by dismounting at the place of recitation; nor by the walking of an animal while praying. Explanation: Here it mentions twelve things that do not change the session: [1] Moving to different corners of the house and mosque does not change the session, even if the mosque or house is large, because the entire house is considered one place. [2] A ship is moving, so the sea location changes, but the person sitting in the ship reciting the verse, his session does not change because he is sitting in one place. [3] Praying one or two rak'ahs does not change the session. [4] Drinking does not. [5] Eating one or two morsels does not. [6] Walking a few steps does not. [7] Leaning does not. [8] Sitting does not. [9] Standing does not. [10] Riding does not. [11] Dismounting at the place of recitation, i.e., where the recitation ended, he dismounted from the animal, this does not change the session. [12] The walking of the animal while praying does not change the session. The animal was moving and the man was praying on it and reciting the verse; even though the animal's location changes, the man is [in the same position].
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah discusses the rulings of Sujūd al-Tilāwah (prostration of recitation) when a verse of prostration is repeated. The passage is a sharh (expansion) on the matn, providing detailed rulings and proofs from the Athar of the Tabi'un. The author first presents three scenarios: (1) If someone recites a prostration verse outside prayer, prostrates, then prays and recites the same verse in prayer, a second prostration is required in prayer because the prayer's prostration is higher and cannot be fulfilled by a lower one. (2) If someone recites outside without prostrating, then prays and recites again, the prayer's single prostration suffices for both due to the principle that the higher fulfills the lower. (3) If the verse is repeated multiple times in one session (majlis), one prostration suffices due to tadakhul (merging). The key principle is that the session determines whether multiple prostrations are needed. The author then defines what constitutes a change of session: moving from one place to another, such as climbing from branch to branch or swimming across a river. On the other hand, minor movements within the same location—like moving to different corners of a house or mosque, or actions like praying, eating, drinking, walking a few steps—do not change the session. The proofs provided are athar from Mujahid, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, and Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami, all indicating that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one session. The Hanafi position is based on the principle of tadakhul to avoid hardship (haraj), and it is the relied-upon ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): Merging of obligations; here, multiple recitations of the same prostration verse in one majlis result in only one prostration being required.
مجلس (majlis): The physical location or session in which a person is present; a change of majlis occurs by moving to a different place, not by minor actions within the same location.
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran. It is wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone recites a verse of prostration in the morning in the mosque, then later in the same mosque but in a different corner recites the same verse again without prostrating, and then recites it a third time in yet another corner, how many prostrations are required according to this passage?
A) Three prostrations, one for each recitation
B) Two prostrations, because the corners change the session
C) One prostration, because the entire mosque is one session
D) None, because he did not prostrate after the first recitation

Key Takeaway
One prostration of recitation suffices for multiple recitations of the same verse in one session due to the principle of tadakhul.

Sujūd al-Tilāwah: Change of Session (Majlis)
Definition of majlis change and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify actions that change the majlis and those that do not, and apply the corresponding ruling on sujud al-tilawah.

Core Idea
The majlis changes by moving to a different place; minor movements within the same place do not break the session.

The principle of tadakhul applies only when recitations occur in a single session. But what constitutes a change of session? This lesson provides a detailed definition from the Hanafi school, listing actions that change the majlis (like climbing to another branch or swimming across a river) and those that do not (like moving to different corners of a mosque or eating a morsel). Understanding this is essential for correctly applying the rule on multiple prostrations.

Guided Path
1
Recall the principle of tadakhul and session
Remember that one prostration suffices only if the recitations are in one session. If the session changes, separate prostrations are required.
This lesson defines 'change of session'.
2
Identify actions that change the session
From the passage, list the actions that change the majlis: moving from one place to another, climbing from branch to branch, swimming across a river or large basin.
These involve a clear physical relocation.
3
Identify actions that do NOT change the session
List the twelve actions mentioned: moving to different corners of a house/mosque, sailing on a ship, praying one or two rak'ahs, drinking, eating a morsel, walking a few steps, leaning, sitting, standing, riding, dismounting, and an animal walking while you pray.
These are considered minor movements within the same location.
4
Apply the definition to new scenarios
Given a situation, determine whether the session has changed. If yes, a new prostration is required for recitations in the new session.
The key is whether the person has physically relocated to a different place.

باب سجود التلاوة
اعاد فيها سجد اخرى وان لم يسجد اولا كفته واحدة فى ظاهر الرواية كمن كرّرها في مجلس واحد لا مجلسين. (٦٧) ويتبدّل المجلس بالانتقال منه ولا مسدّيا وبالانتقال من غصن الى غصن
كرے اور اگر پہلے سجدہ نہ کیا ہو تو اس کو ظاہر روایت میں ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے، جیسے اگر کوئی ایک ہی مجلس میں دو مجلس میں نہیں ، ایک آیت کو مکرر پڑھے تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے۔
تشریح : یہاں تین مسئلے ہیں ۔ [1] نماز سے باہر آیت سجدہ پڑھی اور وہیں سجدہ بھی کر لیا، پھر نماز کی نیت باندھی اور اس میں بھی وہی آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو نماز میں دوبارہ سجدہ کرے، کیونکہ پہلا سجدہ ادنی ہے اور نماز کا سجدہ اعلی ہے اس لئے ادنی سے اعلی ادا نہیں ہوگا ، دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ کئی مرتبہ آیت پڑھی اور بعد میں سجدہ کرے تو سب کے لئے کافی ہے، یہاں پہلے سجدہ کر لیا اس کے بعد آیت پڑھی اس لئے پہلا سجدہ بعد کے لئے کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ [۲] دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ نماز سے باہر آیت پڑھی اور اس کا سجدہ نہیں کیا اور پھر اسی جگہ نماز کی نیت باندھی اور اس میں دوبارہ آیت پڑھی تو نماز کا سجدہ باہر کے لئے کافی ہوگا، کیونکہ باہر کا ادنی ہے اور نماز کا اعلی ہے اس لئے اعلی سے ادنی ادا ہو جائے گا۔[۳] تیسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مجلس میں ایک آیت کو کئی مرتبہ پڑھے تو ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا ، کیونکہ اتحاد مجلس کی وجہ سے تداخل ہو جائے گا۔
وجه : (۱) نماز کا سجدہ اعلی ہے اس لئے ادنی کے لئے کافی ہے۔ اور چونکہ مجلس ایک ہے اسلئے نماز والا ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہو گا (۲) ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہونے کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے۔ عن مجاهد قال اذا قرأت السجدة اجزاك ان تسجد بها مرة ، عن ابراهيم في الرجل يقرأ السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها قالا تجزيها السجدة الاولی . (مصنف بن ابی شیبۃ ۲۰۴ ، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها كيف يصنع ج اول ص ۳۶۵، نمبر ۴۱۹۹/۴۲۰۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کئی مرتبہ آیت سجدہ پڑھنے سے اگر مجلس ایک ہو تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے۔ اصول : مجلس بدلتی جائے گی تو سجدہ لازم ہوتا جائے گا۔ اور ایک ہی مجلس میں چند بار آیت سجدہ پڑھی تو ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔ ترجمه : (۷۶۷) اور مجلس بدل جاتی ہے اس جگہ سے منتقل ہونے سے، چاہے وہ تا نا بنتے ہوئے دوسری ڈالی پر جائے، اور منتقل ہونے سے ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف ، اور نہر ، یا بڑے حوض میں تیرنے سے ہیچ تر روایت میں ۔ تشریح : ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ کی طرف منتقل ہو جائے اس سے مجلس بدل جاتی ہے، اور جتنی مرتبہ مجلس بدلتی جائے اور اس میں ایک ہی آیت کو پڑھتا جائے اتنی مرتبہ سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔ آگے مجلس بدلنے کی چند صورتیں پیش کر رہے ہیں ۔ [1] تانا بنتے ہوئے ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف جائے تب بھی مجلس بدل جائے گی۔ [۲] ایک ہی درخت کی مختلف ڈالیوں پر ایک ڈالی سے دوسری ڈالی کی طرف جائے تو مجلس بدل جائے گی [۳] نہر یا بڑے حوض میں تیرے اور ایک کونے سے دوسرے کونے کی طرف

 جائے تو مجلس بدل جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) قیاس کے اعتبار سے ہر آیت پڑھنے کے لئے الگ الگ سجدہ واجب ہونا چاہئے۔ لیکن حرج کے لئے تداخل کر دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اس میں شرط یہ ہے کہ مجلس ایک ہو۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ ادنی اعلی میں داخل ہوگا لیکن اعلی ادنی میں داخل نہیں ہوگا۔ اب اوپر کی صورت میں ایک ہی آیت کئی مرتبہ پڑھی ہے تو اگر مجلس ایک ہے تو تداخل ہو کر ایک ہی سجدہ لازم ہوگا۔ اور مجلس بدل گئی تو کئی سجدے لازم ہونگے ۔ (۲) اس قول تابعی میں ہے۔ عن ابی عبد الرحمن انه كان يقرأ السجدة فيسجد ثم يعيدها في مجلسه ذلك مرارا لا يسجد - (مصنف ابن ابی شیت ۲۰۴، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها كيف يصنع ، ج اول ص ۱۳۶۶ نمبر ۴۲۰ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مجلس میں کئی مرتبہ آیت سجدہ پڑھا تو تداخل ہوگا اور ایک ہی سجدہ لا زم ہوگا۔ (۳) عن مجاهد قال اذا قرأت السجدة اجزاك ان تسجد بها مرة ، (۴) عن ابراهيم في الرجل يقرأ السجدة ثم يعيد قرأتها قالا تجزيها السجدة الاولى. (مصنف بن ابى شيبة ۲۰۴ ، باب الرجل يقرا السجدة ثم يعيد قر آ تھا کیف یصنع ج اول ص ۱۳۶۵، نمبر ۴۱۹۹/۴۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کئی مرتبہ آیت سجدہ پڑھنے سے اگر مجلس ایک ہو تو ایک ہی سجدہ کافی ہے۔
لغت : مدیا سدی سے مشتق ہے، تا نا بنا۔ غصن : ڈالی ۔عوم: تیرنا۔ ترجمه : (۷۶۸) اور گھر اور مسجد کے مختلف کونوں میں جانے سے مجلس نہیں بدلتی چاہے بڑا ہو۔ اور نہ کشتی کے چلنے سے ، اور نہ ایک دو رکعت پڑھنے سے ، اور نہ پینے سے ، اور نہ ایک دو لقمے کھانے سے، اور ایک دو قدم چلنے سے ، اور نہ ٹیک لگانے سے، اور نہ بیٹھنے سے، اور کھڑے ہونے سے، اور سوار ہونے سے، اور تلاوت کی جگہ اترنے سے، اور نہ نماز پڑھتے ہوئے چوپائے کے چلنے سے تشریح : یہاں ۱۲ صورتیں بیان کر رہے ہیں جن سے مجلس نہیں بدلتی ۔ [1] اورگھر اور مسجد کے مختلف کونوں میں جانے سے مجلس نہیں بدلتی چاہے مسجد اور گھر بڑا ہو ، کیونکہ پورا گھر ایک ہی جگہ شمار کی جاتی ہے۔ [۲] کشتی چل رہی ہے جسکی وجہ سے سمندر کا مقام بدلتا جارہا ہے، لیکن جو آدمی کشتی میں بیٹھا آیت پڑھ رہا ہے اس کی مجلس نہیں بدلے گی، کیونکہ وہ ایک ہی جگہ بیٹھا ہوا ہے۔[۳] اور نہ ایک دو رکعت پڑھنے سے، [۴] اور نہ پینے سے، [۵] اور نہ ایک دو لقمے کھانے سے ، [۶] اور ایک دو قدم چلنے سے، [۷] اور نہ ٹیک لگانے سے ، [۸] اور نہ بیٹھنے سے ، [9] اور کھڑے ہونے سے ، [۱۰] اور سوار ہونے سے ، [۱۱] اور تلاوت کی جگہ اترنے سے ، جہاں تلاوت ختم ہوئی وہیں سواری سے اتر گیا تو اس سے مجلس نہیں بدلے گی [۱۲] اور نہ نماز پڑھتے ہوئے چوپائے کے چلنے سے۔ سواری چل رہی تھی اور آدمی اس پر نماز پڑھ رہا تھا اور آیت بھی تلاوت کر رہا تھا تو چاہے سواری کا مقام بدلتا جارہا ہے، لیکن آدمی ایک
Chapter of Prostration of Recitation. If he repeats it, he prostrates another [prostration], and if he did not prostrate the first time, one prostration suffices him in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), like one who repeats it in one session, not two sessions. (767) And the session changes by moving from it, whether by climbing to another branch, and by moving from one branch to another. ... Explanation: Here there are three issues. [1] He recited a verse of prostration outside prayer and prostrated there, then he intended prayer and recited the same verse in prayer, so he should prostrate again in prayer because the first prostration is lower and the prayer's prostration is higher, so the higher is not fulfilled by the lower. Another reason: if he recites multiple times and prostrates afterward, it suffices for all; here he prostrated first then recited, so the first prostration does not suffice for the later [recitation]. [2] Second issue: He recited a verse outside prayer and did not prostrate, then he intended prayer in that same place and recited the verse again, then the prayer's prostration will suffice for the outside [recitation] because the outside is lower and the prayer's is higher, so the lower is fulfilled by the higher. [3] Third issue: If he recites one verse multiple times in one session, one prostration becomes obligatory because due to the unity of the session, merging (tadakhul) occurs. Proof: (1) The prayer's prostration is higher, so it suffices for the lower; and since the session is one, the one prostration of prayer suffices. (2) For one prostration being sufficient, there is this saying of a Tabi'i: From Mujahid, he said: When you recite the prostration verse, it suffices you to prostrate once for it. From Ibrahim regarding a man who recites a prostration verse and then repeats its recitation, they both said: The first prostration suffices for it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 204, Bab al-Rajul yaqra' al-sajdah thumma yu'id qira'ataha kayfa yasna', Vol. 1, p. 365, nos. 4199/4200). From this athar it is known that if one recites the verse of prostration multiple times and the session is one, one prostration suffices. Principle: If the session changes repeatedly, prostration becomes obligatory repeatedly. And if he recites the verse of prostration several times in one session, one prostration becomes obligatory. Translation: (767) And the session changes by moving from that place, whether by climbing to another branch, and by moving from one branch to another, and by swimming in a river or a large basin, in some narrations. Explanation: When one moves from one place to another, the session changes; and as many times as the session changes and he recites the same verse, that many times prostration becomes obligatory. It presents several forms of session change: [1] When climbing from one branch to another, the session changes. [2] When moving from one branch to another of the same tree, the session changes. [3] When swimming in a river or large basin from one corner to another, the session changes. Proof: (1) By analogy (qiyas), for every recitation a separate prostration should be obligatory. But to avoid hardship, merging (tadakhul) is allowed. However, the condition is that the session is one. Another point: the lower is included in the higher, but the higher is not included in the lower. Now in the above case, if he recited one verse multiple times and the session is one, then due to merging one prostration becomes obligatory. And if the session changes, multiple prostrations become obligatory. (2) There is this saying of a Tabi'i: From Abu Abd al-Rahman, that he used to recite the prostration verse and prostrate, then repeat it in that same session many times and would not prostrate. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 204, Bab al-Rajul yaqra' al-sajdah thumma yu'id qira'ataha kayfa yasna', Vol. 1, p. 1366, no. 4201). From this athar it is known that if one recites the verse of prostration multiple times in one session, merging occurs and one prostration becomes obligatory. (3) From Mujahid, he said: When you recite the prostration verse, it suffices you to prostrate once for it. (4) From Ibrahim regarding a man who recites a prostration verse and then repeats its recitation, they both said: The first prostration suffices for it. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 204, Bab al-Rajul yaqra' al-sajdah thumma yu'id qira'ataha kayfa yasna', Vol. 1, p. 1365, nos. 4199/4200). From this athar it is known that if one recites the verse of prostration multiple times and the session is one, one prostration suffices. Lexicon: Misdad is derived from sadda, to climb. Ghush: branch. 'Awm: swimming. Translation: (768) And the session does not change by moving to different corners of the house and mosque, even if large; nor by the sailing of a ship; nor by praying one or two rak'ahs; nor by drinking; nor by eating one or two morsels; nor by walking a few steps; nor by leaning; nor by sitting; nor by standing; nor by riding; nor by dismounting at the place of recitation; nor by the walking of an animal while praying. Explanation: Here it mentions twelve things that do not change the session: [1] Moving to different corners of the house and mosque does not change the session, even if the mosque or house is large, because the entire house is considered one place. [2] A ship is moving, so the sea location changes, but the person sitting in the ship reciting the verse, his session does not change because he is sitting in one place. [3] Praying one or two rak'ahs does not change the session. [4] Drinking does not. [5] Eating one or two morsels does not. [6] Walking a few steps does not. [7] Leaning does not. [8] Sitting does not. [9] Standing does not. [10] Riding does not. [11] Dismounting at the place of recitation, i.e., where the recitation ended, he dismounted from the animal, this does not change the session. [12] The walking of the animal while praying does not change the session. The animal was moving and the man was praying on it and reciting the verse; even though the animal's location changes, the man is [in the same position].
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah discusses the rulings of Sujūd al-Tilāwah (prostration of recitation) when a verse of prostration is repeated. The passage is a sharh (expansion) on the matn, providing detailed rulings and proofs from the Athar of the Tabi'un. The author first presents three scenarios: (1) If someone recites a prostration verse outside prayer, prostrates, then prays and recites the same verse in prayer, a second prostration is required in prayer because the prayer's prostration is higher and cannot be fulfilled by a lower one. (2) If someone recites outside without prostrating, then prays and recites again, the prayer's single prostration suffices for both due to the principle that the higher fulfills the lower. (3) If the verse is repeated multiple times in one session (majlis), one prostration suffices due to tadakhul (merging). The key principle is that the session determines whether multiple prostrations are needed. The author then defines what constitutes a change of session: moving from one place to another, such as climbing from branch to branch or swimming across a river. On the other hand, minor movements within the same location—like moving to different corners of a house or mosque, or actions like praying, eating, drinking, walking a few steps—do not change the session. The proofs provided are athar from Mujahid, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, and Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami, all indicating that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations in one session. The Hanafi position is based on the principle of tadakhul to avoid hardship (haraj), and it is the relied-upon ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
مجلس (majlis): The physical location or session in which a person is present; a change of majlis occurs by moving to a different place, not by minor actions within the same location.
تداخل (tadakhul): Merging of obligations; here, multiple recitations of the same prostration verse in one majlis result in only one prostration being required.
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran. It is wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following changes the session (majlis)?
A) Moving to a different corner of the same mosque
B) Walking a few steps within the same room
C) Swimming from one bank of a river to the opposite bank
D) Eating a morsel of food

Key Takeaway
The session (majlis) changes only when a person physically relocates to a different place; minor actions within the same location do not affect it.

Salah — Prayer
